# run-kit UI Patterns

## URL Structure

| Route | View | Component Pattern |
|-------|------|-------------------|
| `/` | Host-page host-console home | Standalone page (`HostOverviewPage`) ‚Äî `flex-col h-full` (was `h-screen`; since `260707-4vq2-lift-topbar-root-layout` the root layout owns viewport height and the shared TopBar mounts once at the persistent root layout above the outlet, NOT pinned by this page ‚Äî `HostOverviewPage` no longer renders `<TopBar>`, it registers `isConnected: hostMetricsConnected` into the slot context; see ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí persistent root mount). Zones in order: HOST HEALTH ‚Üí BOARDS ‚Üí TMUX SERVERS ‚Üí SERVICES (each a `[ LABEL‚ñä ]‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ` `SectionHeading` ‚Äî the `[ cockpit ]` `PageHeading` row was REMOVED by `260704-pr0p-navbar-page-heading-boot-sweep`; the Host page's page identity is now the solo `Host` heading in the top-bar center cell, plus the in-page `Host Overview` SectionHeading at the top of the scroll container since `260715-zs1y` ‚Äî see ¬ß Page Overview Headings). No sidebar and no Shell grid. Since `260701-vshd-cockpit-host-console-home` `/` DOES carry live host data ‚Äî the server-independent host-metrics subscription opens here (a `metrics` subscription on the shared state socket since `260716-qf3j-state-socket`, was a dedicated `?metrics=1` SSE stream; no per-server subscription is attached, which is why the Host-page TopBar drives its connection dot from `hostMetricsConnected` rather than a per-server slice). The tile grid + count/loading line render from SessionContext's `servers`/`serversLoaded` (since `260701-f4e5-serverlist-create-waiting-state` dropped the page's own `listServers()` state) so the "+" create path shares the pending-marker ‚Üí `ServerWaiting` ‚Üí auto-swap lifecycle (¬ß Create-server lifecycle). See ¬ß HOST HEALTH Zone, ¬ß BOARDS Zone, ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar). |
| `/$server` | Session-tiles density view | `AppShell` layout with `SessionTiles` content (was `Dashboard` ‚Äî deleted by `260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`). SSE connected to the specified server. See ¬ß Session Tiles. |
| `/$server/$window` | Terminal / Iframe / Chat | `AppShell` layout. The second segment is the **numeric part** of the stable tmux **window ID** (`@N` sans `@`, e.g. `/testServer/0`) ‚Äî the window ID (`@N`) remains the identity everywhere in code/params/API, restored from the segment by the route's idempotent parse (since `260703-8mpy-numeric-window-url`). **`$session` was dropped from the route by `260529-jad6-window-api-stability`** (`@N` is server-global, so the session is redundant); the session name shown in chrome is derived from the active window's SSE snapshot, not a URL segment. The address bar carries `/{server}/{N}` ‚Äî since `260703-8mpy` the `@` is dropped for display, NOT percent-encoded (before that change the router percent-encoded `@` in the path segment, so `@2` rendered as `%402`). Old bookmarked `/{server}/%40N` deep links still resolve: the decoded segment `@N` passes through the idempotent parse unchanged (never `@@N`). Rendering branch: since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` the renderer is selected by the **resolved view** ‚Äî `chat` renders `ChatView` (`260714-r7rq`), `web` renders `IframeWindow` (URL bar + iframe), otherwise `TerminalClient` + `BottomBar` (was `rkType === "iframe"` identity; see ¬ß Window Views (Lens Model)). The route also carries a validated `?view=web|chat` search param (per-viewer lens state). SSE connected. Old 3-segment `/$server/$session/$window` URLs are a hard break (no redirect shim). |
| `/board/$name` | Pane board (cross-server) | `BoardPage` shares the `<Shell>` grid wrapper with AppShell ‚Äî sidebar / `<TopBar mode="board">` / pane-row content / shared `<BottomBar>`. Retains its own `<CommandPalette>` mount for board-route-only entries. Peer to `/$server`, NOT under it ‚Äî boards aggregate windows across multiple tmux servers. Invalid `name` (fails `^[A-Za-z0-9_-]{1,32}$`) renders `NotFoundPage`. See ¬ß Boards View. |

Two-tier URL model (`/$server/$window`) with server always in path (since `260529-jad6` dropped the `$session` middle segment). URLs are fully shareable ‚Äî copying a URL and opening it elsewhere on the same host opens the same server and window (the session is re-derived from the snapshot). TanStack Router uses nested routes: `/$server` is a layout route (`serverLayoutRoute`) whose component (`ServerShell`) wraps `SessionProvider` + `AppShell`; the terminal child route is `path: "/$window"` and, since `260703-8mpy-numeric-window-url`, uses the paired `params: { parse, stringify }` API (replacing the former `parseParams` pass-through) to serialize the single `window` param (no `session`) as its numeric part in the URL. The two directions are the exported pure helpers `windowIdToUrlSegment` (stringify ‚Äî strips the leading `@`) and `urlSegmentToWindowId` (parse ‚Äî idempotently prepends `@`) in `router.tsx`; parse restores the `@N` form so every `params.window` consumer keeps receiving `@N`. Child routes (server index and terminal) are matched by the router but rendered conditionally by `AppShell` based on whether the `window` param exists.

**Canonical page names** ‚Äî the spoken/documentation vocabulary for referring to each route (established by `260702-nuup-route-page-names`; renamed Cockpit ‚Üí **Host** and Server Cabin ‚Üí **tmux Server** in `260715-zs1y`, dropping the aviation metaphor in favour of the concrete nouns the internals already used). Use these names in conversation, PRs, and docs instead of the raw path patterns. A mirror of this glossary is a comment beside the `routeTree` definition in `app/frontend/src/router.tsx`.

| Route path | Canonical name | Component |
|------------|----------------|-----------|
| `/` | **Host** | `HostOverviewPage` (global home / server list; also the host-console HOST HEALTH zone, PR #290) |
| `/$server` | **tmux Server** | `ServerShell` (a single server's view; the `resolveServerView` route guard runs here) |
| `/$server/$window` | **Terminal** | *(inherited layout ‚Äî no dedicated component)* (a specific window `@N`) |
| `/board/$name` | **Board** | `BoardPage` (lazy) (cross-server pane board) |
| not-found fallback | **Not Found** | `NotFoundPage` (root `notFoundComponent` catch-all ‚Äî not a registered path) |

The `$server` / `$window` / `$name` segments are **route params** (actual server names, window ids, board names), not literal path segments. The pages were named "Cockpit"/"Server Cabin" under the original aviation metaphor; `260715-zs1y` renamed them to **Host** / **tmux Server** ‚Äî promoting the existing internal nouns to the UI (`host-*` metrics, the `/$server` route already meant a tmux server) so the codebase carries one vocabulary rather than two.

**Vocabulary split** (`260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar`, generalized by `260704-pr0p-navbar-page-heading-boot-sweep`) ‚Äî canonical page names are no longer docs-and-conversation ONLY. Since `260704-pr0p` **every** route surfaces a `PageType: name` identity heading in the top-bar CENTER cell (`Window: <window>` ‚Äî static in every lens since `260714-uco1`, `Board: <board>`, `tmux Server: <server>`, solo `Host`) ‚Äî the canonical page type is the two-tone prefix, the instance name is the subject (¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) center cell). The `260702-6m46` in-page `PageHeading` rows (which under the pre-`260715-zs1y` vocabulary read `[ cockpit ]` / `[ server cabin ¬∑ {server} ]`) were REMOVED ‚Äî page identity lives in the chrome, not the page body. The split now reads: **the left breadcrumb ends at the PARENT** (server / session ‚Äî *the trail to here*), **the centered heading is the current-page leaf** naming both the page type and the instance (*what & where you are*), so a name never appears twice in one bar (move-don't-copy ‚Äî ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar), ¬ß Section Heading). The bracket idiom that PageHeading carried transferred to the in-page **section** labels (the tmux Server page's `Sessions`, the four Host-page zones) via the shared `SectionHeading` (¬ß Section Heading). *(Canonical page names Cockpit/Server Cabin ‚Üí Host/tmux Server in `260715-zs1y`; that change also added two new in-page overview headings ‚Äî see ¬ß Page Overview Headings.)*

**Window identity is the tmux window ID (`@N`), not the index** (since `260529-chgz-window-id-routing`), and **`@N` is the *only* window identity carried by the URL** (since `260529-jad6` dropped `$session`) ‚Äî though since `260703-8mpy-numeric-window-url` the URL *segment* carries only `@N`'s numeric part (`@N` sans `@`), restored to `@N` by the route's idempotent parse (see the `/$server/$window` route-table row above). The `$window` route param holds a stable `@N` string; all URL/API/relay/tmux layers address a specific window by this ID, while the window *index* is retained only for positional reorder/move. The owning **session name is derived from the active window's SSE snapshot** (locating `@N` within `sessions[].windows[]`), not read from the URL ‚Äî `app.tsx` computes `currentSession = sessions.find(s => s.windows.some(w => w.windowId === windowParam))` and `sessionName = currentSession?.name`. Old index-based bookmarked URLs (`/$server/$session/3`) AND old session-bearing URLs (`/$server/$session/@N`) are a **hard break** ‚Äî they no longer resolve (no redirect shim; constitution ¬ßII ‚Äî ephemeral URLs, no persistent state). See `architecture.md` ¬ß API Layer and `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß Window addressing identity for the cross-layer contract.

Server not found: if the `$server` segment doesn't match any known tmux server, a "Server not found" page renders with a link to `/`. A 3-segment URL no longer matches the 2-segment terminal route and falls through to the `NotFoundPage` / server-dashboard fallback.

**Three-way route guard (view / waiting / not-found)** ‚Äî the `$server` segment is resolved by a pure exported helper `resolveServerView(server, servers, pendingServer, serversLoaded)` in `app.tsx` returning `"view" | "waiting" | "not-found"` (established by `260602-3i5d-fix-create-server-not-found-race`). The branches: (a) `server` IN `servers` ‚Üí `"view"` (render the server view); (b) NOT in list AND `server === pendingServer` ‚Üí `"waiting"` (render `ServerWaiting`, a sibling of `ServerNotFound`); (c) NOT in list AND `server !== pendingServer` AND `serversLoaded` ‚Üí `"not-found"` (render `ServerNotFound` immediately, so a typo'd URL still fails fast); (d) otherwise (e.g. before the first fetch resolves) ‚Üí `"view"`, falling through to the server view / loading rather than flashing not-found. The guard keys on the explicit `serversLoaded` flag, **NOT** the old `servers.length > 0` proxy ‚Äî that proxy was the root-cause bug: with pre-existing servers it was already truthy while the list was stale, so the guard fired not-found immediately for a just-created server before the post-create refresh landed. The `pendingServer` waiting state applies only to the one server the user just created. `ServerWaiting` reuses `ServerNotFound`'s centered idiom (`flex flex-col items-center justify-center h-full gap-4 bg-bg-primary` ‚Äî `h-full`, was `h-screen` pre-`260707-4vq2-lift-topbar-root-layout`, so these edge pages fit the content region below the persistent TopBar without overflow) + the shared `LogoSpinner`, showing a brief "Creating server‚Ä¶ / Waiting for `<name>`" message.

**Create-server ‚Üí pending-marker ‚Üí waiting-then-view lifecycle** (`260602-3i5d`) ‚Äî `SessionContext` (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) carries the transient state for this: `pendingServer: string \| null`, `markServerPending(name)` (an empty-string argument is the clear sentinel ‚Üí sets `null`), and `serversLoaded: boolean` (set `true` in `fetchServers()`'s `finally`, so it counts as loaded even on an empty list or a caught fetch error ‚Äî a permanently-false flag would hang the not-found branch forever). All three are threaded through the context type, the live provider value, and the `StandaloneSessionContextProvider` test fallback as safe no-ops/defaults. **BOTH server-create entry points drive this identical flow** (since `260701-f4e5-serverlist-create-waiting-state` wired the second one in) ‚Äî the waiting state is entry-point-agnostic, not specific to one path: (1) the in-app **AppShell** "Server: Create" dialog (`handleCreateServer` in `app.tsx`), and (2) the `/` home-page **`HostOverviewPage`** "+ New Server" (`handleCreate` in `host-overview-page.tsx`). Each: calls `markServerPending(trimmed)` then navigates to `/$server`; its create `useOptimisticAction` fires `refreshServers()` from `onAlwaysSettled` (unmount-safe ‚Äî the create dialog unmounts on navigation but the hook-owning component's root-level `SessionContext` stays mounted; the refresh touches only that) and clears the pending marker via `onAlwaysRollback` (`markServerPending("")`) so a failed create never strands the UI on the waiting state. Before `260701-f4e5`, the `/` path was NOT wired in ‚Äî it kept its own local `listServers()` state and never called `markServerPending`, so it flashed "Server not found" while the tmux server was still starting; that fix consolidated `HostOverviewPage`'s displayed list onto SessionContext's `servers`/`serversLoaded` (the same source the guard reads, so page-display and guard-check can no longer diverge ‚Äî the root of that bug class) while keeping its local `ghostServers` optimistic tiles and the Host-page HOST HEALTH zone (¬ß HOST HEALTH Zone). `pendingServer` is auto-cleared by an effect **in SessionContext** (not in `app.tsx`) once the refreshed `servers` list contains it ‚Äî event-driven on the list changing, with **no timer and no polling**. The ~5s bounded-fallback timeout was deliberately OMITTED for v1 (synchronous near-instant backend create makes a timer speculative; a polling loop would violate the no-client-polling anti-pattern) ‚Äî the waiting state simply persists until the refreshed list contains the server. If ever added it MUST be a single `setTimeout`, never a polling loop.

**Server-list fetch lifecycle**: the server list (`servers`, from `listServers()` ‚Üí `GET /api/servers`) is a **one-time fetch on `SessionProvider` mount + explicit `refreshServers()`** ‚Äî it is **NOT** part of the per-server SSE stream (SSE streams per-server *sessions*/order/metrics/board-changed only, never the list of servers). So a newly-created server does not appear until `refreshServers()` is called; the create flow above is what triggers that refresh. The `server-gone` event (below) is the symmetric *removal* trigger ‚Äî it likewise drives a `refreshServers()` re-query rather than carrying the list inline.

Kill/not-found redirects go to `/$server` (server dashboard), not `/` (server list). The user stays in their server context.

### Server-Gone Reap ‚Üí not-found flip (in-band `gone` event + connection-loss fallback)

Since `260603-gs2t-reap-dead-tmux-servers-sse` the backend signals a server whose tmux socket is gone right before reaping it from the poll set ‚Äî see `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß SSE Poll-Set Lifecycle. **Since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` this rides the state socket as an in-band `gone` frame** (`{"op":"gone","kind":"server","key":"<server>","reason":"server-exited"}`, replacing the retired per-server SSE `server-gone` event; the `key` names the server since one socket carries every server). There is **no new HTTP endpoint or component** (Constitution IX) ‚Äî it reuses the one state socket and the existing `not-found` route guard.

`SessionProvider` (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) routes it through the `StateSocket`'s `onGone(key)` callback (was `es.addEventListener("server-gone", ‚Ä¶)`). The handler: drop the server from `ackedServersRef` (its dot goes disconnected) and from `subscribedServersRef`, call `socketRef.current.unsubscribeServer(key)` to **release the StateSocket ref-count** (so the diff effect can re-subscribe cleanly if the server is later restored while still attached ‚Äî the rework-cycle-1 fix; see `architecture.md` ¬ß State Socket ‚Üí `onGone`), delete the server's slice from `slicesByServer`, then call `fetchServers()` (the `useCallback` that `refreshServers` aliases). The now-dead server is already absent from `GET /api/servers` (enumeration is socket-file-based and self-healing), so the refreshed list **shrinks**, and if the user is currently viewing that server `resolveServerView(server, servers, pendingServer, serversLoaded)` flips to `"not-found"` (`serversLoaded` is already `true` post-mount), rendering the existing `ServerNotFound` view. This extends the three-way route guard (¬ß above): the same `not-found` branch that catches a typo'd URL now also catches a reaped server.

**Connection-loss fallback** (belt-and-suspenders): a catastrophic socket death the backend can't signal (no poll tick lands, or the daemon is mid-restart) is covered by the socket-level disconnect debounce ‚Äî the state socket's `onConnectionChange(false)` clears each acked server's `isConnected` after the 3s debounce, and the provider's server-list refresh path (a `fetchServers()` on reconnect / list change) still shrinks the list, so the guard-flip path fires even with no `gone` frame. The two paths are idempotent and **first-to-fire wins**: the `gone` frame is the fast path (sub-second), the connection-loss refresh is the guaranteed-eventual path. If the server is in fact still alive, the refreshed list still contains it and no flip occurs.

### URL as Resumable Bookmark

**tmux is the sole source of truth for "current window" per server.** The URL is a **resumable bookmark** ‚Äî consulted on initial mount (and reload), then treated as derived state that follows tmux. Two contracts:

1. **Mount-time alignment (one-shot)**. On the first SSE payload after a route mounts, `app.tsx` compares the URL's `$window` window ID (`windowParam`, a `@N` string) to `currentSession.windows.find(w => w.isActiveWindow)?.windowId`. If they differ, it fires exactly one `selectWindow(server, urlWindowId)` to align tmux to the URL ‚Äî `selectWindow` takes `(server, windowId)`, no session, since a window ID is a self-contained tmux target (and the backend `/select` handler derives the owning session for group disambiguation; see `architecture.md` ¬ß API Layer). Guarded by `hasAlignedToUrlRef: useRef(false)` keyed on the `${server}|${windowParam}` key (since `260529-jad6` the key is window-id-only ‚Äî `$session` is gone from the URL, so it can no longer be part of the alignment key). Subsequent route changes to the same window never re-fire alignment. This supports reload (URL=active is a no-op) and deep-link (URL‚âÝactive aligns tmux, then yanks any other tabs on the same server per multi-client convergence). Since the compared identifier is the stable `@N`, a reorder/kill that shifts indices never spuriously triggers re-alignment.

2. **URL writeback (continuous)**. A separate effect watches the SSE-derived `activeWindow` and calls `navigate({ replace: true, to: "/$server/$window", params: { server, window: activeWindow.windowId } })` whenever `activeWindow.windowId !== windowParam`. Since `260529-jad6` the writeback writes the **window id only** ‚Äî there is no `session` param to write. No debounce ‚Äî tmux truth wins always. The effect skips when `dialogOpenRef.current === true` to avoid focus-stealing re-renders mid-dialog (this gates the URL writeback only, not the underlying SSE-derived selection). Comparing `windowId` (not `String(index)`) is the side-effect bug fix from `260529-chgz-window-id-routing`: an index shift from reorder no longer produces a phantom writeback navigation to a different window.

**The 3-second `userNavTimestampRef` debounce is gone.** Pre-change, the URL was the source of truth on every render and a 3000ms `elapsed < 3000` guard tried to protect recent user clicks from being clobbered by SSE-derived URL writebacks. With tmux now authoritative, there is no client-owned window selection state worth protecting; the debounce became dead weight and was deleted entirely.

**Sidebar clicks navigate optimistically AND mutate.** `navigateToWindow(windowId)` in `app.tsx` runs a `runSwitch()` body that fires an optimistic `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params: { server, window: windowId }, search: {} })` *and then* calls `selectWindow(server, windowId)` to bring tmux into agreement. Since `260715-m4xy-history-push-window-switch` this navigate **pushes** (the `replace: true` it formerly carried was removed) ‚Äî a user-initiated window switch IS a navigation, so every switch routed through `navigateToWindow` (sidebar click, window-switcher ‚ñæ, command palette, keyboard shortcut, spawn-agent same-server branch) creates a distinct browser-history entry the top-bar ‚óÄ ‚ñ∂ arrows can retrace (see ¬ß Chrome ‚Üí Browser-history arrows). **No dedup on distinct hops** ‚Äî `w1‚Üíw5‚Üíw1` pushes three entries and Back retraces every hop (explicit no-dedup requirement). Since `260715-38kg-window-switch-confirmed-motion` there IS one early-return guard, but it is NOT a history dedup: `navigateToWindow` early-outs when the target is a **redundant no-op** ‚Äî BOTH the URL window AND tmux's active window (`isRedundantSwitch(windowId, windowParamRef.current, activeWindowRef.current?.windowId)` ‚Äî a mobile-drawer dismissal tap, the palette's `"(current)"` entry). Such a click can change nothing (tmux emits no bytes, the event-driven SSE snapshot never re-confirms), so arming the pending-switch machinery would guarantee a spurious spinner mask at 300ms plus a false failure toast at 5s over the very terminal the user is on; the early-out keeps only the ergonomic drawer close. A genuine `w1‚Üíw5‚Üíw1` still pushes duplicates (each hop IS a real switch); only the degenerate self-click is inert. The two tmux/preference-driven navigates that MUST stay `replace: true` are the SSE URL-writeback effect (contract 2 above ‚Äî tmux corrections aren't user intent, pushing would fight the Back button) and `switchView` (¬ß Window-View Lens ‚Äî per-viewer lens toggles must not step through Back); the fix removed `replace` from `runSwitch` ONLY. The optimistic navigate is what makes the terminal render immediately (including the first click from the `SessionTiles` density view and cross-session clicks the SSE writeback alone can't express); `pendingClickRef` suppresses the writeback's bounce-back until the SSE snapshot confirms the switch (typically sub-500ms with the tmuxctl control-mode subscription; see `architecture.md` ¬ß tmux Control-Mode Subscription). **SSE confirm is the PRIMARY, event-driven clear** ‚Äî but since `38kg` a single per-switch `CONFIRMATION_WINDOW_MS` (5s) failure-bounce timer now BACKSTOPS it: on an explicit `selectWindow` POST rejection OR no confirmation within the window, the intent is cleared, the URL/heading bounce to tmux truth, and a failure toast shows (¬ß Window-Switch Slide Transition ‚Üí Confirmation-gated motion). This is distinct from the removed 3s `userNavTimestampRef` debounce (¬ß above): that timer fired to PROTECT recent clicks from SSE writebacks; this one fires ONLY on non-confirmation to un-stick a silent-failure limbo ‚Äî never to prefer the click over an external event. Server-side overrides during a click (another agent or hook calling `tmux select-window` concurrently) still resolve to whichever mutation tmux processed last ‚Äî the confirmation timer does not contest a genuine external switch (SSE confirming ANY active window clears the intent). On mobile, `runSwitch` additionally closes the overlay sidebar after a destination tap. **Timing caveat (since `260703-l4nf-window-switch-slide-transition`):** on an *instant/fallback* switch ‚Äî no View Transitions support, reduced motion, no outgoing window, or an unresolvable direction ‚Äî `runSwitch` still executes synchronously at click time (byte-identical to before). But on an *animated* same-server switch the body runs INSIDE `document.startViewTransition`'s async callback, i.e. **‚â•1 frame after the click** (the browser first captures the outgoing snapshot, then invokes the callback). So "navigate at click time" is now precise only on the instant path; see ¬ß Window-Switch Slide Transition.

**Keyboard switch path via the command palette.** The window-switch path is also surfaced as `Window: Switch to <session> ‚Ä∫ <name>` palette entries ‚Äî the `windowSwitchActions` useMemo in `app.tsx` (renamed from the old `Terminal:`-prefixed `terminalActions` by `260613-o20f-palette-window-switch`), one entry per window across **every** session (built from `flatWindows`, the current server's merged sessions ‚Äî not cross-server). Each entry reuses `navigateToWindow(fw.window.windowId)`, so it inherits the same `selectWindow` + URL-writeback + mobile-close + `pendingClickRef` suppression as a sidebar click ‚Äî no separate `selectWindow` plumbing. The URL-active window (`fw.window.windowId === windowParam`) gets a `" (current)"` suffix, mirroring `Server: Switch to <name> (current)`. The `‚Ä∫` separator is U+203A (single right-pointing angle quote) ‚Äî the chosen precedent for `<session> ‚Ä∫ <name>` palette labels. The block composes last in `paletteActions` (see ¬ß Boards Command Palette).

**Click-intent and URL-match key on `{server, @N}` ‚Äî never the session name** (server-scoping added by `260715-38kg-window-switch-confirmed-motion`, dropping the session field since `260529-jad6`). `pendingClickRef` is a `PendingSwitchTarget = { server: string; windowId: string }` (`src/lib/window-transition.ts`) ‚Äî the `session` field was dropped in `jad6`, and the `server` field was ADDED in `38kg`. Every consumer compares BOTH fields via the pure exported `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, windowId)`: the writeback's `urlMatchesPending` is `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, windowParam)` and `sseConfirmed` is `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, activeWindow.windowId)`; the mount-alignment skip and `bouncePendingSwitch`'s guards use it too.
- **Why NOT the session name** (the `jad6` half, unchanged): before `jad6` the match compared `pending.session === sessionName && pending.windowId === windowParam`, so a session rename (or a cross-session move where `@N` survives but the session name changed) flipped the session comparison false and released the pending-click suppression early, **bouncing the selection**. Dropping the session field made the selection survive session rename and cross-session move.
- **Why the `server` field is now load-bearing** (the `38kg` half): tmux window ids (`@N`) are only unique **per server**, and `AppShell` persists across `$server` route changes WITHOUT remounting. Window-id-alone matching therefore false-positives on a cross-server id collision (serverA `@5` vs serverB `@5`): a stale serverA intent would suppress serverB's tmux alignment, keep stale tracking alive through the writeback, and later let serverA's failure bounce yank the user cross-server with a false toast. Server-scoping the identity closes all four seams; a same-session click on one server is unaffected. See ¬ß Window-Switch Slide Transition ‚Üí Confirmation-gated motion for the full cross-server identity story.

**Sidebar selection follows the URL window ID, falling back to `isActiveWindow`.** `WindowRow.isSelected` derives from `currentSessionName === session.name && (hasUrlWindow ? currentWindowId === win.windowId : (!ghost && win.isActiveWindow))` in `app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/index.tsx`, where `hasUrlWindow = currentWindowId != null` and `currentWindowId` is the URL's `@N` window ID. When the route carries a window ID (the normal terminal-route case), selection is the stable `currentWindowId === win.windowId` comparison. The `isActiveWindow` term (set by the backend `WindowInfo.IsActiveWindow` from tmux's `#{window_active}`) drives selection only when no URL window is present ‚Äî e.g., the dashboard route, or before the first navigation resolves. Because the URL window ID is now written back from `isActiveWindow` (see contract 2 above), the two stay in lockstep with `tmux select-window` (external switches, `rk riff` window creation) without the index‚ÜîID seam that previously required comparing `String(win.index)`. Ghost windows (mid-creation, before the SSE snapshot includes them) still match only via the `!ghost && win.isActiveWindow` fallback path when no URL window applies.

### Multi-Client Convergence

All clients viewing the same server's window route converge on the same window ‚Äî the per-server invariant. When the SSE `event: sessions` payload changes which window is `isActiveWindow` for the currently-viewed session, every browser tab on `?server=<same>` and viewing `/$server/$window` navigates to the new window's `windowId` via `navigate({ replace: true })` (the URL writeback effect above).

Clients viewing `/board/$name` SHALL NOT navigate ‚Äî the board route does not subscribe its URL to `isActiveWindow`. The SSE payload still arrives and `BoardPane` rendering still receives the updated `isActiveWindow` data; the route stays put.

Clients viewing different `?server=` values are independent ‚Äî each server's SSE stream drives its own clients. Cross-server tabs never yank each other.

**Stale-URL tab yanks other tabs on mount**: when a new tab opens at `/$server/@7` while existing tabs are on `/$server/@2` (tmux active is window `@2`), the new tab's mount-time alignment fires `selectWindow(server, "@7")`. The resulting SSE snapshot then yanks every existing tab on that server to window `@7` via the writeback effect. This is intentional ("yanking is OK" per the change intake) ‚Äî the new tab represents user intent to view that window, and existing tabs collectively reflect "what tmux is now doing." A URL whose `@N` no longer exists on the server simply fails to resolve a current window (no nearest-index arithmetic) ‚Äî see ¬ß Kill-redirect.

## Session Tiles

> Renamed from **Dashboard**, and re-scoped, by `260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`. The old `app/frontend/src/components/dashboard.tsx` (+ `dashboard.test.tsx`) were **DELETED**; the new component is `app/frontend/src/components/session-tiles/session-tiles.tsx` (`SessionTiles`). The route did not change ‚Äî `SessionTiles` renders in the same no-`$window` branch the Dashboard used to fill. *(The last cosmetic "Dashboard" label ‚Äî the top-bar breadcrumb leaf for the no-window state ‚Äî was DELETED by `260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar`, which replaced it with the server-name `aria-current` leaf; the literal string "Dashboard" no longer appears anywhere in the chrome. See ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar).)*

`SessionTiles` is the **multi-agent monitoring-DENSITY view** ‚Äî "what is every agent doing right now" at a glance, the differentiator vs single-session tools. It renders in the terminal area when no `$window` param is present: the `windowParam ? <TerminalClient/> : <SessionTiles/>` branch in `app.tsx` (`windowParam` is the `@N` window ID; `sessionName` is derived from the active window's SSE snapshot, not a URL segment). The empty `serverIndexRoute` (`router.tsx`) is still componentless ‚Äî rendering is done conditionally by `AppShell` based on whether `$window` exists, exactly as the Dashboard was (no new route ‚Äî Constitution IV).

**The load-bearing constraint** ‚Äî window previews are **static text**, NOT a live xterm/relay per tile. N live relays for N tiles would re-trigger the documented HTTP/1.1 6-per-origin connection-pool starvation (see the board-route entries in this domain). A tile upgrades to a real live terminal ONLY on click (navigate to `/$server/$window`, where the single relay opens). The preview mechanism is a periodic `tmux capture-pane` snapshot delivered over the existing SSE hub as `event: preview` ‚Äî see `architecture.md` ¬ß Session-Tile Previews (`event: preview` + preview-scope) for the backend.

**Layout** (since `260704-pr0p-navbar-page-heading-boot-sweep`): Outer wrapper `flex-1 min-h-0 flex flex-col`. The former pinned `PageHeading` header row was REMOVED ‚Äî the tmux Server page's page identity is now the `tmux Server: <server>` heading in the top-bar center cell (¬ß Chrome (Top Bar)). What remains is a single scrollable tile area (`flex-1 min-h-0 overflow-y-auto ...`); since `260715-zs1y` its first child is a page-level `<SectionHeading label="tmux Server Overview" />`, and the grid below is preceded by a `<SectionHeading label="Sessions" side={"{N} sessions, {M} windows"} />` ‚Äî the relocated server-view stats ride the `side` slot, right-aligned after the rule (`[ SESSIONS‚ñä ]‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ {N} sessions, {M} windows`; ¬ß Section Heading, ¬ß Page Overview Headings). This replaced the earlier bare `Sessions` `<h2>` + `TypedLabel` subheading (`260702-6m46`/`260703-5ilm`); the `<h2>` + TypedLabel typed-sweep now live INSIDE the brackets. Only the tile area scrolls.

**Session tiles grid**: `grid grid-cols-1 sm:grid-cols-2 lg:grid-cols-3 gap-3`. One tile per session (`bg-bg-card border border-border rounded`; `data-testid="session-tile-{name}"`), plus an always-visible dashed **New Session** tile at the end (calls `onCreateSession` ‚Üí instant session creation, no dialog). A ghost/optimistic session tile gets `opacity-50 animate-pulse`.

**Session tile header**: A `<button>` toggling inline expansion (`aria-expanded`, `aria-label` "Expand/Collapse {name}"). Shows session name, window count, and activity summary (`{N} active, {M} idle`, derived from each window's `activity`). Chevron `‚ñ∂`/`‚ñº`. Multiple sessions may be expanded simultaneously. Expand state is local `useState<Record<string, boolean>>` keyed by session name.

**Window tiles** (inside an expanded session): each is a `<button>` (`rounded border border-border bg-bg-primary hover:border-text-secondary`; `data-testid="window-tile-{session}-{index}"`) that on click calls `onNavigate(win.windowId)` ‚Äî the same `navigateToWindow` path a sidebar click uses (optimistic navigate + `selectWindow`; see ¬ß URL as Resumable Bookmark) ‚Äî routing to the live-terminal route. NO preview relay is ever opened. A ghost window tile is `disabled` + pulsing. Each tile shows:
- A leading unified `<StatusDot win={win} />` (the SAME component as the sidebar row / pane panel / ‚Äî see ¬ß Status Dot) + window name; a fab-stage badge (`bg-accent/10 text-accent`) when `win.fabStage` is set
- The **pane text preview** as a static monospace `<pre>` (`h-24 overflow-hidden whitespace-pre text-[10px] font-mono bg-bg-inset`, `data-testid="window-tile-preview-{windowId}"`) ‚Äî the `capture-pane` snapshot for `win.windowId`, read from the context `previewsByServer.get(server)` map. Empty (`""`) until the first `event: preview` arrives for the expanded set ‚Äî the view degrades gracefully to an empty preview area before the first snapshot. Never an xterm instance.
- Fab change ID + slug when present (`parseFabChange`)

**New Window button**: dashed-border button inside each expanded session (`onCreateWindow(session.name)`).

**Preview subscription lifecycle** (bounded to expansions): `SessionTiles` consumes `previewsByServer` and `setPreviewScope` from `useSessionContext()`. A `useEffect` keyed on the sorted+joined expanded-session-name key POSTs the current expanded set via `setPreviewScope(server, expandedNames)` whenever it changes (expand/collapse) and on server change. It opens NO live relay per tile and does NOT `setInterval`+fetch ‚Äî previews arrive on the single existing per-server SSE stream. On unmount / server change the declared scope lapses naturally (the connection drop clears the server-side per-connection set ‚Äî see `architecture.md`).

**Touch targets**: session tile headers and window tiles use `coarse:min-h-[44px]`.

## PR Status

Live PR status is exposed two ways: a **full one-line detail** (the Pane panel `PR` L3 register) and a **single status dot** (the unified `StatusDot`, see ¬ß Status Dot below). The detail surface is:

1. **Pane panel `PR` (L3) register** (the per-*selected*-window detail view; see ¬ß Pane Panel / `status-panel.tsx`). This is the **only** full-line PR surface. *(`260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid` DELETED the Dashboard, whose window card previously rendered the `PrStatusLine` component; the replacement `SessionTiles` window tile carries only the `StatusDot`. `260706-y1ar` then folded the last full-line PR surface into the L3 register, leaving `PrStatusLine` with zero live sites, and `260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh` **removed the component**. Its module `pr-status-line.tsx` remains ‚Äî it is the single source of the shared PR color vocabulary + the StatusDot's exported model ‚Äî see ¬ß Shared PR vocabulary (`pr-status-line.tsx`).)*

The *dot* (a single colored dot, not the full line) reaches the remaining surfaces: the sidebar window-tree row and the `SessionTiles` window tile. `260610-obky-pr-status-to-pane-panel` removed the full PR line from `WindowRow` to keep the dense tree compact, and that still holds ‚Äî the tree shows a single `StatusDot`, never the multi-part line. Since `260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing` that single dot is the unified `StatusDot` driven by the palette-v3 **two-family ladder** (cool fab blue/green/purple, warm ad-hoc agent yellow/orange, gray floor; core hue = phase, shape = status, additive yellow halo = `waiting`), reused on all its surfaces (sidebar row, SessionTiles window tile, pane-panel header). See ¬ß Status Dot.

### `PR` (L3) register ‚Äî colored segments + open-first (`status-panel.tsx`)

> **Rewritten by `260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing`** ‚Äî `WindowContent` now renders the pyramid's **four orthogonal signal registers** (spec ¬ß Row Minimalism). See ¬ß Pane panel four-register view for the full L0/L1/L2/L3 model; this subsection covers the L3 `PR` register (formerly the standalone `pr` row).

The **`PR` (L3) register** shares the `tmx/cwd/git/fab` icon + value idiom but with an **open-first** interaction (since `260703-41ks-pr-row-open-first-action`) ‚Äî it is the exception to the panel's "click row = copy" default. `getPrSegments(win)` returns `null` unless `win.prNumber` ‚Äî the gate was **ungated from `fabChange` by `260706-y1ar`** (it was `win.fabChange && win.prNumber`): the L3 register shows the PR for ANY pane on a branch with a derived PR (universal derivation, Principle X; dot ownership is a separate family-gated concern ‚Äî see ¬ß Status Dot D1). Otherwise it returns an array of colored `{text, color}` segments ‚Äî `#<n>` (`text-text-primary`), `<state>[ (draft)]` (via `PR_STATE_COLORS`), and, for an `open` PR only, `checks <prChecks>` (`PR_CHECKS_COLORS`) and `review: <prReview‚Üíspaces>` (`PR_REVIEW_COLORS`). `state` can be `open`/`merged`/`closed` ‚Äî the collector queries `states: [OPEN, MERGED, CLOSED]`, so a recently-merged PR shows `merged` (checks/review suppressed for non-`open`), see `architecture.md` ¬ß `internal/prstatus`. The three color maps are imported from `pr-status-line.tsx` (single source shared with the sidebar dot ‚Äî the module remains the shared vocabulary home after `260715-jykd` removed the `PrStatusLine` component), so segment coloring follows GitHub state per-segment (no whole-value red swap) ‚Äî the color story lives in ¬ß PR Status (draft-follows-health) above. The PR icon (`Ôêá`) is the Nerd Font git-pull-request glyph, matching the other rows' accent icons.

**Open-first split** (`260703-41ks`) ‚Äî supersedes the previous "click row = copy, hover `‚Üó` = open" description of this surface. The segment JSX is single-sourced via a shared `segmentSpans` const in `WindowContent` (consumed by both branches below, so the two can't drift), and the row branches on `win.prUrl`:

- **URL present** ‚Üí the row body is a file-private `PrLinkRow` ‚Äî a real `<a href={win.prUrl} target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" title={win.prUrl} aria-label="Open PR #<n> in a new tab">` (NOT a `<button>` + `window.open`, so native middle-click / Ctrl-Cmd+click / right-click ‚Üí "Copy link address" all work; mirrored the now-removed `PrStatusLine`'s anchor ‚Äî the same anchor-not-button PR-link idiom). The anchor is a flex row: a `shrink-0` prefix span + PR icon span, then a `min-w-0 truncate` segment-text child, then an **always-visible** (not hover-gated) `shrink-0` inline `‚Üó` sibling immediately after it ‚Äî so the `‚Üó` hugs the (possibly truncated) text end, is never eaten by truncation, and never floats to the far right of a wide row. The `‚Üó` is the affordance that signals this row **opens** rather than copies; the existing row hover treatment (`hover:bg-bg-inset`, segment `group-hover:text-accent`) is kept as the row-level cue. Because the anchor is a flex container (whitespace-only `{" "}` text nodes between flex items are dropped and a trailing collapsible space trimmed), the inter-column gaps live as NBSPs INSIDE the prefix/icon spans ‚Äî the at-rest prefix is `"pr"`+2√óNBSP (4 monospace advances) matching `CopyableRow`'s `${prefix} ` (3 + gap = 4), and the `copied ‚úì`+NBSP feedback is 9 advances matching `CopyableRow`'s `copied ‚úì ` ‚Äî keeping the icon/content column-aligned with `tmx/cwd/git/fab` and the no-URL branch. **Copy is role-swapped, not dropped**: a sibling hover-revealed copy `<button aria-label="Copy PR URL">` (the `ÔÉÖ` clipboard glyph) sits in an absolutely-positioned right-side container reusing the **sidebar window-row icon-cluster gating** ‚Äî the container is `pointer-events-none` at rest with `group-hover/pr:pointer-events-auto coarse:pointer-events-auto has-[:focus-visible]:pointer-events-auto`, and the button is `opacity-0 group-hover/pr:opacity-100 coarse:opacity-100 focus-visible:opacity-100` (revealed on hover / coarse pointers / keyboard focus; the anchor reserves `pr-6` so the icon doesn't overlap the inline `‚Üó`/text). Its `onClick` does `e.preventDefault(); e.stopPropagation(); handleCopy("pr", win.prUrl)` ‚Äî the button is a SIBLING of the anchor (not enclosed, so `<a>`-in-`<a>`/`<button>`-in-`<a>` nesting is avoided; `preventDefault` is belt-and-suspenders). Its color follows the window-row cluster precedent (`text-text-secondary hover:text-text-primary`), NOT `ICON_CLASS` (whose `text-accent-bright` would fight at equal specificity). The `copied ‚úì` feedback is unchanged ‚Äî the copy still keeps the `copiedRow === "pr"` + `COPY_FEEDBACK_MS` mechanism, and since the row body is no longer a `CopyableRow`, `PrLinkRow` replicates the prefix swap (`pr` ‚Üí `copied ‚úì`) inline. Both the anchor and the copy button are natively keyboard-focusable (Constitution V).
- **URL absent** (`prNumber` set, `prUrl` missing) ‚Üí nothing to open, so the row stays a plain `CopyableRow` (prefix `"pr¬Ý"`) copying the segment text (`prText`) on click ‚Äî the row body IS the copy action, no anchor, no inline `‚Üó`, no hover copy icon (unchanged from before).

`CopyableRow`'s dead `className` prop was removed by this change (zero call sites); its `title` prop remains live (the `cwd` row uses it).

**Draft state-color follows health, not readiness** (`260615-2olv-pr-status-dot-traffic-light`). `getPrSegments(win)` (the colored-segment variant used in the panel) NO LONGER forces a draft PR's state-color to `text-text-secondary` ‚Äî the old `color: win.prIsDraft ? "text-text-secondary" : PR_STATE_COLORS[win.prState]` override is **gone**. A draft's state segment now follows `PR_STATE_COLORS[win.prState]` like any other (open ‚Üí `text-accent-green`/green), under the same "green = HEALTH, not merge-readiness" semantic as the sidebar dot. The doc comment was rewritten from "draft is 'not ready', not a healthy green" to the health framing. Everything else in `getPrSegments` is unchanged ‚Äî checks/review are still suppressed for `!open` (merged/closed) PRs, and `merged` is still `text-purple-400`. **This delivers the ONE color story** (as of `260615-2olv`): the sidebar dot, these status-panel segments, and (while it existed, until `260715-jykd` removed the component) `PrStatusLine`'s shared `isFailish`-driven coloring all agreed (green = health, red = fail, purple = merged). *(Caveat: `260615-0hsz` later re-keyed the sidebar `StatusDot` off the lifecycle `PHASE_HUE`/shape model, not `prDotState`/`PR_DOT_COLOR` ‚Äî see ¬ß Status Dot. The PR phase still renders purple/red-center/green within that model, so the cross-surface story holds in spirit, but the dot no longer shares the literal `PR_DOT_COLOR` tokens with these text segments ‚Äî that map was deleted.)* Note the `PrStatusLine` component (removed by `260715-jykd`) was never itself recolored ‚Äî it kept its binary red (`isFailish`) / `text-text-secondary` line color; convergence was delivered via the shared `isFailish` predicate plus the status-panel draft alignment, not by re-coloring `PrStatusLine`.

### Pane panel four-register view (`status-panel.tsx` `WindowContent`, `260706-y1ar`)

The pane panel's `WindowContent` renders the pyramid's **register view** ‚Äî one line per signal layer, **orthogonal, never collapsed**, so the sidebar `StatusDot` is a pure function of what the panel shows and can be **mentally derived** from it (the user's own framing: "keep them orthogonal, separate, so we can mentally derive the status dot"). The four registers, each rendered as absent when its layer is absent (a plain shell pane shows only `out`). All prefixes are the **fixed-width 3-char vocabulary** `out`/`agt`/`fab` (+ `tmx`/`cwd`/`git` identity rows), each followed by a single-space advance; only `PR` is 2-char + NBSP-padded to the same 4-advance column (`260706-4h26-durable-merged-pr-register-keys` normalized `output`‚Üí`out` and `agent`‚Üí`agt`):

```
out  active ¬∑ <command>   /   <command> ‚Äî idle Xm since last output   (L0: activity + activityTimestamp)
agt  waiting 3m           /   active   /   idle 12m                    (L1: agentState + epoch duration)
fab  <id> <slug> ¬∑ <stage>[ ¬∑ <displayState>]                         (L2: fabChange ¬∑ fabStage ¬∑ fabDisplayState)
PR   #<n> ¬∑ <state>[ ¬∑ checks <c> ¬∑ review: <r>]                      (L3: prNumber/state/checks/review, ungated)
```

- **L0 `out`** (`getOutputLine`) ‚Äî ALWAYS rendered (the floor layer's precondition is "always"). Speaks about bytes, not intent. Its elapsed is **never muted** here ‚Äî the register view is uncontested for space, so the **waiting-pierce rule is automatic** (the duration-mute rule that hides elapsed when output flows applies only to the tip's one-line summary, spec ¬ß Duration-Text Ladder). Icon: `BrailleSnake`.
- **L1 `agt`** (`getAgentLine`) ‚Äî `null` when no `agentState`, else `${agentState} ${agentIdleDuration}` (or bare state when no duration). The rk-computed `agentIdleDuration` is present for `waiting`/`idle`, empty for `active`. Icon: `StarTwinkle`. This is where a waiting duration is always visible regardless of flowing output (the pierce rule).
- **L2 `fab`** (`fabLine`) ‚Äî `<id> <slug> ¬∑ <stage>[ ¬∑ <displayState>]`; the `displayState` segment is appended when present (`fab pane map` may omit it on older binaries). Rendered as a `CopyableRow` (copies the change id). Icon: `ClockSpinner`.
- **L3 `PR`** (`getPrSegments`) ‚Äî see ¬ß `PR` (L3) register above. **Ungated from `fabChange`** ‚Äî shows for ANY pane with a derived `prNumber` (universal derivation, Principle X). The former open-first `PrLinkRow` / `CopyableRow` branch on `win.prUrl` folds in here unchanged.

The identity rows (`tmx`/`cwd`/`git`) are pane metadata, orthogonal to these four signal registers, and render above them. This register view **replaced** the earlier mixed `run`/`agt` lines ‚Äî `getProcessLine` and the standalone `agt` line are gone; the `out` (L0) and `agt` (L1) registers are their register-view successors (the prefixes were `output`/`agent` until `260706-4h26` normalized them to the 3-char `out`/`agt`). The per-second `useNow()` tick still lives in this leaf (`WindowContent`) ‚Äî the bottom panel is a single instance, so its tick is negligible and never touches the memoized sidebar tree (¬ß Render Performance).

### Shared PR vocabulary ‚Äî `pr-status-line.tsx`

> **The `PrStatusLine` component was REMOVED by `260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh`.** It had zero live render sites well before then (the Dashboard deletion `260701-70a0` removed its window-card site; `260706-y1ar`'s four-register view folded the last full-line PR surface into the PANE panel's L3 register ‚Äî see ¬ß `PR` (L3) register), so `260715-jykd` deleted the component, its private-to-it helpers `stateGlyph`/`summarySegments`, and the `refreshPrStatus` import. **The module `pr-status-line.tsx` is NOT deleted** ‚Äî it is the single source of the shared PR **color vocabulary** AND the lifecycle **status-dot model** (below), still imported by 5 modules (`status-dot.tsx`, `status-dot-tip.tsx`, `status-dot-label.ts`, `sidebar/status-panel.tsx`, `status-dot.test.tsx`). Removing the file wholesale would break all of them; only the `PrStatusLine`-specific code was removed. **Rename candidate** (deferred, plan.md ¬ß Deletion Candidates): the module's namesake component is gone, so `pr-status-line.tsx` ‚Üí e.g. `pr-status-model.ts` would be truthful ‚Äî held off to keep the diff surgical (5 consumers would need import updates).

The module survives purely as the colocation home of the shared exports. The removed component historically rendered `PR #<n> <state-glyph> <state>[ (draft)] ¬∑ <checks/review summary>` (open-first anchor when `win.prUrl` present, click-to-refresh via the old single-poller endpoint) on the Dashboard window card and the Pane-panel `pr` row ‚Äî both surfaces predeceased it. The PR text detail now lives solely in the PANE panel's L3 `PR` register (`getPrSegments`, ¬ß `PR` (L3) register).

**Shared exports** (colocated in `pr-status-line.tsx`):

- **PR color vocabulary**: `PR_STATE_COLORS`/`PR_CHECKS_COLORS`/`PR_REVIEW_COLORS` (the per-segment GitHub-state color maps, consumed by the L3 register in `status-panel.tsx`) and `isFailish(win)` (`prChecks === "fail" || prReview === "changes_requested"` ‚Äî the single fail predicate).
- **Status-dot model** (PR-dot vocabulary added by `260615-2olv-pr-status-dot-traffic-light`): `PrDotState` (the `"merged" | "fail" | "pending" | "healthy" | "neutral"` union) and `prDotState(win)` (the first-match-wins precedence function, reusing `isFailish` for its `fail` branch ‚Äî kept as the single source of the fail definition, shared with the Pane panel). The palette-v3 dot model (`260706-y1ar`): `DotShape` (`"ring" | "solid" | "failed" | "done" | "skipped"`), `DotPhase` (`"intake" | "apply" | "pr" | "agent" | "agentPr" | "none"`), `StatusDotState = { phase: DotPhase; shape: DotShape; waiting?: boolean }`, `fabPhase(stage)`, `fabShape(displayState)`, `prShape(win)` (reuses `prDotState`), `hasFreshAgent(win)`, `prOwnsDot(win)`, `PHASE_HUE` (phase‚Üíhue token map), and the two-family `statusDotState(win)` (see ¬ß Status Dot for the ladder + D1/D2).

The `StatusDot` component (`status-dot.tsx`, see ¬ß Status Dot) imports `statusDotState`/`PHASE_HUE`; `status-dot-tip.tsx` and `status-dot-label.ts` import `StatusDotState`/`DotShape`; `dotLabel` lives in its own `status-dot-label.ts` module (`260706-y1ar`, to break the dot‚Üîtip import cycle). **`PR_DOT_COLOR` and `PR_DOT_LABEL` were DELETED by `260615-0hsz`** (zero-call-site once the redesigned dot stopped using them). `prDotState`/`PrDotState`/`isFailish` remain live (the L3 register + `prShape` use them; `prDotState` is reused by `prShape` and the `prDotState precedence` block in `pr-status-line.test.tsx`, which `260715-jykd` preserved after dropping the `PrStatusLine`-render cases).

### Status Dot (`status-dot.tsx`) ‚Äî palette-v3 two-family ladder + waiting halo (`260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing`)

> Spec: `docs/site/status-dot.md` (+ `docs/img/status-dot-matrix.svg`) is the canonical reference for the full matrix and the palette rationale. Design authority: `docs/specs/status-pyramid.md`.

> Tooltip surface: since `260616-37ub-status-dot-tooltip` the dot no longer uses the native HTML `title` ‚Äî it mounts a custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card (floating-ui based). See ¬ß Status Dot hover-card (`status-dot-tip.tsx`) below.

`StatusDot({ win }: { win: WindowInfo })` (`app/frontend/src/components/status-dot.tsx`) is the **one** dot reused on all three surfaces ‚Äî the sidebar window row (leading position, now the row's ONLY status signal ‚Äî see ¬ß Window rows / Row Minimalism), the `SessionTiles` window tile, and the pane-panel header. `260706-y1ar` rewrote the former three-tier `PR > fab > tmux` precedence (`260615-0hsz`) into the palette-v3 **two-family ladder** and made the dot a **first-class consumer of `agentState`** (the deferred UI-surfacing work #314 punted). It uses **TWO orthogonal visual channels PLUS an additive attention overlay**: **core hue = phase** (which journey + position in it), **shape = status** (health, ONE shape vocabulary across fab AND PR), and **`waiting` ‚Üí a ladder-exempt additive yellow halo** (see ¬ß Waiting halo below).

**Ladder ‚Äî two families joined at the top** (`statusDotState(win)` in `pr-status-line.tsx`, palette v3). First precondition wins for the core hue + shape; `waiting = win.agentState === "waiting"` is computed independently and attached as `state.waiting` on every branch:

- **`fabChange` present ‚Üí cool family (fab pipeline):** `prOwnsDot(win)` ‚Üí `{ phase: "pr", shape: prShape(win) }` (purple); else `{ phase: fabPhase(win.fabStage), shape: fabShape(win.fabDisplayState) }` (blue if `intake`, else green).
- **no `fabChange` but a fresh `agentState` ‚Üí warm family (ad-hoc agent):** `prOwnsDot(win)` ‚Üí `{ phase: "agentPr", shape: prShape(win) }` (orange); else `{ phase: "agent", shape: agentState === "idle" ? "ring" : "solid" }` (yellow ‚Äî a `waiting`/`active` agent is mid-turn ‚Üí solid, only a resting `idle` agent is a ring).
- **neither ‚Üí the gray L0 floor:** `{ phase: "none", shape: win.activity === "active" ? "solid" : "ring" }`.

The result type is `StatusDotState = { phase: DotPhase; shape: DotShape; waiting?: boolean }`. `hasFreshAgent(win)` is `agentState ‚àà {active, waiting, idle}` ‚Äî #314 already clears stale/shell-reconciled values server-side (the reconciler + rollup omit a plain-shell pane), so a non-empty rolled-up `agentState` on the window IS fresh; no client-side staleness heuristic (R4).

**D1 ‚Äî per-family PR ownership** (resolved): `prOwnsDot(win)` is `!!win.prNumber && win.prState !== "closed"`. PR ownership is PER-FAMILY ‚Äî **purple requires `fabChange && prNumber`, orange requires `fresh agent && prNumber`**. A **plain floor pane never lets its PR own the dot**: with no fab change and no fresh agent it stays gray even when its branch has a derived PR. The PR still shows everywhere derivation reaches ‚Äî the PANE panel's L3 register and the StatusDotTip "Open PR" link ‚Äî but never as a mystifying floor-pane dot (Principle X: derivation is universal; dot ownership is a separate, family-gated concern). *(The full-line `PrStatusLine` component was a third such surface until `260715-jykd` removed it.)*

**D2 ‚Äî merged/closed PR ownership**: a **CLOSED-unmerged** PR never owns the dot (`prState !== "closed"` in `prOwnsDot`) ‚Äî the pane falls through to its underlying tier (a live-change window shows its green working stage, not a dead PR's skipped ring ‚Äî decision-table row 20). A **merged** PR (served durably by the backend's `--state all` branch derivation ‚Äî no grace clock; see [architecture](/run-kit/architecture.md) ¬ß Branch‚ÜíPR Derivation) still owns the dot as the purple/orange done square. The frontend `prState === "closed"` drop and the backend's stateless/restart-proof merged durability are the two halves of D2 (the earlier `260706-y1ar` backend grace window was replaced by `260706-4h26`'s state-all + precedence model).

**Waiting halo ‚Äî additive attention overlay, ladder-exempt** (R2): when `state.waiting`, `StatusDot` appends the `rk-waiting-halo` class to the dot element ‚Äî a **constant-yellow pulsing box-shadow ring** layered around it (the `rk-waiting-halo` keyframe in `globals.css`). It is **ADDITIVE** ‚Äî the core hue AND shape are untouched (a blue intake dot keeps its blue core; a green failed dot keeps its failed shape; a waiting `done` square keeps sharp corners). NEVER a hue-flip ‚Äî family identity must survive attention. The class rides the dot element itself (box-shadow renders outside the border-box, disturbing neither size nor hue), so the floating-ui `setRef` stays on one element. Under `prefers-reduced-motion` the halo is a **static yellow ring** (no pulse). The glance rule: **cool core = my pipeline, warm core = my ad-hoc agents, gray = just a terminal, yellow HALO = needs me now.**

**Hue = phase** ‚Äî palette v3, TWO families + floor (spec ¬ß The Channel Model). The old amber `execution`/`completion` grouping (`260615-0hsz`) **RETIRED** in the "green collapse": every fab stage after `intake` (apply/review/hydrate/ship/review-pr) collapses to the single green `apply` phase. `fabPhase(stage)`: `intake`‚Üí`intake`; everything else (incl. unknown/absent)‚Üí`apply`. The purple `pr` phase is chosen in `statusDotState`, never in `fabPhase`. `DotPhase = "intake" | "apply" | "pr" | "agent" | "agentPr" | "none"`. `PHASE_HUE: Record<DotPhase, string>` maps phase‚Üícore-hue token:

| Phase (`DotPhase`) | Family / source | Hue token |
|--------------------|-------------------|-----------|
| `intake` | cool fab ‚Äî `intake` stage | `text-blue-400` |
| `apply` | cool fab ‚Äî every other stage (green collapse) | `text-accent-green` |
| `pr` | cool fab ‚Äî the live PR (`fabChange && prNumber`) | `text-purple-400` |
| `agent` | warm ad-hoc agent ‚Äî working (no PR) | `text-yellow-400` |
| `agentPr` | warm ad-hoc agent ‚Äî its PR (`fresh agent && prNumber`) | `text-orange-400` |
| `none` | gray L0 floor (no journey) | `text-text-secondary` |

> **Why the green collapse**: the old ship/review-pr green barely rendered ‚Äî `/git-pr` creates the PR mid-ship, so purple takes the dot the moment `prNumber` exists. Collapsing apply‚Üíreview-pr to one green frees the palette to give the ad-hoc agent tier its own warm hues (yellow/orange) and reserves purple for the PR endpoint. This is the deliberate break from fab-kit's README 4-phase grouping (Intake/Execution/Completion/Shipping) ‚Äî noted in `docs/site/status-dot.md` and the matrix SVG.

**Shape = status** ‚Äî ONE vocabulary, five shapes, rendered by `StatusDot` from `{phase, shape}` with `color = PHASE_HUE[phase]` (except `skipped`, which forces `text-text-secondary` regardless of phase); the halo is layered on top when `state.waiting`:

| Shape (`DotShape`) | fab `fabDisplayState` / PR equivalent | Rendering |
|--------------------|----------------------------------------|-----------|
| `ring` | `pending` (PR: checks running) | hollow circle, `1.8px solid currentColor` border in phase hue, transparent fill |
| `solid` | `active`/`ready` (PR: open/healthy) | filled circle (`backgroundColor: currentColor`, `border: none`) in phase hue |
| `failed` | `failed` (PR: checks fail / changes requested) | **dotted ring** (`1.2px dotted currentColor`, transparent) in phase hue + a centered small **red** `bg-red-400` dot (`w-[3px] h-[3px]`) |
| `done` | `done` (PR: merged) | filled **sharp-cornered square** (`rounded-none`, `backgroundColor: currentColor`) in phase hue |
| `skipped` | `skipped` (PR: closed unmerged) | gray hollow ring (hue FORCED to `text-text-secondary`) |

Every shape EXCEPT `failed` renders at one uniform 7px footprint (`DOT_SIZE = "w-[7px] h-[7px]"`), so the filled square and the hollow circles read as the same size in the dense sidebar ‚Äî the square is distinguished by its sharp `rounded-none` corners, not by being larger (at 7px even a 1px radius blurs the square-vs-circle distinction). The **`failed` dot is the lone size exception** ‚Äî a slightly larger 9px footprint (`w-[9px] h-[9px]`): a CSS `dashed` border can't control its dash count and at 7px fits only ~4 dashes that read as flower petals, so it uses a `1.2px dotted` border at 9px, which renders as a delicate bead ring, with a `3px` red center sitting inside the 9px ring's ~6.6px hole (the earlier `dashed`/7px/4px-center description is superseded).

**Shape mappings**:
- `fabShape(displayState)`: `pending`‚Üí`ring`; `active`,`ready`‚Üí`solid`; `failed`‚Üí`failed`; `done`‚Üí`done`; `skipped`‚Üí`skipped`; unknown/absent‚Üí`solid` (a live fab window with a future/unrecognized state still reads as a live dot, not gone).
- `prShape(win)`: reuses `prDotState(win)` so the PR surfaces stay in lock-step ‚Äî `merged`‚Üí`done`, `fail`‚Üí`failed`, `pending`‚Üí`ring`, `healthy`‚Üí`solid`. Its `neutral` catch-all **splits on `prState`**: a **closed-unmerged** PR ‚Üí `skipped` (the gray hollow ring, labelled "PR ‚Äî closed"), an open / aged-out-merge ‚Üí `solid`. The `win.prState === "closed"` check lives in `prShape` on the `neutral` fall-through only ‚Äî `prDotState`'s own behavior is UNCHANGED (still returns `neutral` for closed). Note: post-D1 a closed PR never reaches `prShape` from the dot ladder anyway (`prOwnsDot` excludes `prState === "closed"`), so the closed‚Üískipped branch is exercised only by direct-call tests ‚Äî flagged as a deletion candidate.

**Red is used in exactly ONE way** across the whole system: the small center dot of a `failed` dotted ring. The old `fabDisplayState === "failed"` whole-dot red tint AND the old solid-red PR `fail` dot are both REMOVED ‚Äî a failure now reads as a dotted ring **in its phase hue** with only the red center.

**Gray L0 floor** (`phase: "none"`, lowest precedence, no fab change + no fresh agent) is **monochrome gray** ‚Äî color is reserved for the two journeys: `activity === "active"`‚Üígray `solid` filled circle, else gray `ring`. No phase hue is ever applied here.

**Full stage √ó status matrix** (rows = phase/hue, cols = status/shape). The **waiting halo overlays ANY cell** ‚Äî it is an overlay applicable to every tier, not a matrix row (spec ¬ß The Channel Model):

| Phase (hue) | pending | active/ready | failed | done | skipped/closed |
|-------------|---------|--------------|--------|------|-----------------|
| intake (blue) | blue ring | blue solid | blue dotted-ring + red center | blue square | ‚Äî |
| apply‚Üíreview-pr (green, collapsed) | green ring | green solid | green dotted-ring + red center | green square | gray ring |
| PR ‚Äî fab (purple) | purple ring (checks pending) | purple solid (open/healthy) | purple dotted-ring + red center (failing) | purple square (merged) | *(closed never owns the dot ‚Äî D1/D2)* |
| agent ‚Äî warm (yellow) | ‚Äî | yellow solid (active/waiting mid-turn) | ‚Äî | ‚Äî | yellow ring (idle) |
| PR ‚Äî agent (orange) | orange ring | orange solid | orange dotted-ring + red center | orange square | *(closed never owns the dot)* |
| plain (gray floor) | ‚Äî | gray solid (active) | ‚Äî | ‚Äî | gray ring (idle) |

**Accessibility** ‚Äî every dot carries `role="img"` + `aria-label` composed from journey + status + **additive attention suffix**, never color alone (colorblind a11y + Constitution V). (Since `260616-37ub-status-dot-tooltip` the native `title` was DROPPED ‚Äî the dot is wrapped by the custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card, which carries the same label text; `role="img"`/`aria-label` are retained as the accessible name, and `tabIndex={0}` was added so the card also opens on focus. See ¬ß Status Dot hover-card below.) `dotLabel(win, state)` now lives in its OWN module `status-dot-label.ts` (extracted `260706-y1ar` so both `status-dot.tsx` and `status-dot-tip.tsx` import it without an import cycle; `status-dot.tsx` re-exports it, keeping its public surface stable). It composes a **core label + additive `‚Äî agent waiting {dur}` suffix** (`coreLabel` + the `state.waiting` suffix):
- **fab PR tier** (`phase === "pr"`) / **agent PR tier** (`phase === "agentPr"`): PR-native words via `PR_SHAPE_LABEL` (`ring`‚Üí"checks running", `solid`‚Üí"open", `failed`‚Üí"failing", `done`‚Üí"merged", `skipped`‚Üí"closed") ‚Äî e.g. `"PR ‚Äî merged"`, `"PR ‚Äî open"`.
- **fab non-PR tier** (gated on `win.fabChange`, NOT phase ‚Äî so a fab window with an unknown/absent stage still reads `{stage-or-fab} ‚Äî {status}`, never a bare agent/tmux word): the real stage word via `SHAPE_LABEL` (`ring`‚Üí"pending", `solid`‚Üí"active", `failed`‚Üí"failed", `done`‚Üí"done", `skipped`‚Üí"skipped") ‚Äî e.g. `"apply ‚Äî active"`, `"review ‚Äî failed"`, `"intake ‚Äî pending"`.
- **warm agent tier** (`phase === "agent"`): agent-native words via `AGENT_SHAPE_LABEL` ‚Äî the idle `ring` reads **"idle"** (NOT the fab-stage "pending") and `solid` reads "active" ‚Äî e.g. `"agent ‚Äî active"`, `"agent ‚Äî idle"`. (T002 rework: the ring must read "idle" per the module doc + docs/site, not "pending".)
- **L0 floor**: the bare tmux activity word (`"active"`/`"idle"`).
- **Waiting suffix**: when `state.waiting`, append `" ‚Äî agent waiting {dur}"` (duration from the rk-computed `agentIdleDuration`, present for `waiting`/`idle`) ‚Äî so a review-failed waiting window reads `"review ‚Äî failed ‚Äî agent waiting 3m"` (R3).

**Impl symbols** ‚Äî in `pr-status-line.tsx` (colocated, see ¬ß PR Status exports): `DotShape`, `DotPhase` (`"intake" | "apply" | "pr" | "agent" | "agentPr" | "none"`), `StatusDotState = {phase, shape, waiting?}`, `fabPhase`, `fabShape`, `prShape`, `hasFreshAgent`, `prOwnsDot`, `PHASE_HUE`, and the rewritten two-family `statusDotState`. In `status-dot-label.ts`: `dotLabel` + the file-private `coreLabel` + the `SHAPE_LABEL`/`PR_SHAPE_LABEL`/`AGENT_SHAPE_LABEL` maps. In `status-dot.tsx`: `DOT_SIZE`, the `renderDot` shape markup (incl. the `rk-waiting-halo` class append), the `StatusDot` component, and a re-export of `dotLabel`; it imports `statusDotState`/`PHASE_HUE`/`DotShape`/`StatusDotState` from `pr-status-line.tsx` and `dotLabel` from `status-dot-label.ts`. In `status-dot-tip.tsx`: `StatusDotTip` + the pure `dotTipContent(win, state)` resolver (now also carrying an `agent` line ‚Äî see ¬ß Status Dot hover-card) + `DotLink`/`DotTipContent` types.

> **`PR_DOT_COLOR`/`PR_DOT_LABEL` are GONE.** `260615-yg7f` had the dot render its PR branch via `prDotState` + `PR_DOT_COLOR`/`PR_DOT_LABEL`. `260615-0hsz` deleted both maps. The dot renders from `PHASE_HUE` + the shape maps + `SHAPE_LABEL`/`PR_SHAPE_LABEL`/`AGENT_SHAPE_LABEL`. (`prDotState`/`PrDotState`/`isFailish`/`PR_STATE_COLORS`/`PR_CHECKS_COLORS`/`PR_REVIEW_COLORS` are UNCHANGED ‚Äî they serve the Pane-panel L3 `PR` register + its segments, and `prShape` reuses `prDotState`. The `PrStatusLine` component was **removed by `260715-jykd`** ‚Äî it had zero live render sites since the Dashboard deletion, and `260706-y1ar` had already folded the last full-line PR surface into the PANE panel's L3 register; its module `pr-status-line.tsx` survives as the shared-vocabulary home ‚Äî see ¬ß Shared PR vocabulary.)

**Why this shape** (`260706-y1ar` design decisions): (1) two families let a glance separate "my fab pipeline" (cool blue/green/purple) from "my ad-hoc agents" (warm yellow/orange) from "just a terminal" (gray) ‚Äî the user's own two-journey framing. (2) the additive yellow halo keeps family identity intact when attention is highest ‚Äî a hue-flip (rejected) would destroy exactly the signal the user is scanning for; a self-colored halo (rejected) vanishes in the reduced-motion static form. (3) D1's per-family PR ownership keeps derivation universal (PR in register/tip/line everywhere) while a plain shell never shows a mystifying PR dot. Rejected: fuchsia attention hue (the motivating amber collision is gone with the green collapse); hue-flip and self-colored halo (see above).

**Call sites** ‚Äî the three surfaces stay bare `<StatusDot win={win} />` (the hover-card lives inside `StatusDot` via the `renderDot` callback): (1) sidebar `WindowRow` ‚Äî ONE leading dot, now the row's ONLY status signal (¬ß Window rows / Row Minimalism); (2) the `SessionTiles` window tile ‚Äî leading dot before the window name (dot + name + fab-stage badge + text preview); (3) pane panel `WindowPanel` `headerRight` ‚Äî `<StatusDot win={win} />` before `{win.name}`. The dot's inputs (`agentState`, branch-derived `prNumber`/`prState`, `fabChange`/`fabStage`/`fabDisplayState`) all already ride `WindowInfo` via SSE; the halo keyframe is the only new CSS (`globals.css` `rk-waiting-halo`). Tests: `status-dot.test.tsx` (enumerates the decision-table rows across floor/agent/fab families √ó shapes + the additive halo on blue-core and green-failed cores + a11y label composition incl. the waiting suffix); `pr-status-line.test.tsx` covers the ladder + `prShape`; the reduced-motion static-ring form is asserted via the `agent-next-waiting.spec.ts` e2e (jsdom can't evaluate `globals.css` media queries).

### Status Dot hover-card (`status-dot-tip.tsx`) ‚Äî custom floating tooltip (`260616-37ub-status-dot-tooltip`)

`260616-37ub-status-dot-tooltip` replaced the dot's native HTML `title` tooltip with a custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card, built on the **first `@floating-ui/react` dependency in the frontend** (`app/frontend/package.json`). The motivation: native `title` cannot be styled, has a browser-fixed open delay, and **cannot contain links** ‚Äî and the dot needs interactive affordances (open the PR, jump to the docs explaining the state vocabulary). It is rendered on all three StatusDot surfaces (it lives inside `StatusDot`, so the call sites are untouched).

**Wiring** ‚Äî `StatusDotTip({ win, state, renderDot })` wraps the dot via a `renderDot(setReference, referenceProps)` callback: `StatusDot` owns the dot's shape/color markup and spreads the floating reference setter + interaction props onto its `<span>`, keeping the dot the floating anchor. `useFloating` (`placement: "top"`, middleware `offset(6)` / `flip()` / `shift({ padding: 8 })`, `whileElementsMounted: autoUpdate`) + `FloatingPortal` (renders to `document.body`, escaping the sidebar's `overflow:hidden` clip). Interactions: `useHover` (`delay: { open: 150, close: 100 }`, `handleClose: safePolygon()` ‚Äî the bridge so the pointer can travel dot ‚Üí card to click a link), `useFocus` (keyboard-first open, Constitution V), `useDismiss` (Escape / blur). The card surface uses the same theme tokens as `SwatchPopover` (`bg-bg-primary border border-border rounded-md shadow-lg`, monospace) ‚Äî no new color tokens.

**Deliberately NO `useRole({ role: "tooltip" })`** ‚Äî it was present in the plan but REMOVED in review: the W3C tooltip pattern requires a tooltip to contain NO interactive content, but this card holds real `<a>` links (PR + docs). Advertising `role="tooltip"` would lie to AT and wire a misleading `aria-describedby`. The dot's accessible name stays on its own `aria-label`; the links are real Tab-reachable controls, so no extra ARIA role is added.

**`tabIndex={0}` on the dot** is the focus-open tab stop (the floating-ui reference props don't add one). Accepted tradeoff (reviewed): on the sidebar the dot sits inside the row button/treeitem, so it becomes a second tab stop ahead of the row ‚Äî but a `<span role="img" tabindex="0">` is focusable yet NOT "interactive content" in the HTML button content-model sense (valid markup), and the sidebar tree keydown handler still anchors on `closest('[role="treeitem"]')`, so arrow-nav works from a focused dot.

**Content** ‚Äî the pure `dotTipContent(win, state) ‚Üí { label, agent, links, fetchedAtEpoch }` resolver: `label` REUSES the exported `dotLabel(win, state)` (single source of truth shared with the dot's `aria-label`, imported from `status-dot-label.ts`). Since `260706-y1ar` it also carries an **`agent` line** (`agent: waiting 3m` / `active` / `idle 12m`; `null` when no `agentState`) rendered on EVERY tier (fab, PR, warm, or floor) ‚Äî post-Row-Minimalism the tip is the recovery path for the removed row stage word + durations (R7). Any window with a `prUrl` gets one `"Open PR #N"` link ‚Äî on ANY tier including the gray floor (T005 rework): PR-dot OWNERSHIP is family-gated (D1) but the derived PR itself is UNIVERSAL (Principle X / decision-table row 10), so the tip surfaces the link wherever a `prUrl` exists, exactly like the PANE panel's L3 register. (`onClick` `stopPropagation` so opening the PR doesn't also select/navigate the underlying sidebar row ‚Äî the same stop-bubbling PR-link idiom the now-removed `PrStatusLine` used.) **Every** card additionally renders a fixed docs-link icon (NOT part of `links[]`) ‚Üí `https://github.com/sahil87/run-kit/blob/main/docs/site/status-dot.md` (GitHub blob, top of doc ‚Äî `docs/site` is not served locally, matching `top-bar.tsx`'s `NOTIFICATIONS_HELP_URL` convention).

**Freshness line ‚Äî "checked Xs ago" (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`)**: `dotTipContent` gained a fourth field `fetchedAtEpoch: number | null` ‚Äî the window's `prFetchedAt` (the collector-join `PrFetchedAt` timestamp, architecture.md ¬ß PR-Status SSE Join) parsed to **epoch SECONDS** (`Date.parse(win.prFetchedAt)` ‚Üí `Math.floor(/1000)`), or `null` when `prFetchedAt` is absent OR unparseable (`Date.parse` ‚Üí `NaN`), so the card omits the line rather than rendering "checked NaNs ago". Rendered by a dedicated **`FreshnessLine` leaf component** (NOT inline in `StatusDotTip`): it owns a live `useNow()` clock (epoch seconds) and displays `checked ${formatDuration(nowSeconds - fetchedAtEpoch)} ago` (`data-testid="dot-tip-checked"`, styled like the agent line) ‚Äî reusing `formatDuration` (`lib/format.ts`, the Ns/Nm/Nh convention) rather than adding a relative-time formatter, and returning `null` when `fetchedAtEpoch === null`. **Why its own component**: `FreshnessLine` is mounted ONLY inside the open hover-card (`{open && ‚Ä¶}`), so its per-second `useNow()` re-render is leaf-scoped to a card that is actually open ‚Äî the dot wrapper never ticks (the leaf-scoped-`useNow` contract, ¬ß Render Performance / use-now.ts). After a manual refresh the timestamp visibly resets ‚Äî the ambient version of the same trust signal the refresh-button checkmark gives, useful without clicking.

**Tests** ‚Äî `status-dot.test.tsx` covers `dotTipContent` (PR-phase ‚Üí one link with correct `href`; fab/tmux ‚Üí zero links; `label === dotLabel`) and asserts the dot has no `title` (`aria-label` instead). `status-dot-tip.test.tsx` (added `260715-nwla`) covers the freshness line: the "checked Xs ago" line renders with the formatted relative time when `prFetchedAt` is present and is omitted when absent/unparseable. New e2e `tests/e2e/status-dot-tip.spec.ts` (+ sibling `.spec.md`) proves hover-open, focus-open, Escape-dismiss, PR-link + docs-icon presence, and link click-through.

## Attention Surfacing (`waiting` rollups + nav, `260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing`)

The per-window `waiting` overlay (agent blocked on a human) propagates UP the hierarchy as **count badges** and drives a **keyboard-first navigation** action and a **board-pane seam**. This is the UI half of #314's three-state `agentState` ‚Äî see [agent-state](agent-state.md). All counts derive from the existing SSE session data already in the client ‚Äî **no new endpoint, no `setInterval`/fetch** (Constitution II / code-quality anti-patterns).

**Shared rollup helpers** (`lib/waiting.ts`) ‚Äî the single source of truth so every surface counts identically: `isWaiting(win)` (= `win.agentState === "waiting"`, keyed on the server-side window-level rollup that already applies `waiting > active > idle` across panes), `countWaitingWindows(windows)`, `countWaitingInSessions(sessions)`. Pure functions over the streamed `WindowInfo`/`ProjectSession` shape.

**`WaitingBadge`** (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) ‚Äî a small count chip mounted unconditionally; **renders `null` when `count <= 0`** (attention badges are present only when they mean "something needs you"). Styling follows the existing count-chip vocabulary but in the **constant yellow** of the waiting overlay (`bg-yellow-400/15 text-yellow-400`, theme-independent ‚Äî the same "yellow = an agent needs you now" glance language as the status-dot halo), plus a `‚öÝ` glyph. It is TEXT, not motion (the pulse lives on the per-window dot/seam) ‚Äî legible via color + count + `aria-label`, never color-only. Mounted on four surfaces:

- **Session row** (`sidebar/session-row.tsx`) ‚Äî count of the session's waiting windows (`countWaitingWindows(session.windows)`), rendered after the session name button (R8).
- **Host-page TMUX SERVERS server tile** (`host-overview-page.tsx`) ‚Äî per-server count summed over the server's sessions (`countWaitingInSessions(sessionsByServer.get(name) ?? [])`), absolutely positioned top-right on the tile. One glance at `/` answers "does anything need me" (R9). Only attached servers stream windows, so an unattached server's count is 0 (badge absent) ‚Äî never a wrong count.
- **Board header** (top-bar `BoardModeInfo`, `top-bar.tsx`) ‚Äî count of the board's waiting panes (`waitingPaneCount` prop), rendered in the board-mode left info between the pane/server counts and the `‚åò[‚åò] cycle` hint (R10).
- **Sidebar SERVER-panel server tile** (`sidebar/server-panel.tsx`, `260708-4li7-sidebar-server-tile-waiting-badge`) ‚Äî the fourth server-level surface, per-server count over the server's sessions. Placement **differs** from the Host-page tile: it rides the **same flex row as the tile's "N sess" count, right-aligned** (`flex items-center justify-between`) rather than absolute top-right, because the sidebar tile already occupies its top-right with a hover-revealed palette/kill action cluster (`top-1 right-1 z-10`) ‚Äî copying the Host-page tile's `absolute right-2 top-2` would collide. `ServerTile` takes a plain `waitingCount: number`; `ServerPanel` takes the optional `waitingCounts?: Map<string, number>` and forwards `waitingCounts?.get(name) ?? 0` per tile, keeping the presentational panel decoupled from session data. The Sidebar computes the map in `sidebar/index.tsx` via `useMemo(() => ‚Ä¶, [sessionsByServer])` over the already-consumed `sessionsByServer` (same `countWaitingInSessions` helper). Attached-server-only by construction (an unattached server is absent from `sessionsByServer` ‚Üí count 0 ‚Üí badge absent), the same accepted caveat as the Host-page tile ‚Äî no eager attach-all is added (before `260716-qf3j-state-socket` each attach opened a per-server EventSource that pressured the HTTP/1.1 6-per-origin pool on plaintext origins; the state socket removed that budget concern ‚Äî all subscriptions ride one WS ‚Äî but the deliberate lazy-attach behavior is retained, so an unattached server still shows no badge).

**Board-pane waiting seam** (`board/board-pane.tsx` + `board-page.tsx`) ‚Äî a waiting board pane gets a **3px pulsing yellow seam** (border-width system; the `rk-waiting-seam` class + `border-[3px]`), the board-pane form of the status-dot halo. Border precedence: a `waiting` pane always shows the seam (attention is the highest-priority signal); a focused-AND-waiting pane layers the accent focus shadow on top so it reads both. Under `prefers-reduced-motion` the seam is static yellow (`globals.css`). `BoardEntry` is a thin shape with no `agentState`, so `BoardPageContent` **joins each pinned pane back to its live `WindowInfo`** via `(server, windowId)` against the streamed `sessionsByServer` (use-boards attaches every board server, so window data incl. `agentState` is flowing) ‚Äî a `waitingWindowIds` set (`${server}:${windowId}` keys) drives both the per-pane seam and the header count; a pane whose window is not yet in the snapshot is simply not waiting (no wrong signal).
