**`Agent: Next waiting` palette action** (`app.tsx` `agentActions`, R11 ‚Äî keyboard-first, Constitution V): cycles focus through windows whose rolled-up `agentState` is `waiting`, **current server first** (in sidebar order, from `flatWindows`) then other **attached** servers (from a live `sessionsByServerRef.current` read ‚Äî unattached servers' window data isn't streamed, a known constraint). No-op with a `"No agents waiting"` toast when none. The cycle arithmetic is the pure `nextWaitingTarget(ordered, currentServer, currentWindowId)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested): empty ‚Üí `null`; current window not in the list ‚Üí first target (jump in); current IS a target ‚Üí the next one **with wraparound** (`(idx+1) % len`). This is a deliberate contrast with `palette-move.ts` (reorder arithmetic, which does NOT wrap) ‚Äî do NOT extend that module. Same-server targets navigate via `navigateToWindow`; cross-server targets `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window" })` (and close the mobile drawer). The action is appended to `paletteActions` as `agentActions`.

## Iframe Window (the `web` lens renderer)

`app/frontend/src/components/iframe-window.tsx` ‚Äî the renderer for the **`web` lens** (¬ß Window Views (Lens Model)). Since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` it is **no longer selected by `@rk_type` identity** ‚Äî `app.tsx` renders it when the window's *resolved view* is `web`: `resolvedView === "web" && currentWindow?.rkUrl ? <IframeWindow ‚Ä¶/> : <TerminalClient/>` (`resolveView` bakes in availability, so an iframe-typed window with no `rkUrl` resolves to `tty` exactly as the old `rkType === "iframe" && rkUrl` AND-gate did ‚Äî no existing window changes behavior). Bottom bar is NOT rendered for the web lens (no terminal to send keys to). The component is **presentational** ‚Äî it takes `windowId`, `rkUrl`, and an `onSwitchToTty: () => void` callback and owns NO view/URL/localStorage logic (that lives in `window-view.ts` + `app.tsx`); it no longer imports `updateWindowType` (¬ß Window Views ‚Üí decoupling).

**Layout**: Outer wrapper `flex flex-col flex-1 min-h-0` with two children: URL bar (`shrink-0`) and iframe (`flex-1`).

**URL Bar**: Thin toolbar above the iframe (`border-b border-border bg-bg-primary`). Four elements:
- **Refresh button** (‚Üª `&#x21bb;`) ‚Äî forces iframe reload by clearing `src` to `"about:blank"` then re-setting it via `setTimeout(0)`. Styled: `w-7 h-7 rounded hover:bg-bg-card text-text-secondary`
- **URL input field** ‚Äî shows current `rkUrl`, editable. On Enter, calls `updateWindowUrl(server, windowId, url)` which (since `260529-jad6`) delegates to the unified `setWindowOptions(server, windowId, { "@rk_url": url })` ‚Üí `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/options` (partial-merge ‚Äî only `@rk_url` is touched). On API failure, reverts input to the SSE-confirmed `rkUrl`. Styled: `bg-bg-card text-text-primary text-sm px-2 py-1 rounded border border-border`. **This is the one POST the web lens still fires** ‚Äî editing the content ADDRESS is *substrate* state (shared, POSTed, everyone sees it ‚Äî spec R7), distinct from switching which lens you look through (per-viewer, no POST).
- **Submit indicator** (‚èé `&#x23ce;`) ‚Äî decorative visual affordance (`text-text-secondary text-xs`)
- **`>_` switch-to-terminal button** (`aria-label="Switch to terminal"`) ‚Äî since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` it calls the injected `onSwitchToTty()` prop (which runs `app.tsx`'s `switchView("tty")` ‚Üí drops `?view=` + writes localStorage), **NOT** `updateWindowType(server, windowId, "")`. It is now a per-viewer *view switch*, so flipping to the terminal and back preserves the window (no `@rk_type` mutation, no global flip ‚Äî the e2e asserts zero `/options` POSTs across a flip). This is the retrofit's core decoupling (was the sole in-component `@rk_type` mutation site).

**SSE Sync**: A `useEffect` on `rkUrl` syncs both the URL bar text and iframe `src`. Uses a `currentSrcRef` to avoid re-setting iframe `src` when the URL hasn't actually changed (prevents unnecessary reloads on identical SSE ticks). When `rkUrl` changes externally (Claude or another process runs `tmux set-option`), the URL bar updates and iframe navigates automatically.

**Proxy URL conversion**: `toProxySrc(url)` converts localhost URLs to proxy paths: `http://localhost:8080/docs` -> `/proxy/8080/docs`. Non-localhost URLs pass through unchanged. Pattern: `^https?:\/\/(?:localhost|127\.0\.0\.1):(\d+)(\/.*)?$`.

**Iframe attributes**: `sandbox="allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-forms allow-popups allow-modals"`, `title="Proxied content"`, `border-0`.

**Window creation**: "Window: New Iframe Window" command palette action (id `create-iframe-window`) opens a `Dialog` with two inputs: window name (autofocused, Enter focuses URL input) and URL (Enter creates window). Create button disabled until both fields non-empty. Calls `createWindow(server, session, name, undefined, "iframe", url)` ‚Äî the extended API client function passes `rkType` and `rkUrl` in the POST body. Backend uses `CreateWindowWithOptions` for atomic `\;`-chained tmux command. Only shown when a session is active. **Unchanged by `260714-t97o-web-view-lens`** ‚Äî synthetic iframe windows are still created exactly as before; `@rk_type=iframe` now just means "**default view = web**" (a creation-time hint, ¬ß Window Views ‚Üí `defaultView`), not a locked identity.

## Window Views (Lens Model) (`260714-t97o-web-view-lens`; chat lens `260714-r7rq`)

The model (`docs/specs/window-views.md`, rules R1‚ÄìR7): **a window ROW is a substrate** (a supervised tmux pane); **a VIEW is a lens** over one derivable output of that pane (the tty is a lens; an iframe of the pane's HTTP service is a lens; the parsed agent transcript is a lens; later: desktop). **Which lenses a window offers is a derived capability set; which lens YOU look through is per-viewer client state** carried in the URL + localStorage ‚Äî never a server-side `@rk_type` mutation, never part of the window's identity. `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` built the generalized switcher machinery (spec R4 ‚Äî "whichever ships first builds it") and retrofitted the shipped iframe feature onto it; **the chat view (`260714-r7rq`) folds into this SAME machinery** (its interim `?view=chat`-only mechanism ‚Äî `chat-view-resolve.ts`, `use-chat-view-pref.ts`, `SegmentedViewToggle` ‚Äî was retired). Frontend-only; no Go/API changes (`@rk_type`/`@rk_url`/`@rk_chat` plumbing and `POST /options` are untouched ‚Äî the SSE payload already carried `rkType`/`rkUrl`/`chatProvider`).

Three lenses are implemented: `tty` (always available, `TerminalClient`), `web` (available when `rkUrl` is non-empty, `IframeWindow`), and `chat` (available when `chatProvider` is non-empty, `ChatView` ‚Äî the read-only transcript renderer, ¬ß Chat View). Capabilities are orthogonal and STACK (spec R5): one window can offer `tty`+`web`+`chat` at once. The registry is open-ended ‚Äî `desktop` adds a `ViewName` member, an availability clause, a `defaultView` hint, and a `ViewSwitcher` segment, NOT a new component/route/window-type.

### Pure view-model helper ‚Äî `lib/window-view.ts`

The single source of view logic ‚Äî pure, DOM-free, colocated `window-view.test.ts` (the same pattern as `window-transition.ts`/`navigation.ts`). Both the `app.tsx` render branch AND the window-switch transition classification (¬ß Window-Switch Slide Transition) call `resolveView`, so it MUST live in one place (no drift). Helpers take a minimal structural `{ rkType?, rkUrl?, chatProvider? }` shape (assignable from `WindowInfo`):

- **`ViewName = "tty" | "web" | "chat"`** ‚Äî the lens union.
- **`hasWebUrl(win)` / `hasChat(win)`** ‚Äî the single-source availability predicates: `rkUrl` non-empty after `.trim()` (whitespace-only `@rk_url` is NOT web ‚Äî no blank-src iframe); `chatProvider` non-empty (mirrors the backend `resolveWindowChat` gate).
- **`availableViews(win): ViewName[]`** (spec R1/R3) ‚Äî `["tty"]`, plus `"web"` when `hasWebUrl`, plus `"chat"` when `hasChat`. **Availability is decoupled from `@rk_type`**: an iframe-typed window with no URL offers only `tty` (matches the old render gate's AND-condition). Returned in the registry's fixed order (`chat > web > tty`) via a `HINT_ORDER` filter ‚Äî so a stacked window yields `["chat","web","tty"]`.
- **`defaultView(win): ViewName`** (spec R5) ‚Äî the window's default lens, applied ONLY when the URL and localStorage carry no choice: `"web"` when `rkType === "iframe"` AND `rkUrl` is set, else `"tty"`. `@rk_type=iframe` is **demoted from identity to a creation-time default-view hint** (no data migration). Structured as spec R5's ordered hint precedence `desktop > chat > web > tty` (module const `HINT_ORDER`, only `web`/`tty` wired) so later lenses add a hint clause, not a branch. **`chat` sits in `HINT_ORDER` for capability ORDERING only ‚Äî it contributes NO default hint**: a chat-capable window still defaults to `tty` unless the viewer chose chat (preserves `260714-r7rq`'s terminal-default; a chat-capable window opens on the terminal, chat is one click / `Ctrl+\`` away).
- **`resolveView(searchView, stored, win): ViewName`** (spec R2) ‚Äî precedence **URL `?view=` (if that view is available) ‚Üí localStorage (if available) ‚Üí `defaultView(win)`**. Any unavailable value falls through; the chain always bottoms out at `tty`, so an unavailable `?view=web` deep link (window with no `rkUrl`) OR `?view=chat` on a chat-less window renders the terminal, never a broken iframe / empty chat shell. `searchView`/`stored` are untrusted strings validated against the capability set here ‚Äî callers pass raw values.
- **`nextView(available, current): ViewName | null`** ‚Äî the cycle successor (wraps); `null` when < 2 views or `current` is absent. Powers the `Cmd/Ctrl+.` chord (pure so the order is unit-testable).
- **`shouldSuppressViewChord(target): boolean`** ‚Äî the input-gating predicate for the chord, **byte-for-byte the same rule as `shell.tsx`'s `‚åò\` sidebar toggle**: suppress only inside a NON-xterm INPUT/TEXTAREA/contenteditable (xterm's hidden helper textarea is the terminal's normal focus, so it must NOT be suppressed ‚Äî `target.closest(".xterm") != null` is the exception). jsdom-safe (`contentEditable` attribute fallback for the missing `isContentEditable` getter).
- **localStorage helpers** ‚Äî **value-bearing** key `runkit-window-view:{server}:{windowId}` storing the view NAME, now including `"chat"` (absent = default). `windowViewStorageKey`/`readStoredView`/`writeStoredView`, try/catch-noop per `chrome-context.tsx`. **This supersedes the chat plan's key-present `runkit:chat-view:` `board-autofit`-style convention** (spec R2 explicitly supersedes; no data migration ‚Äî the interim keys were live only hours and self-correct on the next toggle) ‚Äî value-bearing generalizes past two states.

### `?view=` search param ‚Äî `router.tsx`

`view` is a **validated search param** on `terminalRoute` (spec R2, Constitution IV: no new route ‚Äî it is the codebase's first `validateSearch`). The exported pure `validateTerminalSearch(search): { view?: "web" | "chat" }` accepts `view === "web"` or `view === "chat"` and **drops any other/unknown/non-string value** (returns `{}` ‚Äî treated as absent, NEVER errored), so a stale/garbage deep link degrades to the default view. It is wired as the route's `validateSearch` (ONE key ‚Äî the merge briefly had two) and unit-tested directly in `router.test.ts` (accepts `web`/`chat`, drops `?view=bogus`/non-string/absent without throwing). The `declare module "@tanstack/react-router"` `Register` block types `.view` as `"web" | "chat" | undefined`, so `useSearch({ strict: false })` in `app.tsx` reads it **with no `as` cast** (code-quality type-narrowing ‚Äî `tsc --noEmit` clean).

### `app.tsx` integration ‚Äî resolution, `switchView`, render branch

`app.tsx` (terminal route) computes `searchView = useSearch({ strict: false }).view`, `storedView = readStoredView(server, windowParam)`, `currentViews = availableViews(currentWindow)` (memoized), and `resolvedView = resolveView(searchView, storedView, currentWindow)`. There is ONE view-state block (the chat feature's parallel `resolveChatView`/`useChatViewPref`/`activeView` block was deleted). It owns one stable `switchView(view)` callback (deps `server`/`windowParam`/`navigate`):
- writes localStorage (`writeStoredView`),
- `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params, search: view !== "tty" ? { view } : {}, replace: true })` ‚Äî **`web`/`chat` ride the URL (`?view=web` / `?view=chat`); `tty` DROPS the param** (clean URL; tty is the always-available default). The URL is the shareable/deep-linkable seam (push-notification-ready); localStorage is the per-window stickiness that survives R6's param-drop on a window switch. Both seams are required.

The **render branch** selects the renderer by resolved view ‚Äî `chatViewActive ? <ChatView ‚Ä¶/> : resolvedView === "web" && currentWindow?.rkUrl ? <IframeWindow onSwitchToTty={() => switchView("tty")} ‚Ä¶/> : <TerminalClient/>`, where `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"` (`resolveView` already bakes in the `chatProvider` availability gate, so a chat-less window never resolves to chat ‚Äî no separate `chatAvailable` guard). NOT by `rkType === "iframe" && rkUrl`. The **tty-branch "Switch to iframe view" `</>` hint bar** (a SECOND `@rk_type`-mutation site that called `updateWindowType(..., "iframe")`) is **removed** ‚Äî switching to web is now the ViewSwitcher/palette/`>_` job, none of which mutate `@rk_type` (spec R7).

### ViewSwitcher chip ‚Äî `components/view-switcher.tsx`

The ONE switcher UX all lenses share (spec R4) ‚Äî a generic segmented chip: props `{ views: ViewName[]; active: ViewName; onSelect }`. Since `260717-6anu-mobile-view-switcher-overflow` it is the **first candidate of the right-cluster overflow registry** ‚Äî NO longer a leading exempt L1 control (see ¬ß Right cluster ‚Üí overflow chevron menu). As the FIRST `rightItems` entry it keeps its leftmost in-bar position but becomes the **first control to yield** under width pressure (before any L1 split), collapsing into the "More controls" chevron menu as per-view rows (`ViewSwitcherMenuRows`) so the center heading regains its space on narrow viewports (the common phone case). Fed via the `useRegisterTopBarSlot` slot context (`availableViews`/`activeView`/`onSelectView` are the ONLY view fields on the slot ‚Äî the chat feature's `view`/`chatAvailable`/`onSetView` were removed). Renders `null` when `views.length <= 1` (both the chip and the caller gate on this, so a tty-only window shows no chip). Presentational ‚Äî owns no view logic.

- **Segment DISPLAY order is `[tty|web|chat]`** via a component-local `DISPLAY_ORDER = ["tty","web","chat"]`, **deliberately decoupled from `window-view.ts`'s `HINT_ORDER`** (`chat>web>tty`, which governs only default/capability precedence ‚Äî the two orderings answer different questions). Any view not in `DISPLAY_ORDER` sorts to the END (defensive ‚Äî a future lens still renders); later lenses slot into `DISPLAY_ORDER`. Since `260717-6anu` the tty-first ordering is applied by a shared module-local helper `orderViews(views)` (listed-in-`DISPLAY_ORDER` first, unlisted appended) used by BOTH the in-bar pill AND the overflow `ViewSwitcherMenuRows`, so bar‚Üîmenu ordering can never drift.
- Active segment is **inverse-video** (`bg-accent-green text-bg-primary`); house `rk-glint` hover vocabulary (reduced-motion-safe ‚Äî the glint is a CSS media-query no-op, no JS animation). `role="group" aria-label="Window view"` + `data-testid="view-toggle"` + per-segment `aria-pressed`/`aria-label` (`Terminal view`/`Web view`/`Chat view`). **No `hidden sm:*` breakpoint gate** (`inline-flex`) ‚Äî but since `260717-6anu` visibility is **space-driven via the overflow registry, NOT "visible at ALL breakpoints"**: the pill renders inline while the right cluster has room and otherwise collapses into the chevron menu as `ViewSwitcherMenuRows`. Because it is the FIRST candidate it is the first to yield, so on a phone width (and on a squeezed desktop pane) a long-named multi-view window's pill is in the menu, not inline ‚Äî while a very short heading legitimately keeps it inline (no crowding exists then). Segment glyphs are the **lowercase view names** `tty`/`web`/`chat` (spec R4's `[tty|chat]` style).
- **Overflow representation ‚Äî `ViewSwitcherMenuRows`** (`260717-6anu`, exported from `view-switcher.tsx`, same `{views, active, onSelect}` props): when the `view-switcher` registry entry overflows, the pill is represented as **one `role="menuitem"` row per available view** in the shared `orderViews()` tty-first order, labeled `View: {VIEW_LABEL[view]}` (`View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` ‚Äî the palette's `View:` vocabulary). The **active** row is inverse-video accent-green (matching the pill's active segment) and carries `aria-pressed`, so the menu keeps the lens-indicator role while the pill is collapsed; clicking a row calls the same `onSelect(view)` and the menu's role-keyed handler closes the panel. Row styling composes the shared `MENU_ROW_BASE` + `MENU_ROW_REST`/`MENU_ROW_ACTIVE` variants hosted in `top-bar-overflow-menu.tsx` (`tabIndex={-1}` per the menu's roving-focus model), so it stays in lockstep with every other overflow-menu row. Returns `null` for a single-view window (mirrors the pill). Follows the multi-row `NotificationMenuRows` `menuRender` precedent. No NEW inline lens indicator is added while collapsed ‚Äî the marked row + the view content itself (chat bubbles vs. terminal) carry lens identity, and the heading stays the static `Window:` in every lens (¬ß Heading is a static `Window:`).

### Palette parity + keyboard shortcuts (Constitution V)

- **`View: Terminal` / `View: Web` / `View: Chat` palette actions** (AppShell `viewActions` in `app.tsx`), each visible only when its view is **available AND not the current** view ‚Äî the gating + label + shortcut-hint composition live in a pure builder `buildViewActions(available, resolved, onSwitch)` in `lib/palette-view.ts` (mirrors `lib/palette-move.ts`/`palette-update.ts`, unit-tested in `palette-view.test.ts`). The per-entry `shortcut` hint tracks the binding that reaches it: `View: Chat` (and `View: Terminal` when LEAVING chat) show `` Ctrl+` `` (the chat toggle); every other switch shows `‚åò.` (the cycle). These **REPLACE the retired `toggle-iframe-terminal` action** (which mutated `@rk_type`) AND the chat feature's second `buildViewActions(chatAvailable, activeView, onSetView)` call (one call now).
- **`Cmd/Ctrl+.` cycles the current window's lenses** ‚Äî a window-level `keydown` effect in `app.tsx` that `preventDefault()`s (so xterm doesn't also receive it), gated by `shouldSuppressViewChord` and calling `switchView(nextView(views, active))`. No-op when < 2 views. Live view/window values read via a `viewCycleRef` so the listener is stable across SSE ticks. Chosen against the live chord registry (`‚åòK` palette, `‚åò\` sidebar, `‚åò]`/`‚åò[` board pane-cycle) ‚Äî a free binding in the `‚åò<punctuation>` family; `Ctrl+.` is inert in readline (unlike `Ctrl+/`‚Üíundo). Documented in the **App section of the Keyboard Shortcuts dialog** (`ShortcutRow label="Cycle view" keys={["‚åò."]}`).
- **`` Ctrl+` `` toggles tty‚Üîchat** (`use-chat-view-shortcut.ts`, ¬ß Chat View ‚Üí shortcut) ‚Äî the shipped VS-Code "toggle terminal" binding, now speaking `ViewName` (`"tty"`, not `"terminal"`), enabled when `currentViews.includes("chat")`, toggling via `switchView`. Documented as `ShortcutRow label="Toggle chat / terminal" keys={["Ctrl+\`"]}`.

### Heading is a static `Window:` in every lens (spec R4 reversal ‚Äî `260714-uco1`)

The top-bar center `PageType: name` heading on the terminal route reads a **static `Window: <window>` in every lens** (tty / web / chat) ‚Äî it does NOT follow the active view (¬ß Window Heading). A single `WINDOW_PREFIX = "Window:"` constant (`top-bar.tsx`) replaces the retired `TERMINAL_PREFIX` and is passed as a constant `prefix` into `WindowHeading` at the terminal-mode center cell; the lens-following `terminalHeadingPrefix()` helper and the `WEB_PREFIX`/`CHAT_PREFIX` constants were **removed**. Rationale (`260714-uco1`, a deliberate reversal of `docs/specs/window-views.md` R4's "the center page heading follows the lens" sentence ‚Äî updated in-spec within that change): the heading identifies the WINDOW (the substrate); which lens you look through is shown by the `ViewSwitcher` (the overflow-registry chip ‚Äî or its `View:` menu rows when collapsed, `260717-6anu`), not the heading (per window-views.md "rows are substrates, views are lenses"). Bonus: the name's anchor no longer jumps on a lens switch, since the prefix width no longer changes with the lens (¬ß Center-heading stable anchor + nav affordances). The click-to-rename affordance and boot-sweep treatment are unchanged. (The `WindowHeading` prefix-flip replay machinery ‚Äî `prevPrefixRef` + the prefix-keyed effect, `top-bar.tsx` ~:1053/:1108 ‚Äî is now inert since the sole call site passes the constant `WINDOW_PREFIX`; it survives as a plan-recorded deletion candidate.)

### `?view` drops on window switch (spec R6)

Navigating to a DIFFERENT window carries NO `view` param ‚Äî each destination window resolves its own last-view/default independently. Client-side navigations (sidebar/palette/breadcrumb via `navigateToWindow`, plus the window-death redirect and SSE-writeback switch) omit/clear `search`, and TanStack Router's `final` search middleware returns `{}` when `dest.search` is absent, so an outgoing `?view=web`/`?view=chat` does not leak onto the target. (Simplest semantics ‚Äî per-window localStorage covers the intent; the web-view-lens e2e persistence case exercises this through a real sidebar-click navigation to guard against a future `retainSearchParams`/router-upgrade regression.) The one exception is the `Agent: Next waiting` / WaitingBadge deep-link, which INTENTIONALLY sets `?view=chat` for a chat-capable target (¬ß Chat View ‚Üí WaitingBadge).

### Window-switch transition classification (one rule)

The window-switch slide transition's `switchTransitionRef` carries a SINGLE `ungatedIds` set: window ids whose EFFECTIVE resolved view is **not `tty`** ‚Äî i.e. they render `<IframeWindow>` (web) or `<ChatView>` (chat), neither of which has the terminal's xterm first-write receipt seam, so they must use the transition's **ungated capture** (a first-write gate would never release for a non-xterm surface ‚Üí stuck transition / blank pane). Computed at render time from `resolveView(undefined, readStoredView(server, id), win) !== "tty"` (URL is unknown for a not-yet-navigated target, so only localStorage + default hint decide). This replaced the merge's TWO sets (`iframeIds` via `=== "web"` + a lazy-`readChatViewPrefKey` `chatCapableIds`) with one `resolveView`-keyed classification ‚Äî the same "keyed on resolveView, not `@rk_type`" invariant as the render branch (¬ß Window-Switch Slide Transition).

### e2e ‚Äî `web-view-lens.spec.ts` / `chat-view.spec.ts` (+ `.spec.md`)

`web-view-lens.spec.ts` drives real tmux (own session, `window-heading.spec.ts` pattern), setting `@rk_url`/`@rk_type` via `tmux set-option -w`. Its `describe` defaults to a wide **1440px** desktop width (the 1280px "Desktop Chrome" default sits right at the drop threshold once the pill is a candidate, so 1440px is used to clear the whole cluster deterministically). Covers: chip appears only on web-capable windows; flip to web then back preserves the window and fires **zero `/options` POSTs** (asserted via `page.on("request")`); deep link `?view=web` cold-loads the iframe (lens proven by the web chip / iframe + the `?view=web` URL ‚Äî the heading stays the static `Window:` prefix since `260714-uco1`, no longer a lens indicator); `?view=web` on a URL-less window falls back to the terminal; legacy `@rk_type=iframe`+url defaults to web with the chip present; last-view persistence across a real client-side window switch away and back. Since `260717-6anu` the former "switcher chip visible at 375px (all breakpoints)" assertion is **superseded by the space-driven registry contract**: at 375px with a realistically long window name the pill **overflows into the "More controls" chevron menu** (assert the `View: Terminal`/`View: Web` rows + no horizontal overflow), and at desktop width it returns to the bar as the inline chip. `chat-view.spec.ts` covers the chat lens through the SAME unified chip (`view-toggle`, `Chat view` segment): chip gated on `chatProvider`, flip to chat (lens proven via `view-toggle`/`chat-view` presence + `?view=chat` URL, not the heading prefix), the `` Ctrl+` `` toggle, `?view=chat` cold-load, the bubble/tool-card/pending renderer, reduced-motion ‚Äî and the 375px "single-line top bar" test now asserts the **collapsed-pill contract** (long window name ‚Üí pill in the chevron menu as `View:` rows, heading room, single line, no horizontal overflow) rather than an inline `view-toggle` pill. **Since `260717-vhvz` it drives chat over the state socket, NOT SSE**: it dropped its `**/api/windows/*/chat/stream*` `text/event-stream` route mock for the extended `_state-socket-mock.ts` (answers a `kind:"chat"` subscribe with an offset-bearing ack + optional `chat`/`chat-state`/`chat-reset` emits) plus a plain `GET /api/windows/*/chat*` backfill `page.route`; the terminal stub stays on `/ws/terminals` (memory `relay-mux-stale-ws-stub-class` ‚Äî no `/relay/` or SSE stubs). `connection-budget.spec.ts` took its final any-route ‚â§2 WS + 0 SSE form with a chat-lens case (architecture.md ¬ß Testing).

## Chat View (`260714-r7rq-chat-read-frontend`)

A **read-only HTML chat view over the SAME agent pane** ‚Äî a second view over the tmux pane, never a substrate (the pane stays the agent's parent, Constitution VI; the view only renders the streamed transcript). It is the **`chat` lens** of the window-view model (¬ß Window Views (Lens Model)) ‚Äî addressed by `?view=chat` on the existing `/$server/$window` terminal route (Constitution IV, no new route). **All view-state plumbing ‚Äî the `?view=` param, availability gate, the ViewSwitcher chip, localStorage persistence, palette parity, the `` Ctrl+` `` shortcut, and the switch-transition classification ‚Äî is the UNIFIED machinery** described in ¬ß Window Views (Lens Model); this section owns only what is chat-SPECIFIC: the `chatProvider` gate, the connection-dot semantics, the renderer/stream, and the WaitingBadge deep-link. (The heading is no longer part of the plumbing ‚Äî since `260714-uco1` it reads a static `Window:` in every lens, ¬ß Heading is a static `Window:`.) The renderer + data layer live in `architecture.md`/[chat](/run-kit/chat.md) ¬ß Chat View Frontend. Change 3 of the HTML-agent-chat-view stack (consumes the Change-2 backend, `chat.md`). **Since `260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket` the chat stream is a `kind:"chat"` subscription on the shared state socket (NOT an `EventSource`)** ‚Äî the owner hook is `use-chat-subscription.ts` (successor to the deleted `use-chat-stream.ts`), and the connection dot below derives from socket-connected AND chat-acked, not `EventSource` health.

**The `chatProvider` gate.** `WindowInfo` gained `chatProvider?: string` + `chatSessionRef?: string` (`types.ts`) ‚Äî the window-level `@rk_chat` rollup the backend already emitted (typed, not newly parsed). **A non-empty `chatProvider` is the SOLE availability gate** for the chat lens (`hasChat(win)` in `window-view.ts`) ‚Äî mirroring the backend's own `resolveWindowChat` gating ‚Äî so it transitively gates every chat affordance: the ViewSwitcher chat segment, the `View: Chat` palette action, the `` Ctrl+` `` shortcut (enabled iff `currentViews.includes("chat")`), the `<ChatView>` renderer, and the deep-link append. (The heading is NOT among them ‚Äî since `260714-uco1` it is a static `Window:` in every lens, ¬ß Heading is a static `Window:`.) There is NO separate `chatAvailable` variable anymore ‚Äî `resolveView`/`availableViews` fold the gate in.

### View state = the unified lens machinery (NOT a chat-specific mechanism)

The interim chat-only mechanism was **retired** and folded into the lens machinery:
- `lib/chat-view-resolve.ts` (`resolveChatView`, the chat-only `validateTerminalSearch`) ‚Äî **DELETED**. Resolution is `resolveView` (URL‚ÜílocalStorage‚Üídefault); `router.tsx`'s single `validateTerminalSearch` accepts `web`|`chat` (¬ß Window Views ‚Üí `?view=`).
- `hooks/use-chat-view-pref.ts` (the `runkit:chat-view:` key-presence pref + `readChatViewPrefKey`) ‚Äî **DELETED**. Persistence is the value-bearing `runkit-window-view:` key (which now also stores `"chat"`); no migration.
- `SegmentedViewToggle` in `top-bar.tsx` + its `view`/`chatAvailable`/`onSetView` slot fields + `onSetView` toggle body ‚Äî **DELETED**. The chip is the generic `ViewSwitcher` (`[tty|chat]` segments for a chat-only-capable window); flipping is `switchView("chat")`/`switchView("tty")`.
- `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"` is the render + stream gate (`resolveView` already gated on `chatProvider`).

### Center heading `Window: <window>` (static in the chat lens too)

The `chat` lens does NOT change the heading prefix ‚Äî since `260714-uco1` the top-bar heading is a static `Window: <window>` in every lens (¬ß Heading is a static `Window:`; ¬ß Window Heading for the boot-sweep/rename mechanics). The `<ChatView>` renderer preserves the inline-rename affordance (the heading IS the rename surface, especially on mobile) ‚Äî the same parametrized `WindowHeading`, no fork.

### Renderer swap + chat stream (`app.tsx`)

In the `windowParam` render arm, `chatViewActive` selects `<ChatView>` AHEAD of the web-vs-terminal branch (`chatViewActive ? <ChatView> : resolvedView === "web" && rkUrl ? <IframeWindow> : <TerminalClient>`). `AppShell` owns the single owner-hook call ‚Äî **`useChatSubscription(server, windowId)` since `260717-vhvz`** (was `useChatStream`; a call-site-only swap, `<ChatView>` unchanged), opened only when `chatViewActive` (else passed empty strings so the hook idles) ‚Äî and passes `{events, pending, connected, error}` into `ChatView`. ONE chat subscription on the shared state socket feeds both the renderer and the connection dot (below). The chat pane joins the switch-transition **ungated capture** through the unified `ungatedIds` classification (any non-`tty` resolved view; ¬ß Window Views ‚Üí Window-switch transition classification) ‚Äî `<ChatView>` has NO xterm first-write seam, so a first-write gate would never release.

### Connection dot = chat stream health in chat mode (R9)

"Dot-everywhere = per-page live-data health" (¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí connection dot). In chat view, the `isConnected` `AppShell` registers into `TopBarSlot` reflects the **chat subscription's** health instead of the per-server sessions slice: `dotConnected = chatViewActive ? chatStream.connected : isConnected`. **Since `260717-vhvz` `chatStream.connected` = (state socket connected) AND (this window's `kind:"chat"` subscription acked)**, keeping the established 3s disconnect debounce (from `use-chat-subscription`, was the `EventSource`-health form in `use-chat-stream`). In terminal/web view the value is unchanged.

### WaitingBadge click + `Agent: Next waiting` deep-link into `?view=chat`

`WaitingBadge` (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) gained an **optional** `onClick` prop: when passed, the badge renders as a `<button>` (rk-glint hover, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't bubble to the parent row) that navigates to the next waiting window in its scope; when absent, it keeps today's **display-only** `<span>` (so the board-header / Host-page-tile / server-panel mount sites, which pass no onClick, are unchanged). It is currently wired ONLY at the **sidebar session row** (`session-row.tsx` ‚Üí `sidebar/index.tsx` ‚Üí `AppShell`'s `handleWaitingBadgeClick`) ‚Äî the one surface with a navigable per-session scope.

`handleWaitingBadgeClick(srv, sess)` (`app.tsx`) builds the clicked session's ordered waiting windows and calls **`nextWaitingTarget(ordered, server, windowParam)`** (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts` ‚Äî REUSED, not re-implemented; the R12/A-024 review-rework fix: the first cut picked the session's FIRST waiting window via `windows.find(isWaiting)`, so clicking the badge while already ON its first waiting window was a no-op instead of advancing to the next). It appends `?view=chat` via the pure `chatSearchForTarget(hasChat)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested) ‚Äî `{ view: "chat" }` iff the target window has a `chatProvider`, else empty search (the target resolves its own pref). This is the ONE intentional `?view=` carry across a window switch (¬ß Window Views ‚Üí `?view` drops). The existing `Agent: Next waiting` palette action gets the **same** `chatSearchForTarget` append rule for any target it navigates to.

### Connection dot = chat stream health in chat mode (R9)

"Dot-everywhere = per-page live-data health" (¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí connection dot). In chat view, the `isConnected` `AppShell` registers into `TopBarSlot` reflects the **chat subscription's** health instead of the per-server sessions slice: `dotConnected = chatViewActive ? chatStream.connected : isConnected`. **Since `260717-vhvz` `chatStream.connected` = (state socket connected) AND (this window's `kind:"chat"` subscription acked)**, keeping the established 3s disconnect debounce (from `use-chat-subscription`, was the `EventSource`-health form in `use-chat-stream`). In terminal/server view the value is unchanged.

### WaitingBadge click + `Agent: Next waiting` deep-link into `?view=chat`

`WaitingBadge` (`components/waiting-badge.tsx`) gained an **optional** `onClick` prop: when passed, the badge renders as a `<button>` (rk-glint hover, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't bubble to the parent row) that navigates to the next waiting window in its scope; when absent, it keeps today's **display-only** `<span>` (so the board-header / Host-page-tile / server-panel mount sites, which pass no onClick, are unchanged). It is currently wired ONLY at the **sidebar session row** (`session-row.tsx` ‚Üí `sidebar/index.tsx` ‚Üí `AppShell`'s `handleWaitingBadgeClick`) ‚Äî the one surface with a navigable per-session scope.

`handleWaitingBadgeClick(srv, sess)` (`app.tsx`) builds the clicked session's ordered waiting windows and calls **`nextWaitingTarget(ordered, server, windowParam)`** (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts` ‚Äî REUSED, not re-implemented; the R12/A-024 review-rework fix: the first cut picked the session's FIRST waiting window via `windows.find(isWaiting)`, so clicking the badge while already ON its first waiting window was a no-op instead of advancing to the next). It appends `?view=chat` via the pure `chatSearchForTarget(hasChat)` helper (`lib/palette-agent-nav.ts`, unit-tested) ‚Äî `{ view: "chat" }` iff the target window has a `chatProvider`, else empty search (the target resolves its own pref). The existing `Agent: Next waiting` palette action gets the **same** `chatSearchForTarget` append rule for any target it navigates to.

## Boards View

`/board/$name` renders a horizontal pane dashboard for windows pinned to a named board (see `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß Pin Sessions / ¬ß `@rk_board` for storage and `architecture.md` ¬ß Boards Feature for the route placement rationale). The board view does NOT mount AppShell, but it shares the same root-mounted multi-server `SessionProvider`, the same unified `<Sidebar>`, and as of `260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout` the same `<Shell>` grid wrapper ‚Äî the sidebar's per-server session groups stay populated across the route switch because the provider lives at the root.

### SESSIONS + BOARDS dual presence (a pinned window is LINKED, not moved)

Since `260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning`, pinning a window **links** it (`tmux link-window`) into a single-window pin-session (`_rk-pin-<id>`) while it stays a member of its home session, so a pinned window appears on **both** surfaces at once ‚Äî in the SESSIONS sidebar at its real home index AND as a pane on the board. This is honestly tmux-derived (Constitution II): the SSE session snapshot still lists the window under its home session (only the `_rk-pin-*` session name is filtered at the `parseSessions` chokepoint, not the window), so the sidebar shows it with no frontend synthesis. Two ambient dual-residence affordances make the second home legible: the board pane header shows a `{session} ‚Ä∫ {window}` home crumb (¬ß Board Tile Header) and the sidebar pin indicator surfaces a "Go to {board}" navigation row (¬ß Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows). The pin-icon filled state and the active-board accent (below) remain the board-aware affordances on a SESSIONS row ‚Äî now on a row that stays visible while pinned. (Legacy move-based pins ‚Äî created before `260718-co9z` ‚Äî still don't appear in SESSIONS while pinned: the window really isn't in its home session under the old model; they convert to dual presence on unpin + re-pin.)

### BoardPage Layout (`app/frontend/src/components/board/board-page.tsx`)

BoardPage uses the shared `<Shell>` wrapper. Since `260707-4vq2-lift-topbar-root-layout` the Shell grid carries NO `topbar` row ‚Äî the desktop grid is `grid-template-areas: "sidebar content" / "sidebar bottombar"` (rows `1fr auto`; collapses to single-column `"content" "bottombar"` on `< 640px` with the sidebar overlay); the TopBar is mounted once at the persistent root layout above the Shell, not as a grid child (see ¬ß Shell Grid Layout / ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí persistent root mount). Children are placed into named grid areas:

- **Sidebar** (`gridArea: "sidebar"`) ‚Äî the unified `<Sidebar currentServer={null}>` (same component as AppShell). No per-server group is marked current on board routes. Per-server session groups + Boards section + ServerPanel + bottom panels render as on AppShell. Mobile (`< 640px`) renders the sidebar as a Shell-level overlay whose grid child spans `gridRow: "1 / 3"` (content + bottombar, re-indexed by `4vq2` from `"2 / 4"` now that the topbar row is gone) ‚Äî same overlay implementation as AppShell
- **TopBar** ‚Äî NO LONGER a Shell grid child (`4vq2`). `BoardPageContent` deleted its `<header style={{ gridArea: "topbar" }}><TopBar mode="board" ‚Ä¶/></header>` block + `TopBar` import (keeping `HELP_URL` for its palette action) and instead registers the board extras (`boardName: name`, `paneCount: entries.length`, `serverCount`, `waitingPaneCount`, `boards`, `focusedPane` (the focused-tile split target), `onRequestKill: requestKillFocused` (since `260718-co9z` the top-bar ‚úï opens the kill confirm dialog, replacing the direct-kill `onPaneClosed` seam ‚Äî which is REMOVED; post-kill refetch rides `executeKillWindow`'s own `onSettled`, not a top-bar callback), `isConnected: boardConnected`, `sidebarOpen`, `onToggleSidebar`) into the slot context via `useRegisterTopBarSlot`. The persistent `RootTopBar` derives `mode="board"` + `boardName` from the route and renders the board bar fed by those extras (breadcrumb/heading/right-cluster content unchanged from before the move ‚Äî see ¬ß Board and ¬ß center cell for the current board rendering, which supersedes the retired `Board ‚ñ∏ {name} ‚ñæ` breadcrumb and the board-hides-dot behavior)
- **Content** (`gridArea: "content"`) ‚Äî the existing `DesktopRow` (desktop) / `MobileCarousel` (mobile) horizontally-scrollable container of pane "cards" sorted by `orderKey`. Each card is a `BoardPane` with a `BoardHeader` (the `{session} ‚Ä∫ {window}` home crumb ‚Äî see ¬ß Board Tile Header ‚Äî + the pin-glyph unpin button) and an embedded `TerminalClient` streamed over the shared `/ws/terminals` mux keyed by `windowId` (one stream per pane; the per-pane `/relay/{windowId}` socket was retired by `260717-803u`) ‚Äî **the same `TerminalClient`/relay path as the normal terminal route**. The relay attaches the window's `_rk-pin-*` pin-session server-side (the pin-session-first attach preference, `260718-co9z`), so `BoardPane`/`board-page.tsx` need NO structural change for the attach ‚Äî `BoardEntry` shape unchanged. The horizontal-scroll viewport begins at the `content` grid area's left edge ‚Äî flush with `sidebar.right` (or page.left when `sidebarOpen === false`); no left gutter for board-level chrome
- **BottomBar** (`gridArea: "bottombar"`) ‚Äî the shared `<BottomBar>` (NEW on this route ‚Äî board route had no BottomBar pre-rotation). Byte-identical to AppShell's invocation: same three callbacks (`onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`). `onOpenCompose` is `toggleComposeStrip` (the `>_` chip toggles the docked compose strip preference ‚Äî ¬ß Docked Compose Strip); `onFocusTerminal` invokes a ref-tracked `focusFocusedPaneRef.current()` that re-focuses the currently-focused board pane via its `paneRefs[focusedIndex].focus()`; `onScrollLockChange` plumbs through `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel` ‚Üí `BoardPane` ‚Üí `TerminalClient.scrollLocked`. Input target is the focused pane's wsRef (read from `FocusedTerminalContext.focused?.wsRef`). The docked compose strip renders in this footer above `<BottomBar>` when the preference is on (`{composeStripEnabled && <ComposeStrip />}`)
- **Own `<CommandPalette>` mount** ‚Äî BoardPage retains its own palette mount because board-route-only entries (Switch / Leave Board View / Cycle Pane Focus ‚Üí/‚Üê) need a registration site, and the AppShell palette doesn't mount on `/board/<name>`. The mount is preserved through the rotation

Empty / non-existent board (`name` exists in URL but `getBoard` returns `[]`): shows "No panes pinned to this board yet. Pin a window from the sidebar." with a back link.

### Pane Cards (Desktop)

- **Default width 480px**, drag-resizable between 280px (min) and viewport-minus-sidebar (max). Resize handle hidden on coarse-pointer devices
- **Persisted per-board** in `localStorage["runkit:board-widths:<name>"]` as `Record<windowId, number>`. `usePaneWidths(boardName)` encapsulates read/write/clamp; missing entries fall back to 480px; malformed JSON is ignored silently. Pane widths are intentionally browser-local view state ‚Äî they do NOT cross devices (pin state in tmux does)
- **Click-to-focus** transfers focus to the pane's xterm via a `useImperativeHandle`-exposed `focus()` method on `BoardPaneHandle`. **Hover-to-focus is OFF in v1** (no hover handler attached)
- **Visual focus indicator** ‚Äî focused pane has a distinct border/glow; unfocused panes are de-emphasized
- **Keyboard pane cycling** ‚Äî `Cmd+]` / `Ctrl+]` next (wraps), `Cmd+[` / `Ctrl+[` previous (wraps). Bound via a `useEffect` keydown listener on the BoardPage component
- **Autofit override** ‚Äî when the per-board autofit toggle is ON, desktop panes ignore the stored pixel width and become equal-share flex items, and the resize handle is hidden. See ¬ß Board Autofit Toggle. Autofit never mutates `runkit:board-widths:<name>`, so toggling off restores the exact hand-tuned widths above.

### Board Kill Confirm Dialog + Verb Discipline (`260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning`)

The board surfaces two distinct destructive-vs-safe actions with disciplined verbs ‚Äî **Unpin** (safe, reversible ‚Äî removes the window from the board, it stays in its `{session}`) and **Kill** (destructive ‚Äî closes the window everywhere, including its home session). The "close"/"close pane" verb is retired on board surfaces (tooltips, aria labels, palette entries); sidebar and terminal-mode ‚úï vocabulary/semantics are out of scope (unchanged blast radius there).

**Kill is confirm-gated** (`board-page.tsx`). The board top-bar ‚úï (via the slot's `onRequestKill`) and the `board-kill-focused` palette entry both call `requestKillFocused`, which captures the focused entry as `killTarget` (`{server, windowId, windowName, home}`) and opens a `Dialog` ‚Äî they never fire immediately:

> **Kill `{window}`?** This closes it everywhere ‚Äî including session `{home}`.
> `[Unpin instead]` `[Kill]` `[Cancel]`

- **`{home}` derivation + fallback**: `home` is resolved at open time from the `homeSessionByKey` snapshot join (¬ß Board Tile Header ‚Äî the same `ctx.sessionsByServer` join the header crumb uses), read through a ref (`homeSessionByKeyRef`) so `requestKillFocused` (declared above the memo) sees the current map. When `home` is not derivable (legacy pin / home died ‚Äî window absent from the snapshot) the copy falls back to window-only ("This closes the window everywhere.").
- **Default focus on the SAFE action**: `[Unpin instead]` is the FIRST focusable element, so `Dialog` auto-focuses it; the dialog is fully keyboard-operable (Escape/Tab/backdrop via the shared `Dialog`).
- **Confirmed Kill is a WINDOW-kill**: `[Kill]` calls `executeKillWindow` (`useOptimisticAction` over `killWindow` ‚Üí `POST /api/windows/{id}/kill`), destroying the window entity everywhere (home + pin links) in one call ‚Äî NOT the prior board `close-pane`. Its `onSettled` schedules the board refetch (the self-heal for the no-`board-changed`-on-kill gap ‚Äî replacing the removed `onPaneClosed` seam).
- **`[Unpin instead]`** invokes the shared unpin path (`unpin(server, windowId, board)`), the same reversible action the tile-header pin-glyph and `Board: Unpin Focused Pane` use ‚Äî no confirmation.

The tile-header pin-glyph unpin stays **unconfirmed** (unpin is cheap to reverse). See ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí Close pane button for the top-bar ‚úï's `onRequestKill` routing and ¬ß Boards Command Palette for the `board-kill-focused` entry.

### Board Autofit Toggle (`260708-738w-board-autofit`)

A per-board **desktop** toggle that stretches panes to fill the row instead of using explicit pixel widths ‚Äî the minimal-surface answer (Constitution IV: one button + one palette action, no settings page) to boards chronically under-using screen width with 2‚Äì3 panes on a wide monitor. Desktop `DesktopRow` only ‚Äî the `MobileCarousel` is already one full-width `w-full` pane, so autofit is a **no-op on mobile** (no branch there).

**Persistence ‚Äî `useBoardAutofit` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-autofit.ts`)**, mirroring the guard discipline of `use-pane-widths.ts`:

- Key `runkit:board-autofit:<board>` (exported prefix `BOARD_AUTOFIT_LOCALSTORAGE_PREFIX = "runkit:board-autofit:"`), **per-board** ‚Äî enabling autofit on board A does not affect board B, and switching `board` reloads state via a `useEffect`-on-`board` (the same reload seam `usePaneWidths` uses).
- **"on" sentinel with key removal on off**: the literal string `"on"` is the ONLY value that reads as on; anything else (absent, malformed) reads off (window-undefined bail + `try/catch`, malformed-tolerant like `use-pane-widths.ts`). Turning autofit OFF **removes the key** (`localStorage.removeItem`) rather than storing `"off"` ‚Äî the read is `getItem(...) === "on"`, so there is no `"off"` state to persist.
- **Default off** (no key stored ‚Üí current per-pane-width behavior); the key is untouched until the setter runs.
- API: `useBoardAutofit(board) ‚Üí { autofit, toggleAutofit }`; `toggleAutofit` flips + persists and round-trips across a fresh hook instance / reload.

**Layout branch ‚Äî `DesktopRow` / `BoardPane` (`board-page.tsx`, `board-pane.tsx`)**. `BoardPage` owns `useBoardAutofit(name)` and passes `autofit` down to `DesktopRow`, which forwards it to each `BoardPane` and passes `showResizeHandle={!autofit}`:

- **Autofit ON**: `DesktopRow` passes **no pixel `width`** (`width={autofit ? undefined : getWidth(entry.windowId)}`); each pane root becomes `flex: 1 1 0` with `min-width: max(BOARD_PANE_MIN_WIDTH, calc(25% - 3px))` (import the `BOARD_PANE_MIN_WIDTH` constant from `use-pane-widths` ‚Äî 280px ‚Äî never hard-code) inside the existing `overflow-x-auto flex gap-1 p-1` row. Classes drop `w-full`/`shrink-0`; the flex+min-width in `style` drives sizing. Result: ‚â§4 panes stretch to share the row equally with no horizontal scrollbar; >4 panes floor at the 25% arm and the row scrolls exactly as today. Pure CSS ‚Äî **no ResizeObserver on the row** ‚Äî so window resize reflows live for free.
  - **Gap-adjusted floor** (DD): the literal `max(280px, 25%)` from the backlog would force `4√ó25% + 3√ó4px (gap-1) > 100%` ‚Üí a 12px scrollbar at exactly 4 panes, contradicting the "max 4 visible" intent. `calc(25% - 3px)` (3 gaps √ó 4px √∑ 4 panes) makes exactly 4 panes fit flush.
  - **Verified** the percentage `min-width` resolves against the flex container's content box (the scrollport), NOT the scrolled content width ‚Äî the containing block of a flex item is its flex container's content box, and `overflow-x: auto` does not change that. The backlog's JS-measurement fallback is therefore unneeded; the e2e asserts the resulting widths as a safety net.
- **Autofit OFF**: **exactly** the prior per-pane-width behavior ‚Äî explicit pixel widths from `usePaneWidths.getWidth`, `shrink-0`, resize handles present.
- **Non-destructive round-trip**: the stored `runkit:board-widths:<board>` map is **never touched** by autofit (the `width` prop is merely not passed while on; `getWidth`/`setWidth` are not called through the autofit branch), so toggling OFF restores the exact hand-tuned layout.
- **`autofit?: boolean` prop on `BoardPane`** (not a wrapper div ‚Äî DD): the pane root is the row's direct flex child AND the `rootRef` IntersectionObserver target (¬ß Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension), so a wrapper would break both contracts; the flag follows the existing optional-`width` pattern.

**Controls (Constitution V parity)** ‚Äî a top-bar button and a palette action flip the same state:

- **Top-bar `BoardAutofitToggle`** (`top-bar.tsx`): a **board-only** L2-cluster toggle **between `Aa` (`TerminalFontControl`) and `‚úï` (`ClosePaneButton`)**, gated `mode === "board" && onToggleAutofit` (unlike Aa/‚úï which are terminal+board). Mirrors the `FixedWidthToggle` vocabulary ‚Äî `aria-pressed={autofit}`, `rk-glint` CRT-glint hover, `coarse:` touch sizing. See ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí Right cluster (L2).
- **Palette action** `Board: Toggle Autofit (on/off)` (`id: "board-toggle-autofit"`, `boardRouteActions` in `board-page.tsx`, label reflects state) ‚Üí `toggleAutofit`.
- **State plumbing** ‚Äî `BoardPage` publishes `autofit` + `onToggleAutofit: toggleAutofit` into the top-bar slot context (`useRegisterTopBarSlot`, the same channel carrying the board `focusedPane` + `onRequestKill` kill-dialog seam ‚Äî `260718-co9z`, replacing the removed `onPaneClosed`); `top-bar-slot-context.tsx` grows two optional board-mode fields `autofit?` / `onToggleAutofit?`; `RootTopBar` (`app.tsx`) maps `slot?.autofit`/`slot?.onToggleAutofit` ‚Üí `TopBar` props (tolerant-empty ‚Äî absent ‚áí no toggle rendered).

**Alignments (no code change)**:

- **`MAX_LIVE_RELAY_PANES = 4`** (¬ß Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension) equals the 4-visible max the 25% floor produces, so on plaintext origins autofit never forces a visible-but-paused pane; the focused pane is exempt from the cap anyway (`selectLivePanes`). >4 panes still overflow horizontally and off-screen panes still suspend.
- **xterm refit rides the existing `terminal-client.tsx` ResizeObserver** (no autofit-specific wiring): a container `ResizeObserver` rAF-debounces `fitAddon.fit()` + a paired `{type:"resize",cols,rows}` WS message; flex reflow (window resize, pin/unpin, toggle flips) changes each visible pane's size and fires that observer per pane.

**Tests**: unit `use-board-autofit.test.ts` (default-off, "on"-sentinel round-trip + key removal, per-board isolation, board-switch reload, malformed tolerance); Playwright `tests/e2e/board-autofit.spec.ts` + companion `.spec.md` (equal-fill/no-scroll at 2‚Äì3 panes, ~25%-floor/scroll at 5+, per-board persistence across reload, handles-hidden-while-on, top-bar button + palette action parity) ‚Äî run via `just test-e2e`/`just pw` only.

### Board Pane Reorder (`260708-rmiq-board-pane-reorder`)

Desktop board panes are drag-reorderable, with full Cmd+K keyboard parity (Constitution V). Panes render in server `orderKey` order (`GET /api/boards/{name}`); reorder writes a new fractional-index key via the previously-dark `POST /api/boards/{name}/reorder` (see `architecture.md` ¬ß Boards Feature ‚Äî the whole backend half was shipped and unwired before this change). **`MobileCarousel` is untouched** ‚Äî swipe is navigation there, not reorder.

**Adapts the ¬ß Server-tile drag reorder pattern** (`use-server-reorder.ts`) into a sibling hook `useBoardPaneReorder(entries, board, reorder)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-pane-reorder.ts`), inheriting its two hard-won fixes (derive-over-store override, self-target dragover acceptance). Key differences from server/session reorder:

- **Custom MIME `application/x-board-pane-reorder`** (`BOARD_PANE_REORDER_MIME`) ‚Äî must not collide with `application/x-server-reorder`, `application/x-session-reorder`, or the window-move default-JSON payload. Guarded FIRST, before any acceptance (the shared guard-order invariant ‚Äî see ¬ß Server-tile drag reorder).
- **Composite `server:windowId` key** ‚Äî a board spans servers, so `windowId` alone is ambiguous; the override array, the drag payload, and the DnD/palette bookkeeping all key by `server:windowId` (matching the `key={`${entry.server}:${entry.windowId}`}` in `DesktopRow`).
- **Split handle/drop props** ‚Äî `getHandleProps(server, windowId)` returns `{ handle, drop }` separately: `handle` (`draggable` + `onDragStart`/`onDragEnd`) goes on the pane HEADER only (`BoardHeader`) so a live xterm terminal never hijacks the drag or becomes the drag image; `drop` (`onDragOver`/`onDrop`) goes on the pane ROOT (`BoardPane`) so the preview updates and a release commits anywhere over a pane, not only the ~24px header strip. The header unpin button (a pin-glyph since `260715-6jwn`, ¬ß Board Tile Header) opts out (`draggable={false}` + `stopPropagation`) and the resize handle lives on the pane root outside the header, so neither is shadowed by the drag handle (no regression to unpin or drag-resize).
- **ONE `reorderPin` POST per move, no debounce** ‚Äî fractional indexing means one authoritative call per completed move (`before`/`after` = the moved pane's new neighbours' windowIds, `null` at edges), so the drop is the single commit point. This is the deliberate contrast with server/session reorder's 250ms debounced full-order writes + drop-flush (there is no full-order sweep to coalesce). The `board-changed` SSE echo (refetched by `useBoardEntries`, 50ms debounce) reconciles the override away.
- **Committed-drop flag drives cancel-revert** ‚Äî `committedRef` is set true only when `onDrop` fires the POST. `onDragEnd` clears the override when uncommitted (Escape / release outside any pane = revert to authoritative order, no phantom unpersisted order) but keeps it when committed (no snap-back ‚Äî the SSE echo reconciles it). This is the one place the board hook diverges from the no-drag-end-clear discipline of server/session reorder: with drop as the single commit point, native HTML5 cancel semantics = revert, so the no-snap-back rule applies only to committed drops and SSE reconciles.
- **Rollback on POST rejection** ‚Äî `usePinActions().reorder` now shows its toast AND **rethrows** (pin/unpin still swallow ‚Äî they have no client-side optimistic order to revert); the DnD hook `.catch()`es to clear the override and the palette move `.catch()`es to avoid an unhandled rejection, so a rejected reorder reverts the display to the authoritative order instead of leaving the failed order rendered.
- **`onDrop` derives neighbours inline from the final override order** (not from `computeReorderNeighbors` over the authoritative list) ‚Äî the override is what the user sees and is robust to mid-drag entry churn where index arithmetic over the authoritative array is not. The pure `computeReorderNeighbors`/`computeMoveNeighbors` helpers (`src/lib/board-reorder.ts`, mirroring `palette-move.ts`) are the PALETTE path's arithmetic (`computeReorderNeighbors` has one live caller, `computeMoveNeighbors`, so it is kept with a doc comment, not dead).

**Palette parity** ‚Äî `Board: Move Focused Pane Left/Right` (`boardRouteActions`, boundary-hidden per ¬ß Boards Command Palette) act on the focused pane, compute neighbours via `computeMoveNeighbors`, and fire the same single-POST path as DnD. No wraparound (hidden, not disabled, at the edges).

**Focus tracked by `server:windowId` key + a user-intent gate** (`board-page.tsx`, the load-bearing seam):

- Focus is tracked by the focused pane's **`server:windowId` key** (`focusedKeyRef`), NOT by positional index. A single focus-authority effect reconciles `focusedIndex` from `focusedKeyRef` on every order change (via `focusedIndexForKey`) so the focused pane's identity survives reorders ‚Äî own palette move, own drop echo, AND a reorder arriving from another client (key-follow, not index-follow). An index bump alone was insufficient: with `paneRefs` keyed to the authoritative order, `setFocusedIndex(i¬±1)` before the SSE echo routed the imperative xterm `.focus()` into the DISPLACED NEIGHBOUR's terminal (wrong-terminal keystrokes) ‚Äî so the palette `moveFocusedPane` deliberately does NOT bump `focusedIndex`; the reconcile does it once the new order settles.
- **Imperative `.focus()` fires only on user intent** ‚Äî this is the board-route form of the "SSE must not steal focus" invariant (the sidebar tree's `focusMovedRef` gate is the sibling ‚Äî see ¬ß Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA). `useBoardEntries` refetches a fresh `entries` array on EVERY `board-changed` SSE from ANY board on ANY server, so an unconditional `.focus()` on each identity change would yank DOM focus into the xterm while the user types in the docked compose strip / pin-popover / palette / dialogs, and would auto-focus pane 0 on board load. The fix gates `paneRefs.current[focusedIndex]?.focus()` behind `shouldFocusPane(prevFocusedIndexRef.current, focusedIndex)` ‚Äî it fires only when `focusedIndex` actually changed from the last focused index. The silent key‚Üíindex reconcile (`setFocusedIndex(j)` early-return) is unchanged, so an own move still lands imperative focus in the moved pane post-echo (the reconcile bumps the index ‚Üí the re-entered settled pass sees the change ‚Üí focuses). Board load does not auto-focus pane 0 (index 0 unchanged from its seed). `shouldFocusPane`/`focusedIndexForKey` are unit-tested in `board-reorder.test.ts`.
- **Known residual (should-fix, not shipped)**: the index-change gate cannot distinguish an own-move follow from a REMOTE-driven index reconcile. A `board-changed` from another client/tab that shifts the focused pane's index on THIS board (a remote reorder crossing the focused position, or a remote unpin of an earlier pane) reconciles `focusedIndex` and the settled pass then fires `.focus()`, yanking DOM focus into the xterm. The dominant steal vectors (any-board refetch, same-order refetch, board load) are closed and unit-tested, and amended R6 itself endorses the index-change gate, so this narrow multi-client subcase was graded should-fix and deferred. A true intent flag (mirror the sidebar's `focusMovedRef` ‚Äî set on `moveFocusedPane`/click/cycle/own drop; the reconcile branch would advance `prevFocusedIndexRef` when no intent is pending) would close it.

**e2e** (`app/frontend/tests/e2e/board-reorder.spec.ts` + `.spec.md`) mirrors `server-reorder.spec.ts`: it exercises the reorder ENDPOINT + `board-changed` SSE echo + a reload-free GET-order assertion against the live backend, NOT a native HTML5 drag simulation ‚Äî synthetic Playwright DnD is unreliable (the session-reorder drag spec is `test.fixme`, never passed) and `page.reload()` does not commit under the SPA's long-lived SSE. The drag handlers, MIME guard, reconcile, cancel-revert, failure-rollback, and neighbour arithmetic are Vitest-covered (`use-board-pane-reorder.test.ts`, `board-reorder.test.ts`). Backend cross-server neighbour resolution is Go-tested (`router_test.go` `TestLookupNeighbourKeys_*`).

### Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension

On plaintext origins, `DesktopRow` suspends off-screen panes' terminal streams so the live count stays bounded ‚Äî the desktop analogue of the mobile carousel's `paused={idx !== carouselIndex}` pause. Added by `260531-rus8-bound-desktop-relay-websockets`. The mechanism mirrors the proven mobile pause: a paused pane unmounts its `TerminalClient`; scroll-back re-mounts and re-opens, replaying terminal content. **Since `260717-803u-relay-mux` (seam 3 of the mux port) suspension is no longer a closed WebSocket per pane** ‚Äî all panes share the ONE `/ws/terminals` socket, so a paused pane's `TerminalClient` unmount sends a `close` **control op** for its stream (not a socket teardown) and a resumed pane sends a fresh `open` op. This **removes the board pane-resize suspension-drop reconnect cost** (memory `board-pane-resize-suspension-drop` ‚Äî the per-pane socket setup/teardown churn is gone) and means the original HTTP/1.1-pool motivation is now mostly moot (the mux + state socket already hold the tab to a fixed 2 WebSockets); the visibility-pause + cap still bound how many PTY attaches (tmux clients) are live at once, which stays worthwhile. `board-page.tsx` was unchanged by `803u` ‚Äî the unmount-on-pause seam is transport-agnostic.

- **Plaintext-only gate** ‚Äî the entire feature is gated on `plaintext = window.location.protocol === "http:"` (`board-page.tsx`). On HTTPS/h2 (production via Tailscale) every desktop pane stays live (`paused={false}`), no `IntersectionObserver` is created, and no cap applies ‚Äî behavior is byte-identical to before this change. The ~6-connection ceiling is a plaintext HTTP/1.1 artifact (h2 multiplexes; the relay WS limit is ~255), so the fix activates only where the problem exists (E2E/dev `http://localhost:3020`, raw-port `http://...` access)
- **Visibility via `IntersectionObserver`** ‚Äî on plaintext origins, a single observer rooted on the `rowRef` horizontal-scroll container drives each pane's `paused` prop from viewport intersection. Panes are keyed to indices via a `data-paneIndex` attribute on each pane's root element (forwarded through a `rootRef` callback prop on `BoardPane`, kept distinct from the `paneRefs` imperative `BoardPaneHandle` so neither contract leaks into the other). The observer effect mirrors the existing wheel-handler effect's setup/cleanup discipline (`observer.disconnect()` on unmount) and re-subscribes when the pane count changes
- **Pre-warm margin** ‚Äî the observer uses `RELAY_PREWARM_ROOT_MARGIN` = `` `0px ${BOARD_PANE_DEFAULT_WIDTH}px` `` (one pane-width of horizontal `rootMargin`, vertical 0) so a pane is kept live slightly before it enters and after it leaves the strict viewport, preventing pause/resume thrash (and the `[reconnecting...]` flicker) on a quick scroll-past. No debounce in v1 ‚Äî add one only if thrash is observed during Playwright tuning
- **Live-pane cap** ‚Äî simultaneously-live (unpaused) relay panes are capped at `MAX_LIVE_RELAY_PANES = 4` (named constant, not a magic number), backstopping the observer for the wide-monitor case where more panes fit on-screen than the budget allows (`1 SSE + 4 relay + headroom` stays under 6). When visibility alone would leave more than the cap live, the **least-recently-focused** visible panes are paused first. The selection logic is the pure `selectLivePanes` helper in `app/frontend/src/components/board/select-live-panes.ts` (colocated unit tests), consuming the visible-index set, the focused index, the most-recently-focused order, and the cap; `DesktopRow` passes `paused={!livePanes.has(idx)}` (and short-circuits to `paused={false}` when `livePanes === null`, i.e. on secure origins). The MRU order folds the current `focusedIndex` to the front during render (`useMemo` keyed on `focusedIndex`) so cap eviction never sees a stale focus
- **Focused pane always live** ‚Äî `selectLivePanes` adds `focusedIndex` unconditionally before filling the remaining slots, so the focused pane is exempt from both visibility-pause and the cap. This preserves `Cmd+]`/`Cmd+[` cycling (cycling to an off-screen paused pane re-selects it ‚Üí unpauses ‚Üí re-mounts ‚Üí imperative `focus()` via `paneRefs`) and BottomBar targeting of the focused terminal
- **Composes with the sibling change** ‚Äî `260531-m3pl-static-xterm-imports` removes the xterm chunk-fetch pressure from the runtime connection budget while this change bounds the persistent relay streams; together they fit the board route under the 6-connection cap on plaintext origins (the original board-route E2E hang root cause). `MobileCarousel` is untouched ‚Äî it already suspended correctly

### Mobile Single-Pane Carousel

Below the `min-width: 640px` breakpoint (matching the existing project mobile convention), the BoardPage renders a single-pane swipe carousel:

- One pane fills the viewport width
- Touch swipe left/right cycles in `orderKey` order; threshold 40px on `touchstart` ‚Üí `touchend` `clientX` delta
- **Off-screen panes pause** by unmounting their `TerminalClient` so the WebSocket closes; on swipe-in, the pane re-mounts and the terminal reattaches
- A pagination dot strip indicates the current pane index (no wrap on edges in v1)

### Sidebar Boards Section (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/boards-section.tsx`)

Renders **at the very top of the sidebar** ‚Äî the section order is **Boards ‚Üí Servers ‚Üí Sessions** (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout` reordered this from the previous Servers ‚Üí Boards ‚Üí Sessions). Visible on every route that mounts `<Sidebar>` (`/$server/...` and `/board/$name`). The board route reuses the same `BoardsSection` component for board switching; there is no separate BoardPage listing.

- **Always visible**, regardless of `boards.length` or current route
- **Hint mode** ‚Äî when `boards.length === 0`, the body shows a one-line hint `Pin a window to start a board` (`text-xs text-text-secondary`) verbatim from 4vuv's copy. Applies on every route, not only on `/board/<name>` ‚Äî placing Boards at the top would cause a layout shift if the section hid/showed dynamically (Servers would jump up, then back down when the first board materializes)
- **First board materializes** ‚Äî hint replaced by a single board row in place; no other section's vertical position shifts
- **Last board removed** ‚Äî section reverts to hint mode; no layout shift to ServerPanel or Sessions

Each row: board name (left, truncate with ellipsis), pin count (right, muted), highlighted background when current route matches `/board/<name>`. Clicking the row navigates to `/board/<name>`. **Drag-reorderable** (`260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`): rows render `orderedBoards` from the shared `useBoardListReorder` hook with `getTileProps(b.name)` spread onto each, and the dragged row dims via `opacity-50` ‚Äî see ¬ß Board-list drag reorder.

**Dynamic default-open + header PinIcon** (`260718-gxrq`, discoverability): the `CollapsiblePanel` uses `defaultOpen={boards.length > 0}` (storageKey `runkit-panel-boards` unchanged) so the panel opens live once the first board exists and a fresh pin surfaces where it landed, while an explicit user toggle always wins ‚Äî this falls out of `useLocalStorageBoolean(storageKey, defaultValue)`, which consults `defaultValue` only when no stored key exists and resyncs its effect on `defaultValue` change (see ¬ß Server Pane ‚Üî Sessions Pane scope coupling for the shared hook). The panel `headerRight` renders the shared outline `PinIcon` (`components/pin-icon.tsx` ‚Äî the same glyph the window-row pin button and board-tile-header unpin use) leading the `{boards.length}` count, visually linking the window-row pin affordance to where pins land; the icon stays present in zero-board hint mode (the count is dropped there, the icon is not). A deliberate NON-rename: BOARDS keeps its name (the "Board" vocabulary is load-bearing ‚Äî `/board/$name`, the `Board:` heading/palette, `/api/boards`); discoverability was raised by default-open + the glyph, not by renaming to "PINNED WINDOWS".

### Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows

`window-row.tsx` gains a pin icon button that follows the existing icon-on-hover pattern in the sidebar:

- **Hover-revealed** (always visible on touch devices via `coarse:opacity-100`)
- **Filled** when the window is pinned to ANY board; **outline** when not pinned (computed via `useWindowPins(server, windowId)` which watches every board). The glyph is the shared thumbtack `PinIcon` (`components/pin-icon.tsx`) ‚Äî the same component the board tile header renders in its `slashed` unpin variant (¬ß Board Tile Header). **Accent-colored** when the row is pinned to the currently-viewed board (`isPinnedToActiveBoard`), monochrome `text-text-secondary` otherwise ‚Äî this glyph carries the active-board cue (there is no left border; ¬ß Row Anatomy, ¬ß Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree)
- **Click opens `PinPopover`** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/pin-popover.tsx`) anchored to the icon: an optional **"Go to {board}" navigation row** at the top (since `260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning`) when the window is pinned, then the list of existing boards (each row pins or unpins on click, ordered last-used-first ‚Äî see below), plus an inline "Pin to new board‚Ä¶" text input with an adjacent **Pin button** ‚Äî the mouse submit path, mirroring Enter exactly (`handleSubmitNew`: non-empty input pins to that name, empty input pins to the ‚Üµ-hinted last-used board; disabled when Enter would be a no-op). Enter validates against the board-name regex and creates the board on first pin. Validation errors surface inline. Outside-click + Escape dismiss. Sizing is sidebar-compact: `min-w-[160px] max-w-[220px]`, `text-xs` rows at `min-h-[24px] coarse:min-h-[36px]` (matching BoardsSection row density)
- **Pinned-row ‚Üí board navigation is a deliberate TWO-STEP** (indicator ‚Üí popover ‚Üí "Go to {board}" row) since `260718-co9z`: now that a pinned window stays visible in the sidebar (dual presence), its pin indicator becomes a path to the owning board ‚Äî but the indicator keeps its existing pin/unpin *management* role, so navigation lives on a dedicated popover row rather than hijacking the indicator's click. A window has exactly one pin-session ‚Üí exactly one board, so the row names that single board. `PinPopover` takes a `pinnedBoard?: string` + `onNavigateToBoard?(board)` ‚Äî `sidebar/index.tsx` derives the reverse `windowId ‚Üí board` lookup by extending `useWindowPins` (the existing per-board pin-map aggregation) and wires `onNavigateToBoard` to navigate to `/board/{board}`. Keyboard/palette-reachable per Constitution V

**Cold-start & last-used friction reduction** (`260718-gxrq`): the popover removes the invent-a-name-then-type friction of a cold start and makes bare Enter meaningful once boards exist.
  - **Cold start (`boards.length === 0`)** ‚Äî the new-board input is pre-filled with the default board name `main` (`DEFAULT_BOARD_NAME`) and its text is selected on autofocus (`inputRef.current.select()`), so a bare **Enter** immediately pins to a new board `main` (the existing `handleSubmitNew` path ‚Äî no new submit logic) while typing any character replaces the selection, preserving the invent-a-name path. `ValidBoardName` accepts `main`. When boards exist the input stays empty (placeholder unchanged).
  - **Existing-board ordering** ‚Äî the board list renders via `orderBoardsLastUsedFirst(boards, readLastPinnedBoard())` (`lib/last-pinned-board.ts`): the last-used board is moved to the front when it is still a live board; remaining boards keep their `boards`-prop order; a stale value (board gone) is ignored. `lastUsed` is read once via `useMemo` when the popover opens (stable for its lifetime).
  - **Empty-input Enter ‚Üí last-used** ‚Äî when boards exist, the input is empty, and a valid last-used board exists (`emptyEnterTarget`), Enter pins to it and closes the popover; otherwise it stays a no-op (current behavior). Unreachable on cold start (input pre-filled). The last-used row (rendered first) carries a small `‚Üµ` hint (`aria-label="press Enter to pin here"`) so Enter's target is visible; an already-pinned board additionally shows a `‚úì`.
  - **Last-used persistence** ‚Äî written on every successful pin from any entry point by `usePinActions.pin` ‚Üí `writeLastPinnedBoard(board)` (see ¬ß Pin last-used preference), NOT by the popover itself.

### Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree

When the current route is `/board/<name>`, the cue for a window pinned to **that specific board** is the **accent-colored pin glyph** ‚Äî NOT a left border (the row carries no accent border since the axis split; see ¬ß Row Anatomy). `WindowRow` renders the persistent filled pin glyph accent-colored when `isPinnedToActiveBoard`, monochrome otherwise. Pins to other boards show a monochrome filled glyph. The pin icon's filled state (pinned to ANY board) is independent of the accent. On non-board routes, no window is pinned-to-active-board, so all pins render monochrome.

### Pin Entry Points

| Entry point | Location | Notes |
|-------------|----------|-------|
| Sidebar pin icon | `WindowRow` (every server's window rows in the unified sidebar ‚Äî server routes and board routes alike) | Hover-revealed; popover with board picker + inline input (cold-start prefill + last-used-first ordering + empty-Enter-to-last-used since `260718-gxrq`) |
| Command palette | `boardActions` block in `app.tsx` (AppShell mount) and BoardPage's own mount | Direct `Pin: Current Window to <board>` per unpinned board + `Pin: Current Window to new board‚Ä¶` (opens the popover) since `260718-gxrq` ‚Äî the keyboard-first pin path (Constitution V). See ¬ß Boards Command Palette |
| Board pane header | `BoardHeader` (only on `/board/<name>`) | Per-pane unpin button (a pin-glyph SVG since `260715-6jwn`, ¬ß Board Tile Header) ‚Äî no confirmation (pin is cheap to restore) |

Right-click context menu was deliberately NOT implemented in v1 ‚Äî there is no existing context-menu pattern in the sidebar to extend, and the three entry points above cover all flows.

### Board Tile Header

`BoardHeader` (`components/board/board-header.tsx`) renders each board tile's header: a **home crumb** + an **unpin button**. Since `260718-co9z-link-based-board-pinning` the crumb is `{session} ‚Ä∫ {window}` ‚Äî the top-bar crumb vocabulary (`‚Ä∫` separator) ‚Äî where `{session}` is the pinned window's HOME session, made legible now that a pinned window stays linked into a visible session (dual presence). `BoardHeader` takes a resolved `homeSession?: string` prop; `board-page.tsx` derives it at render time from the `homeSessionByKey` join (a `useMemo` over `ctx.sessionsByServer` mapping each `server:windowId` ‚Üí its owning `ProjectSession.name`) and threads it through `board-pane.tsx`. When `homeSession` is absent (legacy pin / home died ‚Äî window not in the snapshot) the header **falls back to window-only** (`{windowName} ¬∑ {server}` / window name). The whole header is the drag handle for board pane reorder (`dragHandleProps`, ¬ß Board Pane Reorder); the unpin button opts out (`draggable={false}` + `e.stopPropagation()` on click) so a click there unpins rather than starting a drag, and does not refocus the pane. `aria-label={`Unpin ${windowName || windowId} from board`}`, `title="Unpin from board"`, no confirmation dialog (pin is cheap to restore ‚Äî contrast the confirm-gated top-bar Kill, ¬ß Board Kill Confirm Dialog). Wired from `board-page.tsx`'s `onUnpin` per tile (`POST /api/boards/{name}/unpin`).

**Pin-glyph icon** (`260715-6jwn`, consolidated with the sidebar glyph): the button renders the shared **`PinIcon`** (`components/pin-icon.tsx`) in its **`slashed`** variant ‚Äî the thumbtack outline crossed by a diagonal `line` = "remove the pin" ‚Äî NOT the former text `√ó`. The old ‚úï read as a destructive close/kill, misleading now that the top-bar ‚úï is a (confirm-gated) window-kill (¬ß Close pane button / ¬ß Board Kill Confirm Dialog); the slashed pin truthfully signals the safe, reversible unpin. `PinIcon` is THE single pin shape for every board-pin affordance: the sidebar window-row pin button renders the same component (`filled` = pinned-to-any-board, outline = not pinned), so pin and unpin read as two states of one affordance ‚Äî the original `260715-6jwn` glyph was a map-pin (location teardrop), a different icon category from the sidebar's thumbtack, and was replaced by the shared shape. Hand-rolled inline SVG (16√ó16 viewBox rendered at 12px so strokes pixel-align, `stroke="currentColor"` `strokeWidth={1.5}`, round caps/joins) per the project's no-icon-library pattern (matching top-bar `SplitButton`/`HelpLink`). The `slashed` variant is always unfilled ‚Äî a currentColor slash over a currentColor fill would vanish in the overlap. All non-icon behavior (non-draggable, stopPropagation, aria/title, no-confirm) is unchanged from the ‚úï era.

### Boards Command Palette (`Board:` prefix)

`boardActions: PaletteAction[]` is composed in a dedicated `useMemo` block in `app.tsx`, between `windowActions` and `viewActions`:

```ts
const paletteActions = useMemo(
  () => [...sessionActions, ...windowActions, ...boardActions, ...viewActions, ...terminalFontActions, ...themeActions, ...configActions, ...updateActions, ...serverActions, ...pushActions, ...windowSwitchActions, ...agentActions],
  [...]
);
```

(`pushActions` is the Web Push opt-in block ‚Äî see ¬ß Notifications (Web Push opt-in); `updateActions` is the `run-kit: Update‚Ä¶` block ‚Äî see ¬ß Update Notification, folded in after `configActions` and before `serverActions`, followed by `maintenanceActions` then `versionActions` (`260715-ifco` `run-kit: Version ‚Äî v‚Ä¶` ‚Äî see ¬ß Steady-state version surfaces) still before `serverActions`; `windowSwitchActions`/`agentActions` still compose last.)

| Entry | Visibility | Action |
|-------|------------|--------|
| `Board: Switch to <name>` (one per board, `(current)` on the active one) | Always | Navigate to `/board/<name>` |
| `Pin: Current Window to <board>` (one per board the window is NOT already pinned to, ordered last-used-first) (`260718-gxrq`) | Only when `sessionName && currentWindow && server` | Direct pin via `usePinActions.pin` ‚Äî the keyboard-first pin path (Cmd+K ‚Üí type ‚Üí Enter; ¬ß2c success toast is the feedback). Built by the pure `buildPinActions` (`lib/palette-pin.ts`) ‚Äî see ¬ß Pin palette actions |
| `Pin: Current Window to new board‚Ä¶` (`260718-gxrq`, `id: pin-current-new-board`) | Only when `sessionName && currentWindow && server` | Dispatches `pin-popover:open` to the matching `WindowRow` (free-text entry needs the popover ‚Äî the palette has no value input). **Supersedes** the removed inline `Board: Pin Current Window` (`board-pin-current`) action, absorbing its popover-opening role |
| `Board: Unpin Current Window` | Only when current window is pinned to ‚â•1 board | Unpins from all boards the current window is pinned to (single-action ‚Äî no per-board picker in v1) |
| `Board: Leave Board View` | Only on `/board/<name>` | Navigate to last viewed window route, or `/` if none |
| `Board: Cycle Pane Focus ‚Üí` | Only on `/board/<name>` and ‚â•1 pane | Same as `Cmd+]` |
| `Board: Cycle Pane Focus ‚Üê` | Only on `/board/<name>` and ‚â•1 pane | Same as `Cmd+[` |
| `Board: Unpin Focused Pane` (`260704-9o7k`) | Only on `/board/<name>` and ‚â•1 pane | Unpins the focused entry via the shared `unpinFocused` handler (`onSelect: unpinFocused`) ‚Äî non-destructive, NOT a kill. Since `260715-6jwn` this is keyboard parity for the **tile-header pin-glyph unpin** (the top-bar ‚úï became a kill), not the ‚úï |
