Active tile `scrollIntoView({ block: 'nearest', inline: 'nearest' })` on mount when mobile layout active. `ServerInfo` shape (`{name, sessionCount, rank?}` ‚Äî `rank` added by `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`) flows through from `/api/servers`. **Drag-reorder** (`260705-bpnr`): regular server tiles are draggable via the shared `useServerReorder` hook (see ¬ß Server-tile drag reorder) ‚Äî infra tiles are excluded (not draggable, not drop targets); the dragged tile dims via `opacity-50`. **Infra-server name de-emphasis** (`260705-uh8f-deemphasize-infra-servers`): the tile name span carries `text-text-secondary` (not the usual `text-text-primary`) when `isInfraServer(name)` (from `@/api/client`) ‚Äî greyed, not disabled. Hover/click/active-selection and the kill ‚úï are unchanged, so the infra tile stays fully attachable (useful for reading daemon logs) and never reads as dead/disconnected. See ¬ß Infra-server de-emphasis
- `server-selector.tsx` ‚Äî `ServerSelector` (legacy); owns its own dropdown state (`serverDropdownOpen`, `refreshingServers`, `serverDropdownRef`); pinned-bottom server dropdown with outside-click dismiss. Retained for backwards compat ‚Äî `ServerPanel` is the primary server-switcher in the current UI
- `kill-dialog.tsx` ‚Äî `KillDialog`; stateless; renders the kill confirmation dialog for sessions and windows using `<Dialog>`

Consumers import `@/components/sidebar` as before ‚Äî Vite resolves directory imports to `sidebar/index.tsx` automatically.

### Infra-server de-emphasis

`260705-uh8f-deemphasize-infra-servers` de-emphasizes **infrastructure** tmux servers ‚Äî the `rk-daemon` socket (hosting the run-kit daemon itself, backend `ServerSocket`, `app/backend/internal/daemon/daemon.go`) and any `rk-test-*` socket (the isolated test-socket umbrella, backend `IsTestServerName`, `app/backend/internal/tmux/tmux.go:1342`) ‚Äî WITHOUT hiding them. Hiding was explicitly rejected: the backend deliberately surfaces every server so the operator sees exactly what `rk reaper` would reap (the contract at `tmux.go:1332-1341`). Greying + sorting-last preserves that visibility while making the infra/workspace distinction legible.

**Identification lives in one frontend home** (`app/frontend/src/api/client.ts`, near the `ServerInfo` type): an exported `DAEMON_SERVER = "rk-daemon"` constant, a module-private `TEST_SERVER_PREFIX = "rk-test-"` (the one frontend home of that literal, mirroring the backend `IsTestServerName`), an exported `isInfraServer(name)` (true for the exact daemon socket or any `rk-test-` prefix), and an exported `compareServers(a, b)`. A **backend `isDaemon` flag** on the `/api/servers` payload was rejected ‚Äî it adds API surface for a pure display concern, and the socket name is effectively frozen (renaming it orphans deployed daemons). Consumers import these; magic strings are never re-derived at call sites.

**`compareServers` ordering**: regular servers first (alphabetical), then infra servers (alphabetical within their class). Comparison is plain byte-order lexicographic (`a.name < b.name`), NOT `localeCompare` ‚Äî this mirrors the backend's `sort.Strings` byte order so the regular-server segment renders byte-identical to before this change. `rk-test-*` sockets sort within the infra class.

**Single sort choke point** ‚Äî `app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx` `fetchServers`: the fetched array is sorted once at the sole `setServers` ingestion point (`setServers(Array.isArray(data) ? [...data].sort(compareServersRanked) : [])` since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`, formerly `compareServers` ‚Äî note the `[...data]` copy: the sort is non-mutating, and the fresh reference each fetch matches production behavior, where `listServers` already returns a fresh array). Every consumer of `ctx.servers` inherits the effective ordering from this one place: the Sidebar Server-panel tile grid (`server-panel.tsx`), the Sessions-tree per-server `ServerGroup`s (`sidebar/index.tsx`), the Host-page TMUX SERVERS zone (`host-overview-page.tsx`), and the command-palette `Server: Switch to {name}` entries (`app.tsx`). **No backend sort change** ‚Äî `/api/servers` stays alphabetical (an asserted API contract, `servers_test.go:143`); display order is a frontend concern. Environments with only regular servers see no change; the e2e environment (all `rk-test-*`) sees uniform grey + unchanged intra-class order. A beneficial side effect: `servers[0]` (the Host page's "Open in window" target, `host-overview-page.tsx`) now prefers a real workspace over `rk-daemon` (see ¬ß SERVICES Zone on `/`).

**Rank-aware comparator composition** (`260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`): the choke-point sort key is extended to **(infra-class, rank, name)** via `compareServersRanked(a, b)` (exported from `client.ts` beside `compareServers`), which **wraps** `compareServers` rather than replacing it ‚Äî so the infra-last class pin and the byte-order intra-class ordering (and their tests) are preserved verbatim; rank is a secondary key inserted ONLY inside the regular class. Its logic: for a cross-class pair OR two infra servers it defers ENTIRELY to `compareServers` (infra ignore rank ‚Äî their intra-class order stays byte-alphabetical); for two regular servers rank is primary ‚Äî a ranked server sorts before any unranked one, two ranked sort by `rank` ascending, two unranked fall back to byte-order name. Consequence: an **all-regular-unranked** list is byte-alphabetical, identical to `compareServers` (the #260705-uh8f regression guard holds). The rank on each `ServerInfo` comes from the `/api/servers` `rank` field (`@rk_server_rank`, see `architecture.md` / `tmux-sessions.md`). **`compareServers` is retained** ‚Äî the wrapper delegates to it and only `session-context.tsx`'s import switched to `compareServersRanked`.

**Live re-sort without refetch** ‚Äî SessionContext listens for the server-global `event: server-order` on BOTH the per-server pool streams and the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream (identical payload on every stream, since the event is host-global). The `applyServerOrder(order)` handler stamps each named server's `rank` from its index in `order`, drops the rank of any server not listed (so it falls to the unranked tail), then re-sorts the held `servers` array with the same `compareServersRanked` ‚Äî a state update, NO `/api/servers` refetch. Churn is bounded to explicit reorder events (not per-tick SSE), so no dedup guard is needed. See ¬ß Server-tile drag reorder below for the write path.

**Grey (de-emphasized, not disabled) treatment**: the tile **name** text renders `text-text-secondary` instead of `text-text-primary` when `isInfraServer(name)`, on two surfaces ‚Äî the Sidebar Server tile (`ServerTile`, `server-panel.tsx`) and the Host-page TMUX SERVERS tile (`host-overview-page.tsx`). Applied **uniformly** to all infra servers (`rk-daemon` and `rk-test-*`). Hover, click, active-selection, and the kill ‚úï are all unchanged ‚Äî the tile stays fully attachable (reading daemon logs is legitimate) and MUST NOT read as dead/disconnected. **No class change** was made to the Sessions-tree `ServerGroup` header: it already renders `text-text-secondary` at rest and `text-text-primary` only for the current server, and active-selection treatment is intentionally left alone.

**Kill guard for `rk-daemon`** (`app.tsx`): the server-kill confirm Dialog is NOT `kill-dialog.tsx` (that stateless dialog handles sessions/windows only). The server-kill confirm is the `killServerTarget` Dialog in `app/frontend/src/app.tsx` ("Kill tmux server?"), the single choke point for **both** kill entry paths ‚Äî the server-tile ‚úï (`onKillServer` ‚Üí `setKillServerTarget(name)`) and the command-palette `Server: Kill` (`setKillServerTarget(server)`). When `killServerTarget === DAEMON_SERVER`, the dialog renders an extra `text-red-400` warning line ("**rk-daemon** hosts the run-kit daemon serving this dashboard ‚Äî killing it takes the dashboard down"); a regular target shows no warning. The ‚úï affordance is **kept** on every tile (including `rk-daemon`) ‚Äî hiding the tile ‚úï would leave the palette path unguarded and would remove a legitimate capability (an operator may intentionally kill/restart the daemon server), which is why the guard is a dialog warning, not a capability removal. This parallels the change's own de-emphasize-don't-hide principle.

### Render Performance (memo tree + leaf-scoped `useNow`)

`260613-ect6-sidebar-render-perf` made the sidebar tree stop re-rendering on every SSE session tick. The session SSE stream fires several times/sec; each tick produces a fresh `slicesByServer` Map in `session-context.tsx`, which churns the derived `sessionsByServer`/`sessionOrderByServer`/`isConnectedByServer` Maps (intentional fresh refs, documented in that file) ‚Äî and before this change there was **no `React.memo` anywhere in the frontend**, so the whole tree (every `ServerGroup`/`SessionRow`/`WindowRow`) re-rendered on each tick. The fix has three coupled parts; **all three are load-bearing ‚Äî undoing any one silently re-breaks the perf win with no test catching it.**

**1. Row components are `React.memo`'d.** `WindowRow` (`memo(WindowRowInner)`, `window-row.tsx:354`), `SessionRow` (`memo(SessionRowInner)`, `session-row.tsx:200`), and `ServerGroup` (`memo(ServerGroupInner)`, `index.tsx:1280`) are each wrapped in `memo` (bare named import from `react`). **These are the first ‚Äî and currently only ‚Äî `React.memo` usages in the frontend.**

**2. The per-second `now` tick lives in a leaf `useNow()` hook (`hooks/use-now.ts`), NOT a threaded prop.** `useNow()` returns `Math.floor(Date.now()/1000)` and self-ticks every 1s. Since `260706-y1ar` (Row Minimalism removed the window-row duration) it is consumed by **one** leaf: `WindowContent` in `status-panel.tsx` (feeds the L0 `out` register's elapsed via `getOutputLine`). The former tiny `WindowDuration({ win })` leaf inside `WindowRow` (which rendered `getWindowDuration(win, now)`) was **deleted with the trailing status cluster** ‚Äî the sidebar tree no longer ticks per-second at all. The old `const nowSeconds = Math.floor(Date.now()/1000)` computed in the `Sidebar`/`BottomPanels` render bodies and threaded as `nowSeconds` down through `ServerGroup`‚Üí`WindowRow`/`WindowPanel` is also **gone** ‚Äî a value that changes every render threaded into a memoized child defeats the memo. **Do NOT reintroduce a `nowSeconds` prop on these components, and do NOT re-add a per-second tick to `WindowRow`.** The bottom panel (`WindowContent`) is a single instance, so its per-second re-render is negligible and does not touch the memoized `ServerGroup`/`SessionRow`/`WindowRow` tree.

**3. Handler/array props are referentially stable, so the memos actually skip.** Per-row/per-group handlers are identity-arg `useCallback`s in `Sidebar` (taking `server`/`session`/`windowId` as arguments, following the existing `toggleSession` pattern ‚Äî `handleSessionRowKill`/`handleWindowRowKill`/`handleSessionColorChange`/`handleWindowColorChange`/the drag handlers, `index.tsx:723-749` and the rename/drag block above), so a leaf calls a stable callback with its own identity rather than receiving a fresh closure. The Map/array context props (`rowTints`, `ansiPalette`, `allBoards`, `pinnedSet`, `pinnedToBoard`, `isPinnedToActiveBoardFor`) are verified stable across session ticks (sourced from `useMemo`/`useWindowPins`, changing only on theme/board events).

**THE SUBTLE INVARIANT (R6a ‚Äî most regression-prone):** the three handler props `Sidebar` *receives from its parents* ‚Äî `onSelectWindow`, `onCreateWindow`, `onCreateSession` ‚Äî MUST be `useCallback`s **at their source in the parents**, because both parents (`AppShell` in `app.tsx`, `BoardPage` in `board-page.tsx`) consume `useSessionContext()` and therefore re-render on **every** SSE tick. An inline arrow re-added at either parent recreates these references each tick and silently defeats `ServerGroup`'s memo for **every** group (including the currently-viewed one), with **no test catching it** ‚Äî the initial implementation memoized the rows but missed this caller-side leak, and review caught it as rework. The stable callbacks are `handleSidebarSelectWindow`/`handleSidebarCreateWindow`/`handleSidebarCreateSession` (`app.tsx:1116-1154`) and `handleSelectWindow` (`board-page.tsx:363`). **Root-cause fix:** `handleCreateSessionInstant` (`app.tsx:583`) and board-page's `handleCreateSession` (`board-page.tsx:145`) read churning values (`currentWindow`, `isSessionCreatePending`, `ctx.sessionsByServer`) via **render-time-mutated refs** (`currentWindowRef`/`isSessionCreatePendingRef`/`sessionsByServerRef`, set `ref.current = value` on each render) ‚Äî the same `dialogOpenRef`/`orderOverrideRef` idiom used elsewhere ‚Äî so the callbacks stay referentially stable across ticks instead of taking those churning values as `useCallback` deps.

**Why the memo skip is cross-server, not full per-row:** `updateSlice` (`session-context.tsx:216-227`) builds a `new Map(prev)` and replaces only the **changed** server's slice via `next.set(server, ...)`; every other server's slice object ‚Äî and its `slice.sessions` array ref ‚Äî carries over unchanged. So a tick on server B leaves server A's `sessions` prop referentially identical, and `ServerGroup`'s memo skips A's whole subtree. The currently-ticking server's own rows DO still re-render on its own data tick (correct ‚Äî its `sessions` ref changed); the `useNow` leaf is what additionally isolates the pure clock tick from even that server's row bodies.

**Invariants this change preserved (cross-linked, not re-described here):** the derive-over-store session-order pattern (`orderOverrideRef ?? sseOrder` + render-time `arraysEqual` reconcile, `260609-ebks` ‚Äî see ¬ß Session drag-and-drop reorder; memoization did NOT reintroduce a whole-Map watcher effect); #259's triage signals (`fabDisplayState === "failed"` red stage *text* + `isFailish` PR-fail signal ‚Äî see ¬ß Window rows; note the failed-state *dot* tint was superseded by `260615-0hsz`'s phase-hue dashed ring + red center, so the red whole-dot is gone ‚Äî only the stage text stays red); and single-source `isSelected` selection (URL window-id first, `isActiveWindow` fallback ‚Äî see ¬ß URL as Resumable Bookmark). The intra-`WindowRow` `useMemo`s (`tint`/`uncoloredSelectedTint`/`borderColor`/`buttonStyle`/`buttonClass`) are unchanged.

**Desktop** (`>= 640px`): Sidebar occupies the `<Shell>` `sidebar` grid area (rows 2‚Äì3, below the full-width topbar since `260702-6m46` ‚Äî see ¬ß Shell Grid Layout). Drag-resizable panel, default 220px width. Width persisted to `localStorage` key `runkit-sidebar-width` via `persistSidebarWidth(width)` (called once at drag-end; `setSidebarWidth` updates in-memory state per-pointermove). Constraints: min 160px, max 400px. The drag handle on the right edge is a `w-[3px]` visible bar (the 3px structural seam ‚Äî see ¬ß Border-Width System; `bg-border hover:bg-text-secondary`) with `col-resize` cursor, driven by pointer events (unified mouse/touch/pen). Its grabbable area is extended ~8px LEFTward into the sidebar via an invisible `before:` pseudo-element (`before:absolute before:inset-y-0 before:-left-2 before:right-0` ‚Äî pointer events on a pseudo hit its element, so the drag/hover handlers fire unchanged) so the thin visible bar is still easy to grab; it cannot extend rightward over the terminal because the `<aside>` is `overflow-hidden` (`260702-6m46` narrowed the bar from `w-[5px]` and added the pseudo). The handle is hidden when `sidebarOpen === false` ‚Äî the only re-open affordance is the hamburger at TopBar.left. Collapse animation: `grid-template-columns 150ms ease-out` (zero-width column when closed; no 48px rail). Drag-handle wiring is AppShell-only ‚Äî BoardPage doesn't render a drag handle (the dimension lives in `ChromeContext` and is shared across routes).

**Mobile** (`< 640px`, breakpoint changed from 768px in `260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout` to match the existing project `sm:` Tailwind breakpoint and `useIsMobile()` hook): Sidebar renders as an overlay positioned via `gridRow: "2/4"` inside the `<Shell>` (NOT `fixed inset-0`) ‚Äî backdrop and `<aside>` use `position: absolute` so the topbar stays visible during overlay open (matches the existing project convention recorded in `fab/project/context.md`). Backdrop classes include `absolute z-40 bg-black/50`; aside classes include `absolute left-0 z-50 w-[88%] max-w-[320px] bg-bg-primary shadow-2xl` plus `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`. Open/close is driven by `sidebarOpen` (the previous separate `drawerOpen` was removed when the rotation collapsed mobile-vs-desktop into one boolean). Dismissal: tapping the backdrop, tapping a destination row (auto-closes after navigation), the explicit close affordance at TopBar.left (the hamburger), or **Escape** (added by `260613-o20f-sidebar-drawer-a11y`).

**Mobile drawer focus trap** (`260613-o20f-sidebar-drawer-a11y`): the overlay's `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"` contract is now honored. `Shell` attaches a `drawerRef` to the `<aside>` and drives the shared `useFocusTrap(containerRef, active, onEscape)` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-focus-trap.ts` ‚Äî extracted from the focus-cycle logic in `dialog.tsx`/`command-palette.tsx`, adopted by the drawer only; refactoring those two modals to consume it is a documented follow-up Non-Goal). Active **only** when `isMobile && sidebarOpen && !!sidebarChildren` ‚Äî the mobile overlay; the desktop sidebar is a grid region and is NEVER trapped. On activation the hook focuses the first focusable element inside the `<aside>`; Tab/Shift+Tab cycle within it (wrap at the boundaries, `preventDefault` only there); Escape closes the drawer via `setSidebarOpen(false)` (additive to the dismissals above). The `document` `keydown` listener attaches only while active and is removed on deactivate/unmount; `onEscape` is read through a stable `onEscapeRef` so a fresh closure each render still fires the latest. **No focus-return on close** (matches `Dialog`/`CommandPalette`).

**Nested-modal deference** (R10): while a nested **modal** dialog ‚Äî a `[role="dialog"][aria-modal="true"]` **descendant** of the `<aside>` (e.g. `KillDialog`‚Üínon-portaled `Dialog`, which renders inside the Sidebar tree, hence inside the drawer) ‚Äî is open, `hasNestedDialog(container)` detects it and the trap stands down entirely: its `handleKeyDown` early-returns before both Escape and Tab. So a single Escape dismisses only the topmost modal (not the whole drawer), and the drawer-wide Tab wrap can't pull focus out of the nested dialog into the rows behind it. The `<aside>` itself carries `role="dialog"` but is correctly excluded: `querySelector` returns descendants only, backed by an explicit `!== container` guard. **The `aria-modal="true"` part of the selector is load-bearing** (`260613-o20f-sidebar-drawer-a11y` PR review): `PinPopover` carries `role="dialog"` but is NON-modal (no `aria-modal`, no internal Tab-trap) ‚Äî matching it would have made the drawer trap stand down for a layer that doesn't contain focus itself, letting Tab escape the drawer and regressing the `aria-modal` contract; restricting to modal dialogs keeps the trap live for `PinPopover`/`SwatchPopover`. (Those two popovers attach capture-phase `document` keydown listeners with `stopPropagation`, which independently suppress the trap's bubble-phase Escape listener ‚Äî so there's no Escape collision with them even though they are not caught by `hasNestedDialog`.)

**Resize separator cursor convention**: Horizontal separator (server‚Üîsession panel divider, inside `CollapsiblePanel`) uses `cursor-row-resize`; vertical separator (sidebar‚Üîterminal, in `app.tsx`) uses `cursor-col-resize`. Both are the double-arrow-with-middle-bar vocabulary (not `ns-resize`/`ew-resize`). Hover highlight on both uses full-opacity `hover:bg-text-secondary`.

**Document-body cursor override during drag**: Thin drag handles lose their `:hover` cursor once a drag starts because the pointer moves off the narrow strip. Both handlers work around this by writing `document.body.style.cursor = "<axis>-resize"` on drag start and `""` on drag end ‚Äî so the cursor persists at document level across the whole gesture, regardless of where the pointer lands. Both handlers (horizontal `CollapsiblePanel` and vertical sidebar-width) drive this from pointer-event handlers; the vertical handler migrated to pointer events so the corner affordance's `preventDefault()` on pointerdown wouldn't suppress the mouse compatibility events the vertical drag would otherwise rely on. `CollapsiblePanel`'s unmount cleanup also clears the body cursor to prevent a leaked cursor if the component unmounts mid-drag (navigation, hot-reload). Future thin-handle drag affordances should follow this pattern rather than relying on element-level `:hover`.

**Multi-axis corner affordance**: Both sidebar drag handlers use independent document-level listeners (horizontal tracks `clientY` only, vertical tracks `clientX` only) with independent state refs, so they coexist without coordination. The corner element at the separator intersection exploits this: its pointerdown invokes the horizontal handler, then the vertical handler, then writes `document.body.style.cursor = "nwse-resize"` last so the diagonal cursor wins over the axis-specific writes. Corner visibility is coupled to the horizontal handle's `showDragHandle` (`resizable && isOpen && !isMobile`) ‚Äî same guard, no separate source of truth. Wired via optional props: `app.tsx` ‚Üí `Sidebar` (`onSidebarResizeStart`) ‚Üí `ServerPanel` (`onSidebarResizeStart`) ‚Üí `CollapsiblePanel` (`onCornerPointerDown`). All optional at every level so other `CollapsiblePanel` consumers (WindowPanel, HostPanel, mobile drawer) render the default single-handle path unchanged.

**Padding**: `px-3 sm:px-6` (matches top bar and bottom bar chrome padding).

**Sessions header**: The Sessions panel in `sidebar/index.tsx` is a plain always-open `<div>` (intentionally not a `CollapsiblePanel` ‚Äî the session tree is a core always-visible nav surface). Its header row uses `text-text-secondary` as the baseline text color, with the "Sessions" label in `font-medium`. When `currentSession` is non-null, its name is rendered to the right of the label in `truncate text-text-primary font-mono` ‚Äî exactly mirroring the ServerPanel `headerRight` pattern (`server-panel.tsx:81-86`). No background tint on this header ‚Äî per-server tints live on the `ServerGroup` headers below.

**Per-server `ServerGroup`s**: Below the Sessions header, the sidebar renders one `ServerGroup` per server in `servers` (the list returned by `/api/servers`). Each group is a `CollapsiblePanel`-style collapsible whose header carries the server name and the `+` new-session affordance (creates against that section's server, regardless of `currentServer`); the body contains that server's session tree, fed by `sessionsByServer.get(server)` and ordered by `sessionOrderByServer.get(server)`. Per-server slice isolation is the rule ‚Äî drag-and-drop, rename, kill, ghost reconciliation, and optimistic-action keys all carry the server they originated on so cross-server overlays do not leak.

**Default collapse + persistence**: By default the `currentServer` group is open and all other groups are collapsed. User toggles persist per-server in `localStorage["runkit-panel-sessions-{server}"]`. On board routes (`currentServer === null`) no group is the implicit default ‚Äî collapse follows persisted state, falling back to all-collapsed. The legacy single-server `runkit-panel-sessions` key is migrated best-effort into the current server's namespaced key on first read when `currentServer` is non-null; if the user first lands on a board route, the migration is skipped (acceptable per the spec's "best-effort, no error if missing" rule). Expanding a non-current server's group also calls `attachServer(name)` on the provider so its slice starts populating from SSE. **`toggleServerSection`'s `setServerSectionsOpen` updater MUST be pure** ‚Äî it MUST NOT `localStorage.setItem` or call `attachServer` inside the updater body. Under React 19 StrictMode (active via `main.tsx`, dev + e2e) updaters are double-invoked, so a `localStorage` write inside the updater is observed by the second pass (`readServerOpen` re-reads it), inverting the computed `next` and turning a single Expand click into a net no-op (the group never opens). Instead, snapshot `current = readServerOpen(server)` once, compute `next = !current`, run the persist + lazy `attachServer` side-effects ONCE outside the updater, then commit a pure functional update that derives `next` from `prev` (falling back to the pre-write `current` snapshot for an untouched group, never a fresh `readServerOpen`) for batch-safety. Established by `260602-mss7-fix-sidebar-group-expand`.

**Server Pane ‚Üî Sessions Pane scope coupling**: The Sessions Pane's per-server `ServerGroup` list is gated by the Server Pane's open state, so the sidebar exposes exactly one "see all servers" surface and one "switch servers" surface at any moment. Two cases: when the Server Pane is collapsed (the `defaultOpen={false}` first-run state), the Sessions Pane iterates the full `servers` array ‚Äî the pre-coupling baseline behaviour. When the Server Pane is open AND `currentServer !== null`, the Sessions Pane renders exactly one `ServerGroup` (the entry whose `name === currentServer`) and omits all other groups from the rendered tree (not hidden via CSS ‚Äî absent from the DOM). When the Server Pane is open AND `currentServer === null` (e.g., route `/` before resolution, or the previously-current server was killed), no `ServerGroup` is rendered and an empty-state hint takes its place: `Select a server above to see its sessions.`, styled with `text-text-secondary text-xs py-4 text-center` (matching the existing "No sessions" empty-state convention). The transition between the all-servers tree and the current-server-only tree snaps in the next React commit ‚Äî no fade/slide/height/opacity animation is added at the group-list level; only the existing per-group `CollapsiblePanel` body transitions remain. Other servers' persisted collapse states (`runkit-panel-sessions-{server}`) sit dormant while filtered out ‚Äî never cleared or overwritten by the coupling logic ‚Äî and each group re-renders with its persisted value when the Server Pane closes. The current server's group is force-opened while filtered: `Sidebar` passes `isOpen={true}` to the rendered `ServerGroup` regardless of `localStorage["runkit-panel-sessions-{currentServer}"]`, so the filtered view always shows content rather than a degenerate collapsed header. This override is render-time only ‚Äî the persisted key is not written by the force-open path, and chevron clicks still flow through `toggleServerSection(currentServer)` so the persisted state advances; the persisted value takes visible effect once the Server Pane closes. The source-of-truth read path is the `runkit-panel-server` localStorage key (the same key `ServerPanel`'s `CollapsiblePanel` writes via its `storageKey` prop) ‚Äî no new state is introduced. Both `Sidebar` and `CollapsiblePanel` read this key through the shared `useLocalStorageBoolean` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-local-storage-boolean.ts`), which provides same-tab reactivity via an in-module pub/sub keyed on the storage key (a localStorage write alone does not trigger a React render, and the native `storage` event fires only across tabs); cross-tab parity is a free byproduct of the hook also subscribing to `storage`. `CollapsiblePanel`'s external API surface is unchanged ‚Äî the hook is an internal refactor of its previous `readPersistedState` + manual `setItem` pattern, so `WindowPanel`, `HostPanel`, `ServerPanel`, and other consumers keep their existing prop sets.

**Current-server visual marker**: The `currentServer`'s group header carries the same selected-tile shade convention used by `ServerPanel` ‚Äî `rowTints.get(serverColors.get(currentServer)).selected` when the server has a color assigned, with a neutral `UNCOLORED_SELECTED` fallback otherwise. No marker is drawn when `currentServer === null` (board routes / index). The marker tracks `currentServer` reactively, so server-route switches re-paint the marker without remounting the group.

**Cross-server window navigation**: Clicking a session name or window row in a non-current server's group navigates to that server's route (`/$server/$window`) via `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params: { server: thatServer, window } })`. The provider picks up the new `currentServer` via `useMatches()` on the next route match ‚Äî no explicit `setCurrentServer` call. The previously-current server's group remains rendered (per default-collapse rules); its EventSource and slice persist so re-visiting is instant.

**Cross-server drag-and-drop is rejected**: Dragging a window from one server's group and dropping it on another server's session/group fires a toast `"Moving windows across tmux servers isn't supported yet"` and skips any move API call. tmux's `move-window` does not span servers, so cross-server move is a separate problem. Within-server drag-and-drop (window reorder within a session, cross-session window move within the same server, session reorder within the same server) is preserved verbatim.

**Session rows**: Chevron toggle (left, expands/collapses window list), session name (selects the session's first window via `onSelectWindow(server, session, windows[0].windowId)` ‚Üí `selectWindow(server, windowId)`), + new window button (right), ‚úï kill button (right, always visible). Click session name fires the select mutation for the first window's `@N`; the URL follows on the next SSE snapshot to `/$server/<windowId>` (2-segment since `260529-jad6`); click chevron toggles expand/collapse. The session-level `+` button triggers instant session creation against the parent group's server (calls `onCreateSession` ‚Üí `executeCreateSessionInstant`), not a dialog. The window-level `+` button triggers instant window creation (existing `executeCreateWindow` behavior, passes `activeWin?.worktreePath` as CWD).

**Window rows** (**Row Minimalism** since `260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing`): Single line with a leading unified `StatusDot` + window name (left) ‚Äî **and nothing else in the status role**. The trailing status cluster (the fab stage-word span + the duration text) was **REMOVED**; the leading `StatusDot` is the row's ONLY externally visible status signal (its core hue = journey, shape = health, additive halo = `waiting`), and the freed width goes to the window name. The exact stage word + durations survive in the `StatusDotTip` hover-card and the PANE panel's register view (their recovery path). Hover-reveal action icons (pin / color / kill) are untouched ‚Äî they are ACTIONS, not status. All rows have `border-l-2` (transparent when not selected to prevent layout shift). Currently selected window highlighted with `bg-accent/10` + `border-accent` + `font-medium` + `rounded-r`. Selection compares the URL window ID against `win.windowId` (falling back to `isActiveWindow` when no URL window) ‚Äî clicking a row fires `selectWindow(server, win.windowId)` (a pure tmux mutation; window ID is a self-contained tmux target, so no session arg); the selection state and URL update follow on the next SSE snapshot. See ¬ß URL as Resumable Bookmark for the full sidebar-click contract. The session row (parent) gains a `waiting`-count badge ‚Äî see ¬ß Attention Surfacing.

**Current-row focus on mobile drawer open** (`260613-o20f-sidebar-drawer-a11y`): `Sidebar` attaches `navRef` to its `<nav aria-label="Sessions">` and runs a `useEffect` (reading `useIsMobile()` + chrome `sidebarOpen`) that, when the drawer is visible on mobile, queries `[data-window-id] [aria-current="page"]` then `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })` + `focus()`es that row ‚Äî landing the keyboard user on their current context. Deferred via `requestAnimationFrame` so it supersedes the focus trap's first-focus (which is committed in `Shell`'s effect). The selector is scoped to WINDOW rows: the active `BoardsSection` row also carries `aria-current="page"` but has no `[data-window-id]` ancestor, so it is excluded ‚Äî board routes (no selected window) no-op and the trap's first-focusable focus stands. Mirrors the `server-panel.tsx:77-82` mount-scroll pattern. Since `260613-wt1v-sidebar-keyboard-nav` this effect ALSO syncs the roving cursor: it `setRovingKey(key)`s the `[data-window-id]` row it focuses so the tab-stop (`tabIndex={0}`) and the DOM-focused row don't desync (otherwise the next arrow press would jump) ‚Äî see ¬ß Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA below.

1. **Leading status dot (unified `StatusDot`) ‚Äî the row's ONLY status signal** (Row Minimalism, `260706-y1ar`): the row's single leading dot is `<StatusDot win={win} />` (`status-dot.tsx`, see ¬ß Status Dot). Since `260706-y1ar` it is the palette-v3 **two-family ladder**: a fab window shows its cool pipeline phase (blue intake ‚Üí green apply‚Üíreview-pr collapsed ‚Üí purple PR) with a shape for health (ring/solid/dotted-ring+red-center/rounded-square); a plain window with a fresh `agentState` shows the warm ad-hoc-agent hue (yellow working ‚Üí orange PR); a plain window with neither shows the monochrome gray floor (solid = active, ring = idle). A `waiting` window of ANY tier gets an **additive constant-yellow halo** (core hue + shape untouched). The old activity-branch `fabDisplayState === "failed" ? text-red-400` whole-dot tint is GONE ‚Äî a failed fab stage renders as a dotted ring **in its phase hue** with only a small red center dot. Pure CSS + the `rk-waiting-halo` keyframe. *(History: `260615-0hsz` was the three-tier `PR > fab > tmux` hue=phase/shape=status model; `260706-y1ar` rewrote it into two families + the additive halo and made the dot consume `agentState`.)*

2. **Row Minimalism ‚Äî the trailing status cluster is REMOVED** (`260706-y1ar`): the fab stage-word span (formerly `text-xs`, red-when-`failed`, quiet-parked-row-gated) and the duration text (`WindowDuration`/`TickingDuration` leaves + their per-second `useNow()` tick) were **deleted** from the row. The leading `StatusDot` is the sole status signal; the freed width goes to the window name. The exact stage word + durations are the tip's + PANE panel's job now (their recovery path ‚Äî see ¬ß Status Dot hover-card, ¬ß Pane panel four-register view). *(The quiet-parked-row `fabDisplayState !== "done"` gate + the `260613-o20f` red-when-failed token, once in this cluster, are moot on the row ‚Äî they lived on the removed stage word. The tip keeps the exact stage label regardless.)*

3. **PR status ‚Äî the PR phase of the leading `StatusDot`**. The high-value PR signal lives in the single LEADING `StatusDot` (¬ß Status Dot), reached when `statusDotState(win)`'s ladder returns a PR phase ‚Äî `pr` (purple) for a `fabChange && prNumber` window, `agentPr` (orange) for a `fresh-agent && prNumber` window (D1 per-family ownership). A plain floor pane's PR never owns the dot; the derived PR still shows in the PANE panel L3 register + the tip's "Open PR" link (universal derivation, Principle X). The PR status shape reuses `prShape`/`prDotState` unchanged (`merged`‚Üí`done`, `fail`‚Üí`failed`, `pending`‚Üí`ring`, `healthy`‚Üí`solid`; closed-unmerged never owns the dot post-D1). **Still NOT the full PR line** ‚Äî full PR detail lives in the PANE panel's L3 register (¬ß Pane panel four-register view).

4. **Hover-icon cluster** (pin / color swatch / kill) ‚Äî absolutely-positioned container (`absolute right-2 top-1/2 -translate-y-1/2 flex items-center gap-1 z-10`) rendered as a sibling of the row button (avoids nested interactive elements); the row button reserves `pr-[68px]` when the pin is wired (`pr-11` otherwise) so labels don't run under the icons. **Inert at rest** (`260612-epqk-display-state-quiet-rows`): the container carries `pointer-events-none` plus `group-hover:pointer-events-auto coarse:pointer-events-auto has-[:focus-visible]:pointer-events-auto`, so on fine pointers a stray click near the row's right edge falls through to the row-select button instead of hitting an invisible kill/pin/swatch target (deliberate icon clicks are unaffected ‚Äî any mouse interaction hovers the row first, restoring interactivity). Each hover-revealed `opacity-0` button (pin's not-pinned branch, color swatch, kill) carries `focus-visible:opacity-100` so keyboard focus never sits on an invisible control ‚Äî the reveal is per-button because a container-level `opacity-100` cannot reveal children carrying their own `opacity-0` (element opacity is independent/multiplicative); the container-level `has-[:focus-visible]:pointer-events-auto` restores interactivity while a child is focused. First codebase use of the Tailwind v4 `has-[]` variant. No geometry change: the `pr-[68px]` reservation, `coarse:opacity-100` always-visible icons on touch, and the pin's permanent visibility when pinned-to-any are untouched. (The former info `‚ìò` button + popover and the pane-CWD hover tooltip are gone ‚Äî window metadata lives in the Pane panel's rows instead, `status-panel.tsx`; see design.md decision #27.)

**Empty state**: When no sessions exist (`sessions.length === 0`), the sidebar displays "No sessions" text with a centered `+ New Session` button. The button triggers instant session creation (same as the sidebar `+` button and breadcrumb dropdown `+ New Session` action). With no active window, `cwd` is omitted and the name falls back to `session`.

**Inline rename** (double-click ‚Äî windows and sessions): Both window names and session names in the sidebar support double-click inline rename. The pattern is identical for both:

- Double-clicking a name `<span>` replaces it with a text `<input>` pre-filled with the current name, auto-focused with all text selected.
- Enter or blur commits the rename if the trimmed value is non-empty and differs from the original name. Empty or unchanged input dismisses the editor without an API call.
- Escape cancels editing. A `cancelledRef` / `sessionCancelledRef` prevents blur from committing after an Escape (or cross-cancel).
- Single-click behavior is preserved (navigate to window / navigate to session's first window) ‚Äî only `onDoubleClick` triggers editing.

**Window rename**: since `260703-5ilm` the sidebar's inline window rename goes through the **shared `useWindowRename()` hook** (`hooks/use-window-rename.ts`) ‚Äî the same hook the top-bar `WindowHeading` uses, so both surfaces rename identically. The hook's `execute(server, session, windowId, newName)` runs the optimistic store rename (`windowStore.renameWindow`), rolls back via `windowStore.clearRename` + toast on API failure, and clears the pending marker on settle; SSE still reconciles the canonical updated name once the server event arrives. The sidebar's former inline ~25-line `executeRenameWindow` `useOptimisticAction` block + its `lastRenameWindowRef` + the `renameWindow` API import were deleted in favor of the one-line hook call. See ¬ß Shared window rename. (The sidebar still owns its own trim/empty-name guard before calling `execute`.)

**Session rename**: calls `renameSession(server, oldName, newName)` via `useOptimisticAction`. The UI updates immediately via `markRenamed("session", server, oldName, newName)`; on API failure it rolls back via `unmarkRenamed(server, oldName)` (`lastRenameSessionRef` snapshots `{ server, name }` together for cross-server-safe rollback). Toast error on failure. The dialog-based session rename in `app.tsx` remains unchanged ‚Äî inline editing is an additional path.

**Cross-cancellation**: Only one inline edit (window or session) may be active at a time. Starting any new inline edit cancels the currently active one without committing it. `handleStartEditing` (window edit) sets `sessionCancelledRef.current = true` and clears `editingSession` before activating the window input; `handleStartSessionEditing` sets `cancelledRef.current = true` and clears `editingWindow` before activating the session input. This ensures blur on the cancelled input is a no-op.

**Window drag-and-drop reorder**: Window items in the sidebar are `draggable={true}` (ghost windows excluded). Uses native HTML5 drag-and-drop ‚Äî no external library (constitution IV). Drag state managed via `dragSource` and `dropTarget` state in `Sidebar`. On `dragStart`, sets `dataTransfer` with JSON `{ session, index, windowId, name }` and `effectAllowed: "move"`. The `windowId` and `name` fields were added for cross-session optimistic operations; within-session drops use only `session` and `index`. Within-session drops: drop indicator is a 2px accent-colored top border (`borderTop: 2px solid var(--color-accent)`) on the hovered window item when source and target differ. On `drop`, uses `useOptimisticAction` to immediately swap window indices in the Zustand store via `swapWindowOrder(session, srcIndex, dstIndex)`, then fires `moveWindow(server, srcWindowId, dstIndex)` API call in the background (server captured at drop-handler time; the move targets the source by its stable `windowId` and the destination by position). The optimistic action's arg tuple is `(server, session, srcWindowId, srcIndex, dstIndex)` ‚Äî `session`/`srcIndex` retained for the store-side swap/rollback, while the API call uses only `srcWindowId` + `dstIndex`. `onSelectWindow` is called immediately (not deferred to API success). On API failure, `onAlwaysRollback` reverses the swap via `swapWindowOrder(session, dstIndex, srcIndex)` and shows a toast error. SSE reconciliation naturally clears the optimistic state when `setWindowsForSession` replaces all entries with server-confirmed data. Same-position drops are no-ops (source === target check). All drag visual state (drop indicators) cleared on `dragEnd` and `drop` ‚Äî handles both successful drops and cancelled drags (Escape, drag outside sidebar).

**Cross-session drag-and-drop**: Dropping a window onto a different session's header moves it to that session. `handleDragOver` accepts drag events on session headers when the dragged window is from a different session. Visual feedback: the session header shows an accent border (`border-accent`) when a valid cross-session drop is hovering. The drag data payload includes `{ session, index, windowId, name }` ‚Äî `windowId` and `name` were added for optimistic store operations (within-session drop ignores the extra fields). On drop, `handleSessionDrop` calls `executeMoveToSession` (a `useOptimisticAction` instance) with all six arguments `(server, srcSession, srcIndex, windowId, windowName, dstSession)`. The optimistic lifecycle:

- **`onOptimistic`**: calls `killWindow(srcSession, windowId)` to hide the window from the source session, `addGhostWindow(dstSession, windowName)` to show it in the target (using the source window's display name, not a placeholder), and navigates to `/$server` immediately. The `optimisticId` is stored in a ref for rollback.
- **`action`**: calls `moveWindowToSession(server, srcSession, srcIndex, dstSession)` ‚Äî the API client function with `server` as the first positional argument.
- **`onAlwaysRollback`** (API failure): calls `restoreWindow(srcSession, windowId)` to un-hide in source + `removeGhost(optimisticId)` to remove from target. Toast: "Failed to move window to session".
- **`onAlwaysSettled`** (success): clears the ref. SSE reconciliation handles final state ‚Äî `setWindowsForSession` removes the entry from the source (not in incoming list), adds it to the target (new incoming entry), and reconciles the ghost (new `windowId` not in ghost's `snapshotWindowIds`).

Same-session header drops are ignored (not a valid cross-session target). Within-session window-to-window drag-and-drop is unchanged. The sidebar handles the move internally ‚Äî no `onMoveWindowToSession` prop or `handleMoveWindowToSession` callback in `app.tsx` (the sidebar imports `moveWindowToSession` directly from `@/api/client`, matching the pattern of other sidebar API calls).

**Session drag-and-drop reorder**: Session header rows are themselves draggable (the row root, not the chevron / name button) ‚Äî except optimistic ghost sessions, which set `draggable={false}` because they have no canonical name to persist yet. The reorder feature shares the SAME `<SessionRow>` `onDragOver` handler used by cross-session window drops; the two are disambiguated by `dataTransfer.types`: window drags use the default JSON payload, session reorder drags use a custom MIME `application/x-session-reorder` (so a window-drag never accidentally triggers a session reorder, and vice versa). Native HTML5 drag-and-drop, no external library (Constitution IV).

The persisted order lives server-side in tmux user-option `@rk_session_order` (see `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß "Server-Scoped User Options"), broadcast to all connected clients via SSE event `session-order`. Frontend pipeline:

- **Source of truth**: `SessionContext.sessionOrder: string[]` populated from the SSE `session-order` event handler in `session-context.tsx` (`es.addEventListener("session-order", ...)`). The handler ignores events whose `server` field doesn't match the current `server` prop ‚Äî defense-in-depth alongside the backend's per-server filtering.
- **Render-time order computation**: `Sidebar` derives `orderedSessions` via `useMemo` over `sessions` and an effective order. Sessions absent from the saved order render at the bottom in their natural sequence (`Number.POSITIVE_INFINITY` rank) so newly created sessions never disappear from the sidebar.
- **Snappy drag (derive-over-store)**: The transient drag override is held in a server-keyed `orderOverrideRef = useRef<Record<string, string[]>>({})` (NOT React state), and the displayed order is *derived at render* as `orderOverrideRef.current[server] ?? (sessionOrderByServer.get(server) ?? [])` ‚Äî `handleSessionReorderStart`/`handleSessionReorderOver` compute the new order via `splice` and write it into the ref for instant visual feedback. Because writing a ref does not re-render, the handlers call a minimal `forceRender` nudge (`useReducer((x) => x + 1, 0)`). The override clears via a **per-server, render-time SSE-equality reconcile** (since `260609-ebks-derive-sidebar-order`): while computing each visible server's props, if `arraysEqual(orderOverrideRef.current[server], sseOrder)` the override is deleted and `localOrder` rendered as `null` in the same pass (no nudge needed ‚Äî the displayed output is unchanged). This replaced the former `localOrderByServer` `useState` + a whole-`sessionOrderByServer`-Map watcher `useEffect`, which re-ran on every unrelated SSE slice tick (sessions/metrics/connection fire a fresh Map reference several times a second) ‚Äî pure render-efficiency churn, not a correctness bug. The per-server equality check (not a whole-Map effect) fires only on the relevant server's echo, so unrelated churn no longer triggers reconcile work. No **data** snap-back: the override outlives the debounced PUT until that server's SSE order echoes the new arrangement, so the *order* never reverts.
- **`dragover` MUST accept the drop even on the self-target row** (`260705-i41e-server-tile-drag-snap-back`): `handleSessionReorderOver` MUST call `e.preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"` for a valid same-server session-reorder drag *even when hovering the dragged row itself* (`sessionDragSource.name === targetName`), then bail with no reorder math. HTML5 DnD registers a release as an accepted drop only when the LAST `dragover` before mouse-up was `preventDefault()`ed; insert-before splicing lands the dragged row under the cursor, so the dragged row's OWN element is the **common terminal hover state** at release. Bailing early there (the pre-`i41e` guard combined the self-name check into the leading `if (!sessionDragSource || ... || sessionDragSource.name === targetName) return;`) left the final `dragover` uncancelled ‚Üí no `drop` fired ‚Üí `dragend` saw `dropEffect: "none"` ‚Üí the browser played its native **cancelled-drag snap-back ghost** flying back to the drag origin, contradicting the visibly-succeeded reorder (the data stuck via the debounce). **Guard order (invariant across both this handler and `useServerReorder.onDragOver` ‚Äî see ¬ß Server-tile drag reorder)**: source/scope guard (`!sessionDragSource || sessionDragSource.server !== server`, confines the drag to one server's group) + MIME guard (`application/x-session-reorder`) come BEFORE acceptance; the self-target no-op (`if (sessionDragSource.name === targetName) return;`) comes AFTER `preventDefault()`. Do NOT re-fold the self-name check back into the leading guard ‚Äî that is exactly the snap-back regression. Session-reorder keeps **debounce-only persistence** ‚Äî even though `drop` now also fires on session rows, no session drop-flush was added (the row's own `onDrop={handleSessionDrop}` is the window-move handler and no-ops safely on a reorder payload: empty `application/json` ‚Üí `JSON.parse` throws ‚Üí `catch` ‚Üí return).
- **Debounced PUT**: 250ms trailing debounce via `orderPutTimerRef` + `setTimeout`. Drag events fire on every cursor frame; coalescing avoids one HTTP call per frame. `handleSessionReorderEnd` (dragend) does NOT cancel the pending timer ‚Äî a fast drag-and-release within 250ms still flushes via the timer, otherwise the user's edit is lost.
- **Drag visual**: Source row gets `opacity-50` while it is the drag source (driven by the `isDragSource` prop on `<SessionRow>`).

`<SessionRow>` exposes optional drag props (`draggable`, `isDragSource`, `onDragStart`, `onDragEnd`) ‚Äî present for the new feature, absent for any future caller that doesn't want session reorder. The row root passes them straight through to the underlying `<div>`.

**Test ergonomics**: `session-context.tsx` exports a `StandaloneSessionContextProvider` test helper that accepts a partial multi-server shape (`sessionsByServer`, `sessionOrderByServer`, `isConnectedByServer`, `metricsByServer`, `currentServer`, etc.) and synthesizes the full context value without opening any network connection. Tests requiring SSE-driven behavior use the full `SessionProvider` with a stubbed `EventSource`; `MockEventSource` is keyed by URL so per-server streams can be driven independently (see `session-context.test.tsx` for the pattern).

**Drop-acceptance unit-test seam** (`260705-i41e`): asserting session-reorder drop acceptance IS practical through the existing `renderSidebar` harness in `index.test.tsx` ‚Äî there is a real seam, contrary to the pre-implementation assumption that none existed (session-row.test.tsx only stubs `onReorderOver` as a noop; index.test.tsx had no reorder coverage). The idiom: render via `renderSidebar`, `fireEvent.dragStart` the `[data-session-row="{server}:{name}"]` row (seeds `sessionDragSource` and writes the MIME onto a shared mutable `dataTransfer` bag mirroring the hook test's `makeDragEvent`), then `fireEvent.dragOver(row, { dataTransfer })` on the SAME row. **`fireEvent.dragOver` returns `false` when the handler called `preventDefault()`** ‚Äî that boolean is the drop-acceptance assertion (`expect(notPrevented).toBe(false)` + `dataTransfer.dropEffect === "move"`), no native-method stub needed. A source-guard negative case (`dragOver` with the MIME but NO prior `dragStart` ‚Üí returns `true`, not accepted) proves the guard fires before acceptance. The window-move `handleSessionDragOver` no-ops when its `dragSource` is null, so a prevented default on a session-reorder dragover is attributable solely to `handleSessionReorderOver`.

**Server-tile drag reorder** (`260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`): the two server-tile grids ‚Äî the Sidebar `ServerPanel` (`server-panel.tsx`) and the Host-page TMUX SERVERS grid (`host-overview-page.tsx`) ‚Äî are drag-reorderable, sharing ONE lifted hook `useServerReorder(servers, onError)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-server-reorder.ts`) so neither grid copy-pastes the handler logic. It mirrors the ¬ß Session drag-and-drop reorder pattern verbatim: native HTML5 DnD (no external library, Constitution IV), a custom MIME `application/x-server-reorder` (`SERVER_REORDER_MIME` ‚Äî so a server drag never collides with the `application/x-session-reorder` session drag or the default-JSON window drag), insert-before splice semantics on `dragOver`, and the derive-over-store optimistic override.

- **Effective-order input**: the hook takes the already-`compareServersRanked`-sorted `ctx.servers` and returns `{ orderedServers, getTileProps(name), isDragging, draggingName }`. Consumers render `orderedServers` (the transient optimistic order during a drag, else the authoritative list) and spread `getTileProps(name)` onto each tile.
- **Infra excluded**: only REGULAR servers participate. `getTileProps` returns `{ draggable: false }` (no drop handlers) for `isInfraServer(name)` tiles ‚Äî they are neither draggable nor valid drop targets, and the reorder POST carries only the regular-class order (rank `i` ‚Üí i-th regular server; infra ignore rank server-side, so omitting them is correct and keeps them pinned last).
- **Derive-over-store optimistic override**: the transient dragged order lives in `overrideRef = useRef<string[] | null>` (of regular server NAMES), NOT React state ‚Äî so writing it doesn't re-render; a minimal `forceRender` (`useReducer((x)=>x+1,0)`) drives the optimistic repaint (the same idiom as the sidebar session reorder). `onDragStart` seeds the override with the current regular order; `onDragOver` splices the dragged name to the target position. The override clears via a **render-time equality reconcile**: once the authoritative regular order element-wise equals the stored override (via `namesEqual`), the round-trip has landed and the ref is dropped (mutating a ref during render is safe ‚Äî output unchanged, no nudge). **No data snap-back on drag-end** ‚Äî the override outlives the debounced POST until the SSE `server-order` echo re-sorts `ctx.servers` to match, which triggers the reconcile, so the *order* never reverts.
- **`onDragOver` MUST accept the drop even on the self-target tile** (`260705-i41e-server-tile-drag-snap-back`): `onDragOver` MUST call `e.preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"` for a valid same-hook server-reorder drag *even when hovering the dragged tile itself* (`dragName === targetName`), then bail with no reorder math. HTML5 DnD registers a release as an accepted drop only when the LAST `dragover` before mouse-up was `preventDefault()`ed; insert-before splicing lands the dragged tile under the cursor, so the dragged tile's OWN element is the **common terminal hover state** at release. The pre-`i41e` guard folded the self-target check into the leading `if (!dragName || dragName === targetName) return;` ‚Äî so on the common release-over-self path the final `dragover` was never cancelled ‚Üí no `drop` fired ‚Üí `dragend` saw `dropEffect: "none"` ‚Üí the browser played its native **cancelled-drag snap-back ghost** flying the tile back to the drag origin, reading as failure even though the reorder visibly succeeded and persisted (the data stuck via the debounce). **Guard order (invariant, shared verbatim with the sidebar `handleSessionReorderOver` ‚Äî see ¬ß Session drag-and-drop reorder)**: originating-instance guard (`!dragName` ‚Äî the hook is instantiated by BOTH `ServerPanel` and the Host-page grid; a null-`dragNameRef` instance did not start the drag and must not accept it) ‚Üí infra guard (`isInfraServer(targetName)`, infra tiles are non-targets) ‚Üí MIME guard (`SERVER_REORDER_MIME`) ‚Äî all BEFORE acceptance; then `preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"`; then the self-target no-op (`if (dragName === targetName) return;`) AFTER acceptance. Do NOT re-fold the self-target check back into the leading `!dragName` guard ‚Äî that is exactly the snap-back regression this change fixed.
- **Debounce + drop-flush**: reorder writes go through a `SERVER_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS = 250` trailing debounce (`putTimerRef`), coalescing a rapid drag-over sweep into one `setServerOrder(order)` POST ‚Äî mirroring the sidebar's `SESSION_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS`. `onDrop` flushes any pending debounced POST immediately so the write isn't lost if the SSE echo races the timer. **The drop-flush path was effectively dead before `260705-i41e`** ‚Äî since the common release point is the dragged tile's own element and self-target dragovers bailed before `preventDefault()`, `drop` never fired there and only the 250ms timer saved the order; accepting the self-target drop (above) **revives** the flush: releasing over the source tile now fires `onDrop`, which flushes and clears the timer (single POST, no double-post). A **mount-scoped unmount cleanup effect** (`useEffect(() => () => clearTimeout(putTimerRef.current), [])`) clears a pending timer so a drag ending right before the grid unmounts never fires a stray post-unmount write (mirrors `sidebar/index.tsx:258-262`).
- **Drag-source feedback**: both grids dim the dragged tile via `opacity-50`, driven by `isDragging && draggingName === name` (the session-reorder `isDragSource` treatment). Do NOT delete the `isDragging`/`draggingName` fields ‚Äî they are the drag-affordance seam (a review found them zero-call-site and the fix WIRED them into both grids, the pattern-consistent direction).
- **Non-drag paths**: the Sessions-tree per-server `ServerGroup`s and the palette `Server: Switch to {name}` entries FOLLOW the order (via the `compareServersRanked` choke point) but expose no server drag affordance. Touch devices get no drag (HTML5 DnD doesn't fire on touch, accepted ‚Äî the palette `Server: Move up/down` are the touch/keyboard path; see ¬ß Command Palette Move up/down). Coverage: the hook's logic (MIME discrimination, insert-before splice, infra exclusion, override seed/reconcile, debounce/drop-flush, **self-target drop acceptance + drop-on-source flush** added by `260705-i41e`) is Vitest-covered in `use-server-reorder.test.ts`; the API+SSE slice is the `server-reorder.spec.ts` e2e (the live-drag e2e was infeasible under the single-infra-server e2e harness `RK_SERVER_ALLOWLIST=rk-test-e2e`, so it was descoped to Vitest, mirroring the `fixme`'d session-drag e2e). **The native snap-back ghost animation is browser-chrome-level and NOT observable via Playwright synthetic DnD** ‚Äî the drop-acceptance (`preventDefault`/`dropEffect`) is the only testable seam, so the fix has unit coverage only, no e2e.

**Board-list drag reorder** (`260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`): the BOARDS list itself is drag-reorderable on its two user-named surfaces ‚Äî the Sidebar `BoardsSection` rows (`sidebar/boards-section.tsx`, the "board pane, top-left") and the Host-page BOARDS zone tiles (`host-overview-page.tsx`) ‚Äî sharing ONE lifted hook `useBoardListReorder(boards, onError)` (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-board-list-reorder.ts`). It is a near-verbatim mirror of ¬ß Server-tile drag reorder (`useServerReorder`), with the same derive-over-store optimistic-override discipline, and is DISTINCT from the within-board PIN reorder (`/api/boards/{name}/reorder`, ¬ß Boards View) ‚Äî this reorders the boards, not the panes inside one.

- **Effective-order input + return shape**: the hook takes the already-backend-sorted board list (the `GET /api/boards` response order via `useBoards`, which is itself the display order ‚Äî see `architecture.md` `/api/boards`) and returns `{ orderedBoards, getTileProps(name), isDragging, draggingName }`. Consumers render `orderedBoards` (the transient optimistic order during a drag, else the authoritative list) and spread `getTileProps(b.name)` onto each row/tile.
- **Custom MIME**: `application/x-board-list-reorder` (`BOARD_LIST_REORDER_MIME`) ‚Äî distinct from `application/x-server-reorder`, `application/x-session-reorder`, and the board-pane window-move payload, so a foreign-MIME drag over a board row/tile is ignored (MIMEs never cross-fire).
- **No infra exclusion**: unlike `useServerReorder`, EVERY board is draggable and a valid drop target ‚Äî `getTileProps` returns the full handler set for every name (there is no board analog of the infra-server class).
- **Derive-over-store optimistic override**: the transient dragged order of board NAMES lives in `overrideRef = useRef<string[] | null>` (NOT React state); a minimal `forceRender` (`useReducer((x)=>x+1,0)`) drives the optimistic repaint. `onDragStart` seeds the override with the current order; `onDragOver` splices the dragged name to the target position (insert-before). The override clears via a **render-time name-equality reconcile** (`namesEqual`): once the authoritative `boards` order element-wise equals the stored override the round-trip has landed and the ref is dropped (mutating a ref during render is safe ‚Äî output unchanged, no nudge). **No snap-back on drag-end** ‚Äî the override outlives the debounced POST until the SSE `board-order` echo re-fetches `boards` to match (see propagation below), which triggers the reconcile.
- **`onDragOver` accepts the drop on the self-target tile BEFORE the self-target bail** ‚Äî the exact `260705-i41e` snap-back fix proven on the server hook: guard order is originating-instance (`!dragNameRef.current`) ‚Üí MIME (`BOARD_LIST_REORDER_MIME`) BEFORE acceptance, then `preventDefault()` + `dropEffect = "move"`, then the self-target no-op (`if (dragName === targetName) return;`) AFTER acceptance. Bailing before `preventDefault()` on the release-over-self path would leave the drop uncancelled ‚Üí native cancelled-drag snap-back ghost + a starved `onDrop` flush. Do NOT re-fold the self-target check into the leading guard.
- **Debounce + drop-flush**: reorder writes go through a `BOARD_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS = 250` trailing debounce (`putTimerRef`), coalescing a rapid drag-over sweep into one `setBoardOrder(order)` POST (mirroring `SERVER_ORDER_DEBOUNCE_MS`); `onDrop` flushes any pending POST immediately so the write isn't lost if the SSE echo races the timer. A mount-scoped unmount cleanup effect (`useEffect(() => () => clearTimeout(putTimerRef.current), [])`) clears a pending timer so a drag ending right before the list unmounts fires no stray post-unmount write.
- **Drag-source feedback + error toast**: both surfaces dim the dragged row/tile via `opacity-50` (`isDragging && draggingName === b.name`), and both pass `useToast().addToast` as the hook's `onError` handler so a failed reorder POST surfaces a toast ‚Äî matching the server-panel / Host-page precedent.
- **Propagation (server-global re-sort)**: `api/boards.ts` gains `setBoardOrder(order)` (POST `/api/boards/order`); `session-context.tsx` exposes a `subscribeBoardOrder` seam on BOTH the per-server pool streams AND the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream (so a zero-attached-server Host page still hears reorders, since the event is host-global); `useBoards` subscribes and reuses its existing `scheduleRefetch`/`REFETCH_DEBOUNCE_MS` machinery to re-fetch `/api/boards` on a `board-order` event ‚Äî the backend-sorted response is the single display-order source, so a reorder on one client re-sorts every other client live (NO client-side order reducer). The top-bar BoardSwitcher dropdown and every other `useBoards` consumer inherit the order passively.
- **Non-drag / keyboard path**: the palette `Board: Move up/down` (see ¬ß Command Palette Move up/down) is the keyboard + touch path (HTML5 DnD doesn't fire on touch). Coverage: the hook logic is Vitest-covered in `use-board-list-reorder.test.ts` (override lifecycle, render-time reconcile, debounce/flush, self-target accept, foreign-MIME ignore) plus BoardsSection + Host-page wiring tests; the API + rank-aware-sort + server-global-SSE slice is the `board-list-reorder.spec.ts` e2e (endpoint/SSE-surface form, mirroring `server-reorder.spec.ts` ‚Äî the live synthetic drag is Vitest's; see ¬ß E2E host-global filesystem state for its `~/.rk/settings.yaml` save/restore).

**Server selector footer** ‚Äî pinned at the bottom of the sidebar below the scrollable session tree, separated by `border-t border-border`. Displays `Server: {name}` with a dropdown trigger. Clicking opens a dropdown listing all available tmux servers (from `GET /api/servers`); the current server is highlighted with `text-accent`. Selecting a different server calls `setServer(name)`, which updates localStorage (`runkit-server`), reconnects SSE, and navigates to `/`. The session tree area is `flex-1 min-h-0 overflow-y-auto` above the pinned footer.

### Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA (`260613-wt1v-sidebar-keyboard-nav`)

The session/window tree is a **W3C-APG two-level disclosure tree** with roving-tabindex arrow navigation, scoped entirely to the Sessions tree DOM (never `document`, never the terminal ‚Äî no xterm.js key conflict). Builds on the Wave-2 memo tree (¬ß Render Performance) and preserves its SSE-tick invariant. Frontend-only ‚Äî no backend/API/route/tmux changes.

**Tree ARIA roles** (two levels ‚Äî decided; the server group stays structural, NOT a treeitem):
- The scrollable Sessions region (`<div role="tree" aria-label="Session tree">`, `index.tsx:1070`) carries `role="tree"`; the outer `<nav aria-label="Sessions">` stays the separate landmark, so the landmark and the tree widget don't collide on one element.
- **Session rows** (`SessionRow`, `session-row.tsx:113-128`) are `role="treeitem"` `aria-level={1}` with `aria-expanded={!isCollapsed}` (lifted onto the treeitem from the chevron), `aria-setsize`/`aria-posinset` (position among `orderedSessions`), and `data-session-row="${server}:${name}"` as the stable focus handle. `aria-controls={windowGroupId}` is emitted **ONLY while expanded** ‚Äî the `role="group"` window list is mounted only when `!isCollapsed`, so a collapsed row pointing `aria-controls` at an unmounted id would be invalid ARIA (SF-5, enforced via `aria-controls={isCollapsed ? undefined : windowGroupId}`).
- **Window rows** (`WindowRow`, `window-row.tsx:204-217`) are `role="treeitem"` `aria-level={2}` LEAF nodes (no `aria-expanded`) with `aria-setsize`/`aria-posinset` (position among `session.windows`), reusing their existing `data-window-id` handle.
- The **window-list container** (`<div className="ml-3" role="group" id={windows-${server}-${session.name}}>`, `index.tsx:1519`) is `role="group"`; that same id is threaded down as `windowGroupId` for the parent session's `aria-controls`. Server-group `<section>` headers stay structural wrappers ‚Äî server collapse/expand remains mouse/Tab-button only for v1.

**Roving-tabindex arrow nav**: exactly one tree row carries `tabIndex={0}` (the roving row), the rest `-1` (`tabIndex={rovingKey === key ? 0 : -1}`, threaded as a single primitive into the memo'd rows so an arrow press flips `tabIndex` on only the two affected rows ‚Äî the Wave-2 memo skip is preserved). The keydown handler is on the `role="tree"` container (`handleTreeKeyDown`) and early-returns when the target is an `<input>`/`<textarea>`/`isContentEditable` (so a row's rename input keeps Enter=commit / Escape=cancel and arrows move the caret). Bindings (APG-standard, each `preventDefault()`s):
- **ArrowDown/ArrowUp** ‚Äî next/prev visible row; **stop at the ends (no wrap)**; flow **continuously across all open server groups** as one flat list.
- **ArrowRight** ‚Äî collapsed session ‚Üí expand (focus stays, via `toggleSession`); expanded session ‚Üí first window child; window ‚Üí no-op (leaf).
- **ArrowLeft** ‚Äî expanded session ‚Üí collapse; window ‚Üí parent session row (scans upward for the nearest `aria-level="1"`); collapsed session ‚Üí no-op (no parent treeitem ‚Äî the server header is a wrapper).
- **Enter AND Space** ‚Äî activate. Derives the target from a typed `RowIdentity` discriminated union (`identityForKey`) and calls `onSelectWindow(server, session, windowId)` / `onSelectWindow(server, session, firstWindowId)` **DIRECTLY** ‚Äî NOT a synthesized `.click()` or a magic-string `aria-label` match (SF-2). Ghost/optimistic rows (`ghost` flag or empty `windowId`) are a no-op (SF-3), mirroring the drag-path `isGhostWindow` guard; an empty session (no first window) is likewise a no-op.
- **Home/End** ‚Äî first/last visible row.

**THE LOAD-BEARING INVARIANT (most regression-prone)**: the roving cursor is a `rovingKey` STRING (the row's `data-window-id` / `data-session-row`), NOT a numeric index ‚Äî so it survives expand/collapse and SSE add/remove without ever pointing at a stale or wrong row, and the "session, then descend into its windows, across groups" order falls out of DOM order for free (`getVisibleRows` reads `[role="treeitem"]` straight from the tree at keypress time). The key-normalization effect (resets `rovingKey` to the first visible row when it matches no rendered treeitem) is gated on `[rovingKey, rowsVersion]`, where `rowsVersion` (a `useReducer` counter) is bumped by `registerGroupRows` **ONLY when a server group's visible-row-SET signature changes** (the `|`-joined ordered row-key string ‚Äî window add/remove, collapse/expand, rename), NOT on the several-per-second passive SSE activity ticks. This preserves the Wave-2 #262 invariant: **an SSE tick must NOT change roving state or steal focus.** A tick recomputes `rowSlice`/`rowSignature` but the signature STRING is unchanged ‚Üí no bump ‚Üí the normalize effect doesn't run (no full-tree `querySelectorAll`, no `setRovingKey`). The only `row.focus()` is gated by `focusMovedRef`, set `true` only on an actual keypress-driven move, so a passive re-render never pulls focus into the sidebar. DOM focus + `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })` on a roving change reuse the CommandPalette/ThemeSelector "Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern" (¬ß Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern). Roving focus is INDEPENDENT of the URL-based `isSelected`/`aria-current="page"` selection (¬ß URL as Resumable Bookmark) ‚Äî do not conflate them. The mobile-drawer focus effect (¬ß Window rows ‚Üí Current-row focus on mobile drawer open) likewise `setRovingKey`s the row it focuses so its DOM focus and the tab-stop stay in sync (SF-4).

**Accepted-for-now APG caveats** (reviewer-noted): the inner per-row buttons (chevron, name, +, ‚úï, pin, swatch, kill) remain natively `Tab`-focusable rather than being subsumed under the single tree tab stop ‚Äî a deliberate keyboard-first choice (every control stays reachable) over strict APG purity. `role="tree"` currently wraps the server `<section>` wrappers (which are not themselves treeitems); a stricter structure would interpose `role="presentation"`, deferred. The implementation reuses the scroll half of the named list-scroll pattern but deliberately diverges from its `selectedIndex` numeric-state model in favor of the `rovingKey` string + DOM enumeration (see ¬ß Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern's third-consumer note).

### Collapsible Panels (Bottom-Aligned)

Two collapsible panels are pinned at the bottom of the sidebar below the scrollable session tree, above the server selector. Layout order top-to-bottom: server selector -> session list (`flex-1 overflow-y-auto`) -> Window panel -> Host panel. Combined height target ~140px when both open.

**CollapsiblePanel** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/collapsible-panel.tsx`) ‚Äî reusable wrapper used by both Window and Host panels. Props: `title` (string), `storageKey` (string for localStorage persistence), `defaultOpen` (boolean, default `true`), `children` (ReactNode), `headerRight` (ReactNode rendered inside the toggle button, right-aligned ‚Äî the StatusDot+name slot; clicking it toggles the panel), and `headerAction` (ReactNode rendered OUTSIDE the toggle button at the header's right edge, whose clicks are **stopped from toggling the panel** ‚Äî the purpose-built seam for an interactive control like the PANE-header refresh button, see WindowPanel below). Header is always visible: the title (`TypedLabel` ‚Äî the section-label typed-sweep hover treatment, `260703-5ilm`, see ¬ß Hover-Animation Vocabulary) + chevron (`&#x25B8;` U+25B8) that rotates 90 degrees on toggle via CSS `transform: rotate()` with `transition-transform duration-150`. Content area uses `max-height` transition (`duration-150 ease-in-out`) for smooth expand/collapse. `overflow: hidden` during transition, `visible` when fully expanded (accessibility). Collapse state persisted to `localStorage[storageKey]` on every toggle. Each panel has `border-t-[3px] border-border first:border-t-0` (a 3px structural seam ‚Äî see ¬ß Border-Width System ‚Äî so panels partition cleanly; the resizable drag handle is transparent by default, letting the next panel's 3px top border be the sole visible inter-panel line).

**WindowPanel** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/status-panel.tsx`) ‚Äî collapsible panel with `title="Pane"`, `storageKey="runkit-panel-window"`, `defaultOpen={true}`. **PANE-header refresh button** (`PaneRefreshButton`, `260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh`; **`idle | spinning | check` feedback state machine `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`**): passed as `CollapsiblePanel`'s `headerAction` (NOT `headerRight` ‚Äî `headerAction` is the seam whose clicks are stopped from toggling the panel; `headerRight` is the StatusDot+name slot inside the toggle button). It kicks a server-side on-demand refresh of BOTH PR pollers via `refreshStatus()` ‚Üí `POST /api/status/refresh` (see architecture.md ¬ß API Endpoints). **Feedback state machine (since `260715-nwla`)**: a single `useState<"idle" | "spinning" | "check">` (discriminated over the three mutually-exclusive visuals ‚Äî code-quality prefers this over booleans; consumed by tests via a `data-state` attribute) replaces the former `busy` bool. The button **spins from CLICK until the server-global `status-refresh` SSE completion event, NOT until the POST settles** (the POST 202s in ~ms while the real `gh` work runs 1‚Äì10s detached ‚Äî the jykd `busy`-cleared-in-`.finally()` behavior was a ~50ms blink and is REPLACED). It branches on the tri-state 202 body: `started`/`coalesced` ‚Üí `spinning` (no distinct coalesced visual ‚Äî the in-flight pass's one completion event clears both); `throttled` ‚Üí skip spinning and `flashCheck()` immediately ("already fresh"; no event will come). Completion is delivered via `useSessionContext().subscribeStatusRefresh` (subscribed ONLY while `spinning`, so an unrelated tab's completion doesn't flash an idle button); on fire it transitions `spinning ‚Üí check` (a brief post-completion checkmark, `REFRESH_CHECK_MS = 1000`, auto-reverting to `idle`, mirroring the same-file `COPY_FEEDBACK_MS` cadence). A **15s UI fallback** (`REFRESH_FALLBACK_MS = 15000`, well under the 60s `statusRefreshTimeout` backend bound) clears a stuck spinner if the event is missed ‚Äî **armed at click ENTRY, not inside `.then`** (a started/coalesced completion event can beat the POST settle, so arming in `.then` would restart a timer `flashCheck()` already cleared ‚Üí a phantom checkmark ~15s later). A `refreshStatus()` rejection (non-2xx via the shared `throwOnError`) is swallowed back to `idle` (clearing the fallback) so a network failure never leaves a stuck spinner. All timers are cleared on every transition and on unmount. Renders `animate-spin` on the `lucide` rotate-cw SVG in `spinning`, a checkmark SVG (`data-testid="pane-refresh-check"`, `text-accent`) in `check`, the static rotate-cw icon in `idle`; 14√ó14 SVGs, 24/30px touch target (`coarse:`), `data-testid="pane-refresh"`, `data-state`, `aria-label`/`title="Refresh PR status"`. Follows the top-bar/board `RefreshButton` **CRT-glint** vocabulary (`rk-glint` ‚Äî ¬ß Hover-Animation Vocabulary). It **renders whenever the PANE header renders, including with no window selected** ‚Äî the refresh is server-global (both pollers are viewer-wide), so gating on window selection would add nothing. Best-effort/fire-and-forget: server-side coalescing + a min-interval throttle make it safe to over-fire (the fallback still clears any spinner). Scope-honest: labeled around PR/status freshness (the other PANE registers out/agt/fab are already fresh within ~7.5s). The `subscribeStatusRefresh` context seam it consumes is a `Set`-of-handlers ref + `fireStatusRefresh` fired from BOTH the per-server pool ES block AND the `?metrics=1` metrics-stream ES block in `session-context.tsx`, mirroring `subscribeBoardOrder`/`fireBoardOrder` (the event is host-global, so both streams carry it). Palette parity: the `PR: Refresh Status` action (¬ß Command Palette `PR: Refresh Status` action) is unchanged ‚Äî a pure POST kick with no shared button state to hook. The `headerRight` slot renders `<StatusDot win={win} /> {win.name}` (in a `flex items-center gap-1.5 truncate text-text-secondary font-mono` span) ‚Äî the unified status dot (see ¬ß Status Dot) leads the header so the window's status (palette-v3 two-family ladder + waiting halo, since `260706-y1ar`) stays glanceable even when the panel is collapsed; since `260616-37ub-status-dot-tooltip` hovering/focusing the dot opens the custom `StatusDotTip` hover-card (the native `title` was dropped ‚Äî see ¬ß Status Dot). Displays the identity rows `tmx` (pane index + ID), `cwd` (shortened path), `git` (branch), then the **four orthogonal signal registers** `out` (L0 activity + elapsed) / `agt` (L1 `agentState` + duration) / `fab` (L2 change ¬∑ stage ¬∑ displayState) / `PR` (L3 derived PR, ungated) ‚Äî the 3-char register view since `260706-y1ar`, prefixes normalized to `out`/`agt` by `260706-4h26` (¬ß Pane panel four-register view). The L1 `agt` register (`getAgentLine`) is `null` when `!win.agentState`, else `${agentState} ${agentIdleDuration}`; a blocked pane shows `waiting <dur>` (the pierce rule: it shows independently of the flowing-output L0 register). No window selected -> "No window selected" in secondary text. `StatusPanel` is exported as a deprecated alias for backward compatibility.

**Copyable rows**: The `tmx`, `cwd`, `git`, and `fab` rows are interactive `<button type="button">` elements that copy their underlying value to the clipboard on click or keyboard activation (Enter/Space). Copy values per row:

| Row | Copy value | Source |
|-----|------------|--------|
| `tmx` | Pane ID (e.g., `%5`) | `activePane.paneId` |
| `cwd` | Full unshortened path (e.g., `/home/sahil/code/run-kit`) | `activePane.cwd ?? win.worktreePath` |
| `git` | Branch name | `activePane.gitBranch` |
| `fab` | Change ID (e.g., `lc2q`) | `fabChange.id` (parsed from `win.fabChange`) |

Non-interactive rows: `run` (process-only, when no fab state) and `agt` remain plain text ‚Äî no hover affordance, no focus ring, no copy behavior. Rows with empty values (`tmx` with empty pane ID, `git` when no branch) are also non-interactive.

**`cwd` deleted-directory marker** (`260614-nj74-sidebar-cwd-deleted-marker`): when the active pane's `cwdMissing` flag is set (the backend `os.Stat` found the pane's cwd no longer exists ‚Äî typically an archived change whose worktree was deleted out from under a still-live tmux window), the `cwd` row keeps the shortened stale path as a breadcrumb but recolors the whole value `text-red-400` and appends a `(deleted)` tag (`data-testid="cwd-deleted"`); the row `title` reads `<full-path> (no longer exists)`. The choice was **color over dimming** ‚Äî a vanished cwd is more notable, not less, so it reuses the panel's existing failure-red token (the same `text-red-400` the `pr` fail-ish row uses) rather than the dimmed `text-text-secondary` of a normal path. The row stays copyable (still copies the stale full path). The marker is **self-healing**: it only shows while tmux still reports the deleted path; once the shell's cwd recovers to a real directory the backend stat succeeds, `cwdMissing` clears, and the row reverts to its normal style.
