This is the minimal honest signal ‚Äî run-kit does NOT close or rename the orphaned tmux window (Constitution ¬ßVI forbids tearing down tmux windows). Backend derivation: `architecture.md` ¬ß `internal/sessions` (`resolveCwdMissing`).

**Register icons** (since `260706-y1ar` the pane panel is the four-register view ‚Äî ¬ß Pane panel four-register view; these inline spinner glyphs lead their register line, `aria-hidden`): `BrailleSnake` (`braille-snake.tsx`, `‚£æ‚£Ω‚£ª‚¢ø‚°ø‚£ü‚£Ø‚£∑`, 80ms) ‚Üí the `out` (L0) register; `StarTwinkle` (`star-twinkle.tsx`) ‚Üí the `agt` (L1) register; `ClockSpinner` (`clock-spinner.tsx`) ‚Üí the `fab` (L2) register; the L3 `PR` register uses the Nerd Font git-pull-request glyph (`ICON_CLASS`). Each follows the same pattern: `useState(0)` frame counter + `useEffect` with `setInterval` + cleanup on unmount, rendered as `<span aria-hidden="true">`. *(`BlockPulse` (`block-pulse.tsx`) is now UNUSED in source ‚Äî it drove the former `run` line's active heartbeat, which the register rewrite replaced; the file remains, a deletion candidate.)*

**Inline feedback**: After a successful copy, the row's prefix label swaps to `copied ‚úì` for 1000ms, then reverts. A single `copiedRow` state variable tracks which row was last copied ‚Äî only one row shows feedback at a time. Clicking a different row immediately moves the indicator.

**Hover affordance**: Interactive rows render `cursor: pointer` and a subtle background tint (`bg-bg-inset` or equivalent) on hover.

**Keyboard accessibility**: Button elements have visible focus state (outline/ring) and are keyboard-activatable (Enter/Space). Styling is reset to preserve the panel's compact plain-text aesthetic ‚Äî no default button chrome (padding, border, background removed in rest state).

**Text-selection guard**: The click handler checks `window.getSelection()?.toString()` ‚Äî if the user has an active text selection (e.g., from drag-selecting text), the copy action is suppressed, preserving native text-selection UX.

**Clipboard utility**: Copy operations use `copyToClipboard()` from `app/frontend/src/lib/clipboard.ts` ‚Äî see [Clipboard Utility](#clipboard-utility).

**HostPanel** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/host-panel.tsx`) ‚Äî the sidebar host-metrics view inside a `CollapsiblePanel` with `title="Host"`, `storageKey="runkit-panel-host"`, `defaultOpen={true}`. Accepts `metrics: MetricsSnapshot | null` and `isConnected: boolean` props. It owns only the chrome ‚Äî the hostname header (truncated, on the left) + SSE indicator (green `bg-accent-green` / gray `bg-text-secondary` dot on the right, connection health) ‚Äî and the `!metrics` "No metrics" branch; the metric ROWS are delegated to the shared `HostMetrics` component.

**Shared `HostMetrics` component** (`app/frontend/src/components/host-metrics.tsx`, `260701-vshd-cockpit-host-console-home`) ‚Äî the metric-row rendering extracted from `HostPanel` into a single **layout-agnostic** presentational component `HostMetrics({ metrics }: { metrics: MetricsSnapshot })`, so the two host views (sidebar `HostPanel` + the `/` HOST HEALTH zone) stay visually consistent. It ALWAYS receives a non-null snapshot ‚Äî the caller owns the surrounding layout chrome AND the `!metrics` empty state. It exports the `formatUptime`/`formatDisk` helpers (moved out of `host-panel.tsx`) and holds the `MemoryLine`/`LoadLine` sub-components. Rows (all `text-xs font-mono`), rendered via `lib/sparkline.ts` + `lib/gauge.ts`:

1. **CPU sparkline** ‚Äî `cpu` label + braille sparkline (`text-accent`) + current percentage (`text-text-primary`). Sparkline rendered by `sparkline()` from `@/lib/sparkline.ts`
2. **Memory gauge** (`MemoryLine`) ‚Äî `mem` label + filled/empty block gauge + `formatMemory` `used/total` text. Gauge color: green < 70%, yellow 70-90%, red > 90%. Uses `gaugeBar()`, `gaugeColor()`, `formatMemory()` from `@/lib/gauge.ts`. A `ResizeObserver` measures the container to size the gauge char-count responsively
3. **Disk + uptime** ‚Äî `dsk` label + `formatDisk` `used/totalG` + ` ¬∑ up ` + `formatUptime` (`Nd Nh` or `Nh Nm` if < 1 day). All `text-text-secondary`
4. **Load averages** (`LoadLine`) ‚Äî `ld` label + three percentages (1/5/15 min) normalized as `(load / cpuCount) * 100`. Any percentage > 90% renders in `text-red-500`

Rejected: duplicating the ~120 lines across the two host surfaces ‚Äî drift risk. `DRY` extraction is easily reversed (Design Decision, `260701-vshd`).

### HOST HEALTH Zone on `/` (Host-page host-console home)

Since `260701-vshd-cockpit-host-console-home`, `HostOverviewPage` (`app/frontend/src/components/host-overview-page.tsx`, route `/`) renders a **HOST HEALTH** zone ABOVE the tmux-server tile grid, inside the scroll container (`div.flex-1.min-h-0.overflow-y-auto`, which since `260702-6m46` carries `pt-6` so the gap below the pinned TopBar matches the `mb-6` inter-section rhythm). This makes `/` ‚Äî the only route that is about the BOX, not a session ‚Äî a machine console. Since `260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar` added the BOARDS zone, the zones render in top-to-bottom order **HOST HEALTH ‚Üí BOARDS ‚Üí TMUX SERVERS ‚Üí SERVICES** (each an uppercase-labelled `<section>`; the server-tile grid gained a "Tmux Servers" heading + inline server count, and SERVICES moved to last, after the tiles ‚Äî `260701-5d0z-service-tiles-host-console`; see ¬ß BOARDS Zone, ¬ß SERVICES Zone on `/`). Since `260715-zs1y` a page-level `Host Overview` `SectionHeading` heads the scroll container above these zones (¬ß Page Overview Headings). Each zone heading is a `[ LABEL‚ñä ]‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ` `SectionHeading` (¬ß Section Heading); the former `[ cockpit ]` `PageHeading` above them was REMOVED by `260704-pr0p` (the Host page's identity is the solo `Host` heading in the top-bar center cell; the `[ cockpit ]` label predates the `260715-zs1y` rename). Read-only awareness view; nothing here mutates host state (Constitution IV).

- The zone (`<section aria-label="Host health">`) shows a `<SectionHeading label="Host Health" className="mb-2" />` (¬ß Section Heading ‚Äî since `260704-pr0p`, replacing the former bare uppercase `<h2>` + side-text idiom), then the live `hostname` (from `useHostMetrics()`) in the zone BODY as a `text-xs text-text-secondary font-mono truncate mb-2` line right below the heading (NOT in the SectionHeading `side` slot, which stays empty on Host-page zones ‚Äî `260704-pr0p` SHOULD-FIX 1 restored the hostname to the body after an initial version parked it in `side`; `260702-6m46` had earlier demoted it to secondary mono), then the shared `HostMetrics` component (CPU sparkline+current, memory gauge, load 1/5/15 normalized, disk used/total, uptime).
- It consumes **`useHostMetrics()`** (the server-independent hook ‚Äî see architecture.md ¬ß Server-independent host-metrics subscription), NOT `useMetrics()` (which is `null` on `/` ‚Äî there is no `currentServer`). Metrics update on each `event: metrics` tick; on a bare `/` with zero servers attached, freshness is the fast ~2.5s (`legacyPollInterval`) cadence, because `safetyIntervalEffective` treats a sentinel-only slice as the exception and returns the fast interval rather than the 12s backstop (the on-connect cached snapshot renders immediately) ‚Äî see architecture.md ¬ß API Layer `/api/sessions/stream`.
- **Empty state**: when `useHostMetrics()` is `null` (pre-first-tick, or a non-Linux zero-valued host), the zone renders a graceful `No metrics` affordance (never a blank/broken layout), mirroring `HostPanel`'s `!metrics` branch.
- The server-tile grid below (create / open / count) and the `+ New Server` affordance are untouched and still function. **Infra-server name de-emphasis** (`260705-uh8f-deemphasize-infra-servers`): each tile's name `<div>` renders `text-text-secondary` (instead of `text-text-primary`) when `isInfraServer(name)` ‚Äî the same greyed-not-disabled treatment as the Sidebar Server tile; the tile stays fully clickable/attachable. See ¬ß Infra-server de-emphasis.

### BOARDS Zone on `/` (Host page)

Since `260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar`, `HostOverviewPage` renders a **BOARDS** zone (`<section aria-label="Boards">`) BETWEEN HOST HEALTH and TMUX SERVERS. A board aggregates windows across tmux servers, so the box-level Host page (not any single tmux Server page) is its list's natural home; it sits above TMUX SERVERS per the page's general‚Üíspecific flow.

- **Data source**: the existing **`useBoards()`** hook (`plain /api/boards` fetch + the shared SSE pool ‚Äî NO new API/endpoint; the same hook `board-page.tsx` and the sidebar consume). Returns `{ boards, isLoading }`.
- **Heading row**: a `<SectionHeading label="Boards" className="mb-2" />` (¬ß Section Heading ‚Äî since `260704-pr0p`, replacing the former bare uppercase `<h2>` + side-text idiom). The board count / `loading‚Ä¶` is NOT in the SectionHeading `side` slot (reserved for the server-view stats) ‚Äî it stays in the zone BODY, a `text-xs text-text-secondary font-mono mb-2` line right below the heading (`loading‚Ä¶` before the first fetch via `isLoading`, else `{N} board(s)`).
- **Tiles**: one `<button>` per board (same tile idiom as the server tiles ‚Äî `bg-bg-card border border-border rounded p-4 hover:border-text-secondary min-h-[60px]`) showing the board name + `{N} pin(s)`; clicking navigates to `/board/$name`. **Drag-reorderable** (`260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`): tiles render `orderedBoards` from the shared `useBoardListReorder` hook (same instance seam as the sidebar) with `getTileProps(b.name)` spread onto each and the dragged tile dimmed `opacity-50` ‚Äî see ¬ß Board-list drag reorder.
- **Always visible**: the section renders even with zero boards ‚Äî the empty state shows the sidebar's "Pin a window to start a board" hint (mirroring `BoardsSection`) instead of the section appearing/vanishing with the first/last board.
- **Not a shared component**: the tile markup is NOT shared with the sidebar `boards-section.tsx` (a parallel surface; the sidebar section still drives the actual sidebar). The un-shared board-tile markup was flagged as a Should-fix duplicated-logic note at review ‚Äî accepted for v1.

### SERVICES Zone on `/` (Host-page host-console home)

Since `260701-5d0z-service-tiles-host-console`, `HostOverviewPage` renders a **SERVICES** zone (`<section aria-label="Services">`) as the LAST zone, below the TMUX SERVERS tile grid, inside the same scroll container. It surfaces the host's listening TCP **ports** as tiles ‚Äî a listening port is a HOST property (owned by no tmux window/session), so `/` (the box-level console) is its home, mirroring the HOST HEALTH rationale. **`260715-vfcz-passive-ports-process-attribution` deleted the ambient HTTP probe and superseded the `260703-8y2a-cockpit-http-only-services` HTTP-only (probe-backed) contract**: the backend (`internal/ports`) now passively enumerates and broadcasts **ALL** listening ports (procfs on Linux, lsof on darwin) with best-effort process attribution on BOTH platforms ‚Äî no probing, no HTTP filter (see architecture.md ¬ß `internal/ports`). A tile is therefore **not guaranteed to speak HTTP**; the frontend does NO protocol guessing and applies no client-side denylist. Read-only awareness view; the only action opens a port's UI in a tmux window (Constitution IV ‚Äî nothing mutates host state directly).

- **Data source**: **`useHostServices()`** (its own `HostServicesContext`, separate from `HostMetricsContext` so the ~2.5s services stream doesn't cascade re-renders into metrics-only consumers). It rides the SAME server-independent broadcast as host metrics ‚Äî the `event: services` frame arrives on every stream (the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream on a bare `/`, and each per-server stream's fan-out), deduped on the raw payload string (`applyHostServices`). Returns `[]` (never null) before the first tick, so consumers map over it unconditionally. See architecture.md ¬ß API Layer `/api/sessions/stream` (`event: services`) and ¬ß Server-independent host-metrics subscription.
- **Tiles**: each `Service` (from `@/types` ‚Äî `{ port, process?, pid? }`) renders a row keyed by `svc.port` showing `:{port}` (mono) + the optional `process` name. **Process attribution is best-effort on BOTH platforms** (`260715-vfcz` ‚Äî "Linux is port-only" is superseded): macOS populates `process`/`pid` from lsof; Linux joins lsof attribution onto its procfs port set and populates them where lsof can attribute the port, leaving them absent (bare tile) for ports lsof can't see (e.g. root-owned `sshd :22` under a non-root lsof) ‚Äî see architecture.md ¬ß `internal/ports`. Empty state: a graceful `No services` affordance when the list is empty (pre-first-tick, nothing listening, or an unsupported platform where the collector returns `[]` ‚Äî Windows/BSD; macOS and Linux both enumerate).
- **"Open in window" action** (`handleOpenInWindow`): opens the port's UI in an `@rk_type=iframe` tmux window via the existing `/proxy/{port}/` reverse proxy (`createWindow(server, session, "port-{port}", undefined, "iframe", "/proxy/{port}/")` ‚Äî the `rkType`/`rkUrl` args become the `@rk_type`/`@rk_url` window options), then navigates to `/$server` (the new window surfaces via SSE). The window **name** is `port-{port}`, NOT `:{port}` ‚Äî tmux rejects colons and periods in window names (`validate.ValidateName`); the tile still *displays* `:{port}`. Since `/` is server-less, it resolves a **target (server, session)**: `servers[0]` + that server's first session from the SSE cache (`sessionsByServer`), else an authoritative `getSessions()` fetch (the per-server stream is usually not attached yet on a fresh `/` load, so the cache can be empty even when sessions exist ‚Äî fetching avoids a duplicate-name 500 on `new-session`), else an instant `"services"` session created on the fly (`createSession`). An `openingRef` guard debounces a double-click into a single create flow. **Note** (`260705-uh8f`): `servers[0]` now benefits from the infra-last sort applied in `session-context.tsx` `fetchServers` (see ¬ß Infra-server de-emphasis) ‚Äî a real workspace is preferred over `rk-daemon` as the "first-listed server" target, consistent with the de-emphasis intent.
- **Button gated SOLELY on server existence**: the "Open in window" button is `disabled` with `title="Create a server first"` ONLY when `servers.length === 0` (there is no target to host the iframe window); otherwise it is enabled regardless of port number. The tile still renders in the disabled case.
- **Well-known-port de-emphasis** (`260715-vfcz`): with the SERVICES zone now showing ALL listening ports, well-known/system ports (`port < 1024`, the reserved range ‚Äî `sshd:22`, `smtp:25`, ‚Ä¶) are visually de-emphasized, mirroring the `isInfraServer` server-tile treatment: their `:{port}` renders grey (`text-text-secondary` instead of `text-text-primary`) and they sort **last as a class**. `isWellKnownPort(port) = port < 1024`; the `orderedServices` `useMemo` partitions `hostServices` into regular vs. well-known, sorts each sub-group by port ascending, and concatenates (regular first) ‚Äî so regular tiles keep their port-ascending order and well-known tiles trail. **Presentation-only, applied at render in `host-overview-page.tsx`**: the backend snapshot stays port-sorted; this is a frontend concern (parallel to the `session-context.tsx` infra-last server sort ‚Äî see ¬ß Infra-server de-emphasis). Every tile, well-known or not, still renders with its "Open in window" button.
- **No HTTP gate anywhere (`NON_HTTP_PORTS` / `isLikelyHttpPort` stay DELETED)**: `260703-8y2a-cockpit-http-only-services` removed the client-side HTTP-likely heuristic (`NON_HTTP_PORTS` denylist, `isLikelyHttpPort(port)`, the disabled branch, the `"Not a web service"` tooltip, the `handleOpenInWindow` guard), and `260715-vfcz` **keeps that deletion** ‚Äî no denylist or HTTP gate returns, client or server. The `8y2a` model where the backend probed and broadcast "only HTTP responders" (so every tile "provably spoke HTTP") is **superseded**: the backend broadcasts ALL listening ports and does no probing. A tile is therefore not guaranteed to be a web service; **opening a non-HTTP port yields a user-initiated failed iframe ‚Äî the iframe load IS the on-demand probe** (visible and harmless; there is no ambient probe). The empty state stays `No services` (now meaning "no listening ports"). `types.ts` `Service`/`ServicesSnapshot` are unchanged (no `http:` flag ‚Äî there is no HTTP verdict).

### Color Tinting ‚Äî Owned Palette + Axis Split

Session rows, window rows, and server tiles support an optional color assignment that applies a full-width background tint. The palette is an **owned set of 10 fixed OKLCH hue families adapted to the active theme**: each family has a stable hue angle, and hue identity survives theme switches (a window labeled "orange" reads orange on every theme). The row's visual channels are split so labeling and selection never collide: **hue = label**, **tint depth = selection**, **left-gutter marker = an independent label axis** (¬ß Left-Gutter Marker).

**Owned hue families** (`themes.ts` `HUE_FAMILIES`): 10 families in stable display order, each `{ name, hue, legacy, neutral? }`. Hue angles are placed non-uniformly ‚Äî tight through the discriminable red‚Üíamber region, the large gap parked in teal‚Üíblue where human hue discrimination is weakest: red 25¬∞, orange 55¬∞, amber 90¬∞, olive 120¬∞, green 150¬∞, teal 185¬∞, blue 250¬∞, purple 290¬∞, magenta 330¬∞, slate 250¬∞ (`neutral`). `PICKER_COLOR_VALUES` is the display-ordered list of the 10 **family names** (the form new writes intend). `FAMILY_BY_NAME` / `FAMILY_BY_LEGACY` are the two lookup maps.

**Theme adaptation (full adoption)**: `themeColorStats(palette) ‚Üí { L, C }` computes the mean OKLab lightness and mean chroma over `palette.ansi[1..6]`, with a chroma floor `THEME_CHROMA_FLOOR = 0.05` (near-monochrome themes stay distinguishable). A family's source hex = `oklchToHexInGamut(L_theme, C_theme, family.hue)`; slate uses a near-neutral chroma `min(C_theme √ó 0.2, 0.025)`. `colorValueToHex(value, palette)` resolves any stored value (family name OR legacy alias) to this adopted hex, returning `null` when it maps to no family.

**OKLCH ‚Üí in-gamut hex, chroma-reduction not channel-clamp**: `oklchToHex(L, C, hueDeg)` converts polar chroma/hue to OKLab (`a = C¬∑cos h`, `b = C¬∑sin h`) then reuses `oklabToHex`. `oklchInGamut(L, C, hueDeg)` reports whether the triple maps inside sRGB without any channel being clamped, reusing the shared `oklabToLinearRgb(c)` matrix helper (extracted so its 18 coefficients stay in lockstep with `oklabToHex` ‚Äî both consume it). `oklchToHexInGamut(L, C, hueDeg)` brings an out-of-gamut triple in by **reducing chroma stepwise** (`GAMUT_REDUCE_FACTOR = 0.92`, `GAMUT_REDUCE_MAX_STEPS = 20`) ‚Äî L and hue are preserved; sRGB channel-clamping is never used because it shifts hue and would defeat the stable-hue goal.

**Legacy color values resolve 1:1 to families (zero migration)**: stored color values remain the **legacy vocabulary end-to-end** ‚Äî the backend stores and validates only numeric/blend descriptors (`"4"` / `"1+3"`), and family names are frontend-side read aliases. The 1:1 map: red‚Üê`1`, orange‚Üê`1+3`, amber‚Üê`3`, olive‚Üê`1+2`, green‚Üê`2`, teal‚Üê`6`, blue‚Üê`4`, purple‚Üê`1+4`, magenta‚Üê`5`, slate‚Üê`3+4`. `resolveFamily(value)` accepts a family name OR a legacy descriptor (normalized via the file-private `normalizeLegacy`, mirroring the backend `NormalizeColorValue` rule) and returns the same family for both. `parseColorValue`/`formatColorValue` (family name form) accept both vocabularies. `familyToLegacy(name)` maps a picker family name to its legacy descriptor for the **write seam** (below); it is idempotent ‚Äî an already-legacy or unrecognized input passes through unchanged.

**Pre-blended row tints, dual-keyed**: `computeRowTints(palette) ‚Üí Map<string, RowTint>` pre-computes the three blended state hexes for every family, keyed under **BOTH vocabularies** ‚Äî the family name AND its legacy descriptor point at the *same* tint entry ‚Äî plus the `"8"` uncolored-selected sentinel. Both keys are populated because consumers (`window-row`/`session-row`/`server-panel`) look up the RAW stored value and the backend emits legacy forms, so a family-name-only map would miss every pre-existing colored row. Each family's adopted source hex (`colorValueToHex`) is saturated √ó1.5 (`TINT_SATURATE_FACTOR`) before blending into the theme background at three ratios:

| State | Constant | Saturated-source ratio |
|-------|----------|------------------------|
| Base | `TINT_BASE_RATIO` | 14% |
| Hover | `TINT_HOVER_RATIO` | 22% |
| Selected | `TINT_SELECTED_RATIO` | 40% |

Selection is carried by tint **depth** alone (the former 4px left border is gone ‚Äî ¬ß Row Anatomy), so the selected ratio is 40%. The uncolored-selected gray sentinel (`"8"`, `UNCOLORED_SELECTED_ANSI`/`UNCOLORED_SELECTED_KEY`) is NOT saturated (gray is near-zero chroma) and uses the deeper `UNCOLORED_SELECTED_RATIO = 0.5` so it beats the `bg-card/50` hover. Each state gets its own concrete hex ‚Äî no stacked transparent layers. The `RowTint` type (`{ base, hover, selected }`) is exported. Hover is applied imperatively via `onMouseEnter`/`onMouseLeave` style mutations to avoid CSS-specificity issues with dynamic backgrounds.

**Contrast-guardrailed borders** (`computeRowBorders(palette, category) ‚Üí Map<string, string>`): each family's adopted source hex passed through a WCAG contrast guardrail, dual-keyed (family name + legacy descriptor + `"8"` sentinel) exactly like `computeRowTints`. `adjustBorderForContrast(border, bg, isDark, BORDER_MIN_CONTRAST)` nudges **only the OKLab lightness L** (lighten on dark themes, darken on light) in `0.03` steps until the border clears `BORDER_MIN_CONTRAST = 3.0` against the background or hits a 24-step cap; **hue and chroma are preserved** so the color keeps its identity. Window rows no longer use these for a selection border (removed in the axis split); **server tiles** still use them for their stripe/edge, and **the marker gutter uses them as its guarded family color** (¬ß Left-Gutter Marker). `sidebar/index.tsx` computes `rowTints` + `rowBorders` once per theme via `useMemo` and threads them to `WindowRow`/`ServerPanel`.

**OKLab + WCAG color-math helpers** (`themes.ts`): `hexToOklab` / `oklabToHex` (Bj√∂rn Ottosson 2020 coefficients; `oklabToHex` and `oklchInGamut` share the `oklabToLinearRgb` matrix helper), the sRGB‚Üîlinear `srgbToLinear` gamma step, `relativeLuminance` (WCAG 2.x) and `contrastRatio(hex1, hex2)` (1..21), and `adjustBorderForContrast`. OKLab is the chosen lightness/distinctness space; WCAG is the separate legibility standard.

**SwatchPopover** (`app/frontend/src/components/swatch-popover.tsx`): shared component used by the command-palette color actions and the per-row hover indicator. Renders the **10 families** from `PICKER_COLOR_VALUES` in a compact 3-column grid plus a "Clear" action (**11 keyboard-navigable items** ‚Äî `totalItems = colorCount + 1`, `clearIndex` past the last swatch). Props are STRINGS: `selectedColor?: string`, `onSelect(color | null)`, `onClose()`. **Write seam** ‚Äî every emit funnels through `familyToLegacy` (the file-private `emit` callback: `onSelect(familyToLegacy(value))`), so a picked family name is stored as its legacy descriptor (`"orange"` ‚Üí `"1+3"`); `null` (Clear) passes through untouched. This keeps stored values in the legacy vocabulary end-to-end ‚Äî the backend validators (`ValidateColorValue`) accept only numeric/blend forms, so a raw family-name write would 400. Each swatch's fill is its `computeRowTints` `selected` tint (falling back to `colorValueToHex` then `theme.palette.foreground`); the selected swatch is matched by `resolveFamily(selectedColor)?.name` so a legacy-stored value highlights the right family. Arrow-key nav reaches every swatch and lands on Clear; lazy-loaded via `React.lazy()`; dismisses on selection, Escape, or outside click.

**Hover indicator**: on hover, a small palette icon appears at the row's trailing edge; clicking opens the SwatchPopover inline. Visible on hover (desktop) or always on touch (`coarse:opacity-100`).

**Command palette actions**: "Session: Set Color" / "Window: Set Color" open the SwatchPopover; every write path ‚Äî window rows, session rows, server tiles, palette "Set Color" ‚Äî flows through the `familyToLegacy` write seam so stored values stay legacy. Selecting "Clear" sends `null`.

**Storage**: stored color values are the **legacy descriptor** (`"4"` / `"1+3"`); frontend wire types are `WindowInfo.color?: string` and `ProjectSession.sessionColor?: string` (`src/types.ts`). Window and session colors are ephemeral tmux user options (`@color` per window, `@session_color` per session ‚Äî survive session lifetime, not tmux-server restarts), set via `setWindowColor`/`setSessionColor` in `client.ts`. Server colors persist in `~/.rk/settings.yaml`. **No color storage/API/backend migration** ‚Äî the owned-palette rewrite is frontend-only for color. See architecture.md ¬ß Data Model for the backend storage/validation contract.

### Row Anatomy ‚Äî Selection & Board-Pin Cues (`window-row.tsx`)

The window row's visual channels are orthogonal: **hue = label** (family tint), **tint depth = selection**, **left gutter = the independent marker axis** (below). Selection and the board-pin cue are borderless ‚Äî the sidebar window row carries no left accent border.

**Selection = tint depth + typography, borderless**: a selected colored row deepens to the 40% family tint (`rowTints.get(color).selected`); an uncolored selected row uses the gray sentinel's deeper 0.5 tint. The name goes `font-medium` + `text-text-primary`. There is **no** left accent border on selection.

**Board-pin active-board cue on the pin glyph** (not a border): the persistent filled pin glyph ‚Äî already `opacity-100` + filled whenever the window is pinned to any board (`isPinnedToAny`) ‚Äî renders **accent-colored** when the row is pinned to the currently-viewed board (`isPinnedToActiveBoard`), and monochrome `text-text-secondary` otherwise. `isPinnedToActiveBoard` implies `isPinnedToAny`, so the accent branch is always the persistent (never hover-gated) glyph. This is load-bearing since link-based pinning (`260718-co9z`) keeps pinned rows visible in SESSIONS: the cue distinguishes "pinned to the board you're viewing" from "pinned to some board" with zero new elements, keeping the left gutter single-purpose (the marker). See ¬ß Active-Board Highlight in Sessions Tree, ¬ß Sidebar Pin Icon on Window Rows.

### Left-Gutter Marker (`window-row.tsx` `MarkerGutter`)

An independent 4-state label axis on the left edge of each window row, orthogonal to hue and selection. Semantics are deliberately unnamed in the UI ‚Äî the states are abstract (todo/doing/done for one user, priority for another).

**4 states, click to cycle**: empty ‚Üí dotted (3px dotted border) ‚Üí solid (3px solid) ‚Üí double (6px double), cycled on click and wrapping back to empty. `themes.ts` owns `MARKER_STATES = ["", "dotted", "solid", "double"]`, `MarkerState`, and `nextMarkerState(current)` (an unrecognized/absent value is treated as empty, so the first click lands on `dotted`). The marker renders in the row's guarded family color (`rowBorders.get(color)`, gray for uncolored rows) via `markerBorderStyle`. Markers are available on **all** rows including uncolored ones (gated only on a present `onMarkerChange` handler + non-ghost + a `server`).

**Gutter mechanics**: the gutter is an absolute `z-20` sibling (`GUTTER_WIDTH = 14`px, full row height) overlaying the left edge; the button content is padded clear with `pl-[18px]` so the leading StatusDot + text start past the gutter (the dot keeps its own hover-card and click-to-select). A gutter click `stopPropagation`s so it does not select the row, and coexists with drag-reorder.

**Two-stage hover + `cell` cursor**: hovering the row fills the gutter to ~20% family color; hovering the gutter itself steps to ~30% (via `color-mix`) and ghosts a faint (`opacity-40`) preview of the NEXT marker state. The gutter uses `cursor: cell` (`cursor-[cell]`).

**Touch (coarse) ‚Äî inert; palette is the marker path**: the gutter is `coarse:pointer-events-none` (no tap target, no accidental cycle on scroll), but its marker STILL renders on touch so state stays visible. It carries no `role="button"`/`tabIndex`/key handler ‚Äî the `Window: Cycle Marker` command-palette action is the sole keyboard/touch path (Constitution V; `aria-label="Cycle window marker"` on the gutter for AT). See ¬ß Marker plumbing.

**Marker plumbing**: `WindowInfo.marker?: string` (`src/types.ts`) carries the state from the `@rk_marker` window option (architecture.md). `setWindowMarker(server, windowId, marker | null)` in `client.ts` delegates to `setWindowOptions({"@rk_marker": ...})` (empty/`null` clears). `sidebar/index.tsx` owns an `onMarkerChange` handler (mirroring `onColorChange`), prop-drilled through `ServerGroup` to `WindowRow`; the row computes `nextMarkerState(marker)` on a gutter click and calls it. The `Window: Cycle Marker` palette action (`app.tsx` `windowActions`, alongside `Window: Set Color`) resolves the current window and calls the same `nextMarkerState ‚Üí setWindowMarker` path. **Scope: window rows only** ‚Äî session rows and server tiles get the owned-palette tints but no marker.

### Easter Egg ‚Äî Double-Marker Scanlines (`globals.css` `.rk-scanlines`)

A window row whose marker is `double` gets a static CRT scanline overlay across its full width, making `double` the one marker state readable from across the sidebar. Selecting such a row brings the scanlines alive.

**Static scanlines**: `.rk-scanlines::before` paints a `repeating-linear-gradient(to bottom, {marker color}@14% 0 1px, transparent 1px 3px)` reading the family color from the `--rk-marker-color` custom property (set on the row when `double`). The overlay is a **dedicated absolutely-positioned inner element** (`absolute inset-0 z-[5] overflow-hidden pointer-events-none`), NOT the row root ‚Äî `overflow-hidden` on the root would clip the row's `top-full` pin/color popovers, so clipping lives on the overlay and the root stays free to overflow. The overlay sits above the tint/button background (`z-5`), below the `z-10` icon cluster and `z-20` gutter. Pure static CSS ‚Äî it does not touch the status pyramid's animation channel (the waiting halo stays unambiguous).

**Selected + double retro animation**: when a double-marker row is ALSO selected, the class `rk-scanlines-crawl` is added, animating a slow downward crawl of the gradient period (`@keyframes rk-scanline-crawl`, `background-position-y` 0 ‚Üí 3px, 1.4s linear infinite) plus an occasional CRT refresh band ‚Äî a soft ~12px gradient band in the marker color rolling top‚Üíbottom via `::after` (`@keyframes rk-scanline-band`, 3.4s cycle with a rest phase, `pointer-events: none`). Static again when deselected.

**Reduced motion**: inside the existing `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)` block, `.rk-scanlines-crawl::before { animation: none }` and `.rk-scanlines-crawl::after { animation: none; display: none }` ‚Äî the crawl and band are fully zeroed (static scanlines only, band hidden). The base rules PRECEDE the reduced-motion block so its equal-specificity overrides win by source order, mirroring the `rk-waiting-halo`/`rk-waiting-seam` discipline.

### Braille Sparkline Renderer

`app/frontend/src/lib/sparkline.ts` ‚Äî converts an array of float values (0-100 range) into a Unicode braille sparkline string. Uses 8 vertical levels from the U+2800-U+28FF braille range filling bottom-to-top: `‚£Ä‚£Ñ‚£§‚£¶‚£∂‚£∑‚£æ‚£ø` (level 0 = `‚£Ä`, level 7 = `‚£ø`). Values linearly interpolated across 8 levels. Zero-filled buffer renders as repeated `‚£Ä`. Exported as `sparkline(samples: number[]): string`.

### Memory Gauge Renderer

`app/frontend/src/lib/gauge.ts` ‚Äî utilities for the memory gauge visualization:
- `gaugeBar(ratio: number): string` ‚Äî builds a filled/empty block string (`‚ñà` filled, `‚ñë` empty) from a 0-1 ratio. Fixed width of 10 characters
- `gaugeColor(percent: number): string` ‚Äî returns a Tailwind color class: `text-green-500` (< 70%), `text-yellow-500` (70-90%), `text-red-500` (> 90%)
- `formatBytes(bytes: number): string` ‚Äî compact human-readable size (`3.1G`, `512M`, `128K`)
- `formatMemory(used: number, total: number): string` ‚Äî compact `used/total` string (e.g., `3.1G/8G`)

### Clipboard Utility

`app/frontend/src/lib/clipboard.ts` ‚Äî shared `copyToClipboard(text: string): Promise<void>` function extracted from `terminal-client.tsx`. Primary path uses `navigator.clipboard.writeText()`; fallback uses `document.execCommand('copy')` for non-secure contexts (HTTP). Signature and behavior preserved from the original. All callers (terminal copy, Pane panel row copy) import from this module. Introduced to decouple sidebar copy operations from the terminal-client module.

CWD display (line 1) uses `shortenPath()` to shorten the active pane's `cwd` (falls back to `worktreePath`):
- Home substitution: `/home/<user>/‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `~/‚Ä¶`, `/Users/<user>/‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `~/‚Ä¶`, `/root/‚Ä¶` ‚Üí `~/‚Ä¶` (exact home dir ‚Üí `~`). Handles Linux and macOS conventions.
- Truncation: if the path (after home substitution) has more than 2 non-empty segments, it is truncated to `‚Ä¶/<second-to-last>/<last>`. Paths with ‚â§ 2 segments are not truncated.
- Examples: `/home/sahil/code/org/repo/src` ‚Üí `‚Ä¶/repo/src`; `/home/sahil/code/org` ‚Üí `~/code/org`; `/var/log/nginx` ‚Üí `‚Ä¶/log/nginx`.
- The `title` attribute on the CWD element always contains the original unmodified `activePaneCwd` ‚Äî hover to see the full path.

## Session Creation Pattern

### Instant Creation (Primary)

All primary session creation entry points create a session immediately without a dialog. Implemented by `executeCreateSessionInstant` in `app.tsx`.

**Algorithm**:
1. Derive a name from the active window's `worktreePath` using `deriveNameFromPath(worktreePath)` (exported from `create-session-dialog.tsx`). If the result is empty (CWD is `/`, `~`, or `worktreePath` is undefined), the name is `session`.
2. Deduplicate against `sessions`: if the name is taken, try `{name}-2`, `{name}-3`, ‚Ä¶ up to `{name}-10`. If all are taken, use `{name}-11` (best-effort).
3. Call `createSession(server, derivedName, worktreePath)`. If no active window exists, call `createSession(server, "session")` (no `cwd` ‚Äî tmux defaults to server CWD).
4. The session appears in the sidebar via the existing optimistic/ghost mechanism.

**Entry points** (all call `onCreateSession` ‚Üí `executeCreateSessionInstant`):
- Sidebar `+` button (session level)
- Sidebar empty-state `+ New Session` button
- `SessionTiles` "+ New Session" dashed-border tile (the density view on `/$server`; was the Dashboard card before `260701-70a0`)
- Top-bar breadcrumb session dropdown `+ New Session` item
- Cmd+K "Session: Create" action

**Name derivation utilities**: `deriveNameFromPath` and `toTmuxSafeName` are exported from `app/frontend/src/components/create-session-dialog.tsx` so `app.tsx` can import them without duplicating logic.

### Folder-Prompted Creation (Secondary, via Cmd+K)

Two secondary entry points open `CreateSessionDialog` for users who want to specify a starting directory:

- **"Session: Create at Folder"** ‚Äî opens `CreateSessionDialog` (mode `"session"`, default). The dialog's path input is pre-filled with `currentWindow.worktreePath` via the `defaultPath?: string` prop added to `CreateSessionDialogProps`. If no active window, the field starts empty.
- **"Window: Create at Folder"** ‚Äî opens `CreateSessionDialog` with `mode="window"` and `session={currentSession}`. In window mode: title changes to "Create window at folder", session name input hidden, confirming calls `createWindow(server, session, undefined, cwd)` ‚Äî **no name** (since `260707-j66b-unnamed-windows-autoname-folder`; was the hardcoded `"zsh"`), so tmux auto-names the window to the chosen folder's basename via `automatic-rename-format` (see [tmux-sessions](/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md) ¬ß Managed Window Creation). This flow sets no optimistic ghost, so there is no ghost label to derive.

`CreateSessionDialog` gains three optional backward-compatible props:
- `defaultPath?: string` ‚Äî pre-fills the path input
- `mode?: "session" | "window"` ‚Äî controls dialog behavior (default `"session"`)
- `session?: string` ‚Äî required in window mode to pass to `createWindow`

### Deprecated: Dialog-First Flow

The `showCreateDialog` / `openCreateDialog` / `closeCreateDialog` API in `use-dialog-state.ts` has been removed. `CreateSessionDialog` is no longer opened by the sidebar `+` button or the primary "Session: Create" palette action. Use "Session: Create at Folder" in Cmd+K for folder-prompted session creation.

### Unnamed `+ New Window` ‚Äî Folder Auto-Naming

Since `260707-j66b-unnamed-windows-autoname-folder`, the `+ New Window` action **no longer pins the window name to `"zsh"`** ‚Äî it calls `createWindow` with **no name**, so tmux auto-names the window to its folder basename and live-updates it (the tmux-layer convention lives in [tmux-sessions](/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md) ¬ß Managed Window Creation). Before this, every window created via the UI stayed named "zsh" forever, so a sidebar full of windows was indistinguishable rows.

**All three formerly-hardcoded `"zsh"` call sites now create unnamed windows:**

1. **Sidebar `+ New Window`** (`app.tsx`, the `create-window` "Window: Create" palette action) ‚Äî `createWindow(srv, session, undefined, activeWin?.worktreePath)`. Its optimistic-ghost label becomes the **raw** (unsanitized) basename of the creation cwd via the local `rawBasename(cwd)` helper (falls back to `"window"` when no cwd). This is deliberately **NOT** `deriveNameFromPath` ‚Äî that runs `toTmuxSafeName` (`.`‚Üí`_` etc.), but tmux's `#{b:pane_current_path}` uses the unsanitized basename, so the ghost must match the raw form tmux will actually display.
2. **Palette "Window: Create at Folder"** (`create-session-dialog.tsx`, `mode="window"`) ‚Äî `createWindow(server, session, undefined, cwd)`; this flow sets **no** optimistic ghost, so no label is derived.
3. **Board-route `+ New Window`** (`board-page.tsx`) ‚Äî `createWindowApi(srv, sess)` (no name, no cwd ‚Äî the backend resolves a default; this action registers no ghost). Identical behavior to the same button on `/$server`.

**Client contract**: `createWindow(server, session, name?, cwd?, rkType?, rkUrl?)` in `api/client.ts` makes `name` optional and **omits it from the JSON body when absent/empty** (matching the existing omit-when-absent handling for `cwd`/`rkType`/`rkUrl`). Explicit names are still sent ‚Äî the deliberate-name paths are unchanged: **iframe/service windows** (`Window: New Iframe Window`, `createWindow(..., name, undefined, "iframe", url)`), the `port-N` "Open in window" service windows (`server-list-page.tsx`), and `rk riff`.

**E2E** (`app/frontend/tests/e2e/new-window-unnamed.spec.ts` + sibling `.spec.md`): asserts, via route interception on `POST /api/sessions/*/windows`, that the `+ New Window` request body carries **no `name` key** ‚Äî a deterministic frontend‚ÜíAPI seam. (The visual auto-rename is NOT asserted: the e2e tmux server is created with a bare `new-session` and `CreateWindow` never sources the config there, so `automatic-rename-format` isn't reliably applied on that server; the tmux-native naming is covered by the config + Go arg-builder tests instead.)

**Ghost TTL backstop** (`GHOST_WINDOW_TTL_MS = 15_000`, exported from `src/store/window-store.ts`, since `260717-hikh-exact-tmux-session-targets`): an optimistic ghost row is **claimed** only when a NEW windowId (one not in the ghost's `snapshotWindowIds`) arrives for its `(server, session)` via SSE (`setWindowsForSession`, oldest-ghost-first). Ordinary creates confirm within one SSE tick (~1-2s), and a *failed* create's caller rollback calls `removeGhost`. But if a create **succeeds somewhere else** ‚Äî e.g. a tmux target ambiguity routes the window into a different session (the 2026-07-17 `ext` misroute, now fixed at the backend by exact-match session targets, see [tmux-sessions](/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md) ¬ß Exact-Match Session Targets) ‚Äî no rollback fires and no claim ever arrives, stranding a permanently greyed, pulsing, unclickable row. `addGhostWindow` therefore arms a `setTimeout(() => get().removeGhost(optimisticId), GHOST_WINDOW_TTL_MS)`: the unclaimed ghost self-clears after 15s (comfortably past any legitimate claim). `removeGhost` is **idempotent** (filters by `optimisticId`), so a timer firing after the ghost was already claimed or rolled back is a no-op. This is a generic frontend backstop for the "no rollback, no claim" strand, independent of the backend root-cause fix. Two fake-timer unit tests cover TTL expiry and the claimed-ghost no-op.

## Bottom Bar (Shell-level, Shared Across Routes)

Single row of `<kbd>` styled buttons, rendered at shell level via `<Shell>`'s `bottombar` grid area on every route that mounts `<Shell>` ‚Äî single-terminal, board, and tmux Server (no-window) alike (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout` lifted it from the terminal column up to shell level). Width tracks the right grid column (page width minus sidebar). Styled with `border-t-[3px] border-border` (the 3px structural seam ‚Äî see ¬ß Border-Width System; `260702-6m46` widened it from `border-t`) and `px-1.5 h-[48px]`. Layout: `Tab Ctrl Alt Fn‚ñ¥ ArrowPad | >_ ‚åòK ‚å®`. Hostname removed from bottom bar ‚Äî now shown exclusively in the sidebar Host panel. Escape moved to the Function key dropdown's extended-keys section. The `>_` button (conditionally rendered when `onOpenCompose` is provided) is an `aria-pressed` accent toggle for the docked compose strip (¬ß Docked Compose Strip), not a modal trigger.

`BottomBarProps` no longer contains `wsRef` ‚Äî the prop was removed when BottomBar moved up the tree. Input handlers read `focused?.wsRef` from `FocusedTerminalContext` and send ANSI escape sequences through it. The component is byte-identical across single-terminal and board routes (same JSX, same callbacks: `onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`) ‚Äî board panes are terminals, so the input toolbar applies identically. When `focused === null` (Dashboard route, no active terminal), input handlers natural-no-op via the existing `wsRef.current?.readyState !== OPEN` guard ‚Äî no error, no toast.

**Modifier toggles** (Ctrl, Alt): Sticky armed state with visual indicator (`accent` bg). Click to arm, auto-clears after next key is sent. Click again while armed to disarm. Multiple modifiers can be armed simultaneously. Cmd (`‚åò`) removed ‚Äî on desktop users hold the real Cmd key; on mobile Cmd combos aren't used in terminal workflows.

**Armed modifier bridging**: When modifiers are armed, a capture-phase `keydown` listener intercepts physical keypresses and translates them to terminal escape sequences (Ctrl+letter ‚Üí control characters, Alt ‚Üí ESC prefix). Sends via WebSocket, preventing xterm from receiving the unmodified key. Ignores real Cmd/Ctrl/Alt held by the OS.

**ArrowPad** (`arrow-pad.tsx`): Combined directional pad replacing individual arrow buttons. Sends ANSI escape sequences (`[A/B/C/D`). With modifiers, use xterm parameter encoding (`[1;{mod}X`). Modifier parameter: 1 + (alt?2:0) + (ctrl?4:0).

**Function key dropdown** (F‚ñ¥): Opens a combined popup above the button. Top section: F1-F12 in a 4-column grid. Divider (`border-t border-border`). Bottom section: Esc, PgUp, PgDn, Home, End, Ins, Del in a 3-column grid (3x3, 7 items). Escape uses `sendSpecial` (preserves Ctrl re-arm semantics); other extended keys use `sendWithMods`. Closes after each selection, on outside click, or on Escape.

**Special keys** (Tab in bottom bar, Esc in Fn menu): Direct send via `sendSpecial`. Ctrl is not consumed for Esc/Tab (Esc IS Ctrl+[, Tab IS Ctrl+I in terminal semantics) ‚Äî Ctrl stays armed for the next key. Alt prefix with ESC (Meta convention).

**All buttons**: 33px min-height / 35px min-width on fine pointers (`min-h-[33px] min-w-[35px]` ‚Äî reduced from 36√ó36 to give the row air), full 36√ó36 touch target on coarse pointers (`coarse:min-h-[36px] coarse:min-w-[36px]`). Row gap is `gap-1.5` (6px) on fine pointers, `coarse:gap-1` (4px) on touch ‚Äî so the 375px single-row budget is byte-identical to before. `text-xs`, `<kbd>` element styling.

**Focus preservation**: All bottom bar buttons that send terminal input or toggle modifier state have `onMouseDown={(e) => e.preventDefault()}` via a shared `preventFocusSteal` handler. This prevents the browser from shifting focus away from xterm.js's hidden textarea when buttons are tapped, keeping the on-screen keyboard visible on iOS/touch devices. The CmdK button is excluded (it intentionally opens a dialog that takes focus). The ArrowPad handles focus preservation independently via its own `onMouseDown` handler.

### Docked Compose Strip

`ComposeStrip` (`components/compose-strip.tsx`) is a single **global**, sticky text-input surface docked at the bottom of the terminal area, immediately **above** the bottom-bar keys. It is a plain `<div>` in the shell footer ‚Äî no backdrop, no `role="dialog"`/`aria-modal`, no focus trap, no Escape-closes, no close-on-send, no terminal dimming. A real `<textarea>` gives mobile autocorrect/IME (xterm is a `<canvas>` with neither) and a stable home for pasting large text blocks over a laggy relay.

**Two distinct send paths** (do not conflate): the compose strip rides the **relay WebSocket as raw bytes** ‚Äî Enter sends `text + "\r"` over the focused terminal's `wsRef` (the muxed RelayMux stream, same path as BottomBar keystrokes), no backend endpoint. The **chat-send** path is entirely separate ‚Äî `POST /api/windows/{id}/chat/send` with named-buffer paste + NOVELTY echo probe + gated Enter + per-`(server,paneID)` lock (see [chat](/run-kit/chat.md) ¬ß send path). Compose does NOT use that machinery.

**Toggle + persistence.** The strip's enablement is the `composeStripEnabled` chrome preference (ChromeContext, `localStorage["runkit-compose-strip"]`, `"true"` sentinel ‚Äî the `terminalFontSize`/`fixedWidth` pattern; see ¬ß Terminal Font Size). Two parity affordances flip it: the bottom-bar `>_` chip (`aria-pressed={composeStripEnabled}` + the ctrl/alt pressed-state vocabulary `bg-accent/20 border-accent text-accent` when on, `text-text-secondary` off; `preventFocusSteal` preserved) and the `View: Text Input` palette action (`toggleComposeStrip`). The caller gates the mount (`{composeStripEnabled && <ComposeStrip />}` in `app.tsx` and `board-page.tsx` footers). Toggling grows/shrinks the footer grid row by the strip's height, which the terminal container's existing `ResizeObserver` picks up ‚Üí `fitAndSync` (FitAddon `fit()` + tmux resize) ‚Äî the same reflow class as a font-size change; no dedicated refit effect.

**Live target (reverses the modal's frozen-target DD-6).** The strip sends to the **currently-focused** pane's `wsRef` from `FocusedTerminalContext`, read live at send time ‚Äî never a target snapshotted at open. A persistent surface that outlives many focus changes would, with a frozen target, silently send to a stale/closed pane. The wrong-pane risk is instead mitigated by an always-visible `‚Üí {window}` target label, resolved in layers: window-store name by `server:windowId` (live ‚Äî tracks renames) ‚Üí the `windowName` the registrant carried into `FocusedTerminalContext` (board entries have a server-derived `windowName`; the store only covers servers whose sidebar group has delivered sessions, so board panes from other servers would otherwise label as `@N`) ‚Üí raw windowId. With `focused === null` (e.g. the `/$server` tiles route) the strip renders **disabled** with a "no target" label and never sends.

**Send semantics.** Enter sends `text + "\r"` guarded on `wsRef.readyState === WebSocket.OPEN`; Shift+Enter inserts a newline; Enter is guarded against IME composition (`e.nativeEvent.isComposing`); empty/whitespace-only Enter is a no-op (bare Enter for TUI y/n prompts stays a terminal tap). After a **delivered** send the textarea + attachments clear and the strip stays open. A **guard-blocked** send (stream not open) early-returns WITHOUT clearing ‚Äî the draft is preserved.

**Draft survives everything.** Because the mount is conditional (toggle-off unmounts it) AND per-route (the AppShell and BoardPage footers are distinct React subtrees), draft text + pending attachments live in a **module store** (`lib/compose-draft-store.ts`) read via `useSyncExternalStore(subscribeComposeDraft, getComposeDraft)` ‚Äî the same module-slot + listener-set + stable-snapshot pattern as the window-switch pending mask (`window-transition.ts`). Any mounted strip instance reads the same live draft, so an unsent draft survives toggle-off/on and terminal‚Üîboard route changes. Blob-URL previews are the one piece of state kept component-local (a fresh per-mount ref, revoked on unmount, recreated lazily from the retained `File` objects on remount).

**Focus routing.** The strip NEVER steals focus (mount / toggle / after-send) ‚Äî the user chooses where to type. Escape in the textarea blurs it back to the terminal (never closes the strip). `preventFocusSteal` (`onMouseDown` preventDefault) is on the Send/üìé buttons. On touch devices the ‚å® keyboard button focuses the strip's real textarea when the preference is on, via the **focus registry** in `lib/compose-strip-events.ts` (`registerComposeStripFocuser`/`focusComposeStrip` ‚Äî a module registry, not a `document.querySelector('[data-testid]')`, since test ids are test-only here; the focuser returns `false` in the disabled "no target" case so `bottom-bar.tsx` falls back to `onFocusTerminal`).

**Uploads ‚Äî eager, worktree-scoped, re-homed on focus change.** The strip calls `useFileUpload(focused.session, focused.windowId, focused.server)` scoped to the **live** focused target, so uploads land in that window's worktree `.uploads/` (backend `upload.go` unchanged ‚Äî see ¬ß File Upload). Retained `File` objects back both previews and re-homing: when the focused target changes while attachments are pending, the held files are re-uploaded to the new worktree and the textarea path lines are rewritten (`lines.indexOf(oldPath)` splice). Re-home failure keeps the original path lines and surfaces a non-blocking inline `role="alert"` error; sending is not blocked (orphaned files in the old worktree are acceptable). Terminal drag-drop / clipboard-paste gestures (`terminal-client.tsx`) hand raw files to the strip via a document `CustomEvent` bridge (`COMPOSE_STRIP_ATTACH_EVENT` + a module hand-off queue in `compose-strip-events.ts`, drained on both the event and mount), enabling the preference first if off ‚Äî no prop-drilling of upload results.

**Board-pane focus cleanup.** `BoardPane` registers itself as the focused terminal while `isFocused`, and clears `FocusedTerminalContext` on **unmount** iff it is still the registered pane (`focusedRef.current?.wsRef === wsRef`, unmount-only `[]` deps, ref-guarded so a sibling's newer registration during a focus cycle is not clobbered). Without it, leaving a board for `/$server` would strand a stale non-null target ‚Äî the enabled strip would render active with a stale label and upload into the stale worktree. With it, the strip reverts to the disabled "no target" state.

### File Upload

Entry points, all on the terminal page:
- **Clipboard paste** (`Cmd+V` / `Ctrl+V`) ‚Äî document-level paste listener; files in `clipboardData.files` trigger upload, text-only paste passes through to xterm
- **Drag-and-drop** ‚Äî drop files onto the terminal area; `ring-2 ring-accent` border highlight during drag-over; non-file drag content ignored
- **Compose strip upload button** (üìé) ‚Äî in the docked compose strip action row, left of Send; opens native file picker via hidden `<input type="file">`

The paste/drop gestures live in `terminal-client.tsx` and hand raw files to the docked compose strip (enabling the `composeStripEnabled` preference first if off) via the `COMPOSE_STRIP_ATTACH_EVENT` document bridge; the strip uploads them to the **focused** target's worktree and inserts one path per line in its textarea (see ¬ß Docked Compose Strip). Server writes to `.uploads/{YYMMDD-HHmmss}-{sanitized-name}` in the target window's worktree. 50MB size limit. `.uploads/` auto-added to `.gitignore` on first use.

### iOS Keyboard Support

`useVisualViewport` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-visual-viewport.ts`) manages all viewport-related CSS side effects: adds the `fullbleed` class to `<html>` on mount (removed on cleanup), and listens to both `resize` and `scroll` events on `window.visualViewport`, setting `--app-height` (and `--app-offset-top`) CSS custom properties from `visualViewport.height`. The `scroll` listener catches iOS Safari viewport panning that doesn't trigger `resize`. **Since `260707-4vq2-lift-topbar-root-layout` the hook is called once in `RootWrapper`** (was in `Shell`) so the `--app-height` var is maintained on EVERY route ‚Äî including the Host page and edge pages that mount no `Shell` ‚Äî and owning the single idempotent effect at the root avoids the double-mount cleanup race a second copy in `Shell` would create.

In fullbleed mode, `globals.css` pins the **`.app-root` root layout container** (`position: fixed; inset: 0; height: var(--app-height, 100vh)`) to the visual viewport regardless of document scroll ‚Äî **moved from `.app-shell` by `4vq2`**, because the persistent TopBar now lives inside `.app-root` above the content region, so pinning that container (not the per-route `.app-shell` beneath it) keeps the header above the content instead of `.app-shell`'s `position: fixed` overlaying it. The per-route `.app-shell` is now `position: relative; height: 100%` ‚Äî it fills the root layout's `flex-1` region (its `overflow: hidden` still contains xterm's canvas). When the iOS keyboard appears, the bottom bar stays pinned above it, the terminal shrinks, and xterm refits via the existing `ResizeObserver`. The `fullbleed` class is also present in `index.html` as a static default (FOUC prevention); the hook takes over lifecycle management at runtime.

**Keyboard toggle** (`‚å®` U+2328): Right-aligned button in the bottom bar, visible only on touch devices (`hidden coarse:inline-flex`). Bidirectional toggle: when terminal is focused (detected via `document.activeElement.closest(".xterm")`), tapping blurs to dismiss the keyboard; when not focused, tapping calls `onFocusTerminal` callback which chains through `app.tsx` ‚Üí `TerminalClient.focusRef` ‚Üí `xtermRef.current.focus()` to summon the keyboard. Dynamic `aria-label`: "Hide keyboard" / "Show keyboard". Uses `preventFocusSteal` to avoid stealing focus on the dismiss path.

**Scroll-lock mode**: Long-press (>= 500ms) on the keyboard toggle button activates scroll-lock ‚Äî a mode that prevents the soft keyboard from appearing when the terminal area is tapped, allowing uninterrupted reading and scrolling. State is a `scrollLocked` boolean in `BottomBar` (default `false`), exposed to the parent via `onScrollLockChange` callback and passed down to `TerminalClient` as a `scrollLocked` prop. When locked, a capture-phase `focusin` listener on the terminal container immediately blurs any `.xterm` element that gains focus, preventing the keyboard from appearing. Touch scroll gestures (SGR mouse sequences) are unaffected ‚Äî only focus is prevented. Activating scroll-lock while the keyboard is visible auto-dismisses it (`document.activeElement?.blur()`). Optional haptic feedback via `navigator.vibrate?.(50)` on toggle (graceful no-op if unavailable).

- **Long-press detection**: `touchstart`/`touchend`/`touchmove` handlers with a 500ms timer (`LONG_PRESS_MS` constant). Touch move > 10px (`LONG_PRESS_MOVE_THRESHOLD`) cancels the long-press. On timer expiry, scroll-lock toggles and subsequent `touchend`/`click` are suppressed via a ref flag. Desktop click behavior is unaffected (touch events only).
- **Tap in locked mode**: Tapping the keyboard button (< 500ms) when `scrollLocked` is `true` unlocks AND summons the keyboard in one action ‚Äî matches user intent without requiring a double-tap.
- **Visual indicator**: When locked, the button shows `bg-accent/20 border-accent text-accent` (same armed-state pattern as Ctrl/Alt modifier toggles) and the icon changes from `‚å®` (U+2328) to `üîí` (U+1F512). `aria-label` updates to "Scroll lock on ‚Äî tap to unlock".
- **State lifecycle**: Session-scoped (component-local React state, not persisted). Resets on navigation (component unmount/remount). The docked compose strip is unaffected ‚Äî it has its own input field outside the terminal container.

### Terminal Touch Scroll

The terminal container div has `touch-pan-y` (CSS `touch-action: pan-y`) ‚Äî allows vertical swipe gestures for scrollback access on mobile/touch devices while blocking horizontal panning (prevents page-level overflow from tmux's ~80 column minimum). The xterm.js `.xterm-viewport` has `overflow-y: scroll` and `overscroll-behavior: none` (in `globals.css`), so the browser delegates vertical touch scroll to xterm natively without page bounce. In the single-view model, fullbleed is always active ‚Äî `overflow: hidden` and `overscroll-behavior: none` are applied to both `html` and `body` (via `globals.css`), preventing iOS Safari elastic bounce scrolling. The docked compose strip and bottom bar are siblings of the terminal container, not children, so their touch behavior is preserved.

## Mobile Responsive

### Breakpoints & Container Width

All zones use `px-3 sm:px-6` ‚Äî reduced horizontal padding on screens < 640px. No `max-w-4xl` constraint ‚Äî terminal, top bar, and bottom bar all span full width. The mobile/desktop breakpoint for the `<Shell>` topology is **640px** (matches the existing `sm:` Tailwind breakpoint and `useIsMobile()` hook): `>= 640px` uses the 2-column grid with sidebar full-height; `< 640px` uses the single-column grid with sidebar overlay. Sidebar is drag-resizable on desktop (default 220px, min 160, max 400); terminal fills remaining space via the right grid column. Terminal container has `py-0.5 px-1` padding for breathing room against border lines. Bottom bar uses `py-1.5` vertical padding.

### Touch Targets

A custom Tailwind variant `coarse:` is defined in `globals.css` via `@custom-variant coarse (@media (pointer: coarse))`. On touch devices, interactive elements are upsized per surface ‚Äî `coarse:` is the mechanism, not a universal size (there is no single 44px minimum; each surface documents its own target). Upsized elements include:
- FixedWidthToggle (`coarse:min-h-[36px] coarse:min-w-[28px]`)
- Sidebar session ‚úï kill buttons + window rows
- Breadcrumb name dropdown triggers
- `‚ãØ` command palette trigger
- Hamburger icon (sidebar toggle ‚Äî single state covers desktop column collapse and mobile overlay since `260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)

Bottom bar buttons use the full `coarse:min-h-[36px] coarse:min-w-[36px]` touch target on touch devices, `min-h-[33px] min-w-[35px]` on fine pointers (with a 6px fine / 4px coarse row gap).

### Viewport Zoom Prevention

The viewport meta tag in `app/frontend/index.html` includes `maximum-scale=1.0` and `user-scalable=no` to prevent iOS Safari from auto-zooming when text inputs (command palette, docked compose strip) receive focus. Without these directives, iOS zooms in on inputs with `font-size < 16px`, displacing the entire interface. Pinch-to-zoom is also disabled ‚Äî acceptable tradeoff for a keyboard-first tool dashboard where zoom doesn't improve terminal readability. The existing `interactive-widget=resizes-content` directive is preserved (controls keyboard layout resizing, unrelated to zoom).

### Terminal Addons

Addons loaded in `init()` from **static top-of-file imports**, after `terminal.open()`, before `ResizeObserver` setup. Order: FitAddon (existing) ‚Üí fit() ‚Üí ClipboardAddon ‚Üí WebLinksAddon ‚Üí UnicodeGraphemesAddon ‚Üí WebglAddon. The Unicode addon MUST precede WebGL so the renderer measures cell widths against the active Unicode 15 table on first paint.

**Static import bundling** (since `260531-m3pl-static-xterm-imports`): all six xterm-family value imports (`@xterm/xterm` `Terminal`, `addon-fit`, `addon-clipboard`, `addon-web-links`, `addon-unicode-graphemes`, `addon-webgl`) are static top-of-file `import` statements in `terminal-client.tsx`, NOT runtime `await import()`. Because `terminal-client.tsx` is already router-lazy, the xterm family bundles into the already-deferred terminal-route chunk and loads **once when that chunk loads** ‚Äî never as a per-pane-mount runtime module-graph fetch. This removes all six chunk fetches from the browser's per-origin connection budget at terminal-init time, fixing the board-route E2E hang: on the plaintext dev/test origin (no HTTP/2 ‚Äî only negotiated over TLS), the browser caps ~6 persistent connections per origin, and long-lived streams (Vite HMR socket, pooled SSE `EventSource`, one `/relay/<wid>` WS per visible pane) already saturate the slots, so a 7th xterm chunk fetch hung pending forever ‚Üí `setTerminalReady(true)` never ran ‚Üí blank pane ‚Üí E2E poll timeout. Masked in production over Tailscale HTTPS (h2 multiplexes). The CSS side-effect import (`@xterm/xterm/css/xterm.css`) and type-only `import("@xterm/...")` annotations were already static and are unchanged.

| Addon | Purpose | Notes |
|-------|---------|-------|
| `@xterm/addon-fit` | Auto-resize columns/rows | Existing ‚Äî loaded first, `fit()` called immediately |
| `@xterm/addon-clipboard` | OSC 52 clipboard sequences | Custom `ClipboardProvider` accepts both `""` (empty/default, tmux's format) and `"c"` (explicit) selection targets. Rejects `"p"`, `"s"`, `"0"`‚Äì`"7"`. Provider exported as `clipboardProvider` for testability |
| `@xterm/addon-web-links` | Clickable URLs in terminal output | |
| `@xterm/addon-unicode-graphemes` | Unicode 15 + grapheme-cluster width tables | Requires `allowProposedApi: true` on the Terminal constructor; `terminal.unicode.activeVersion = "15-graphemes"` set after `loadAddon()`. Must load before the WebGL addon |
| `@xterm/addon-webgl` | GPU-accelerated rendering | The `new WebglAddon()` / `loadAddon(...)` construction stays wrapped in try/catch ‚Äî silently falls back to canvas renderer on GPU/WebGL-context failure. The *module load* is static (resolved at chunk load, cannot fail at `init()` time), but context creation can still throw at runtime, so the runtime guard is retained (`260531-m3pl-static-xterm-imports`) |

### Terminal Font Size (user-controllable global preference)

Terminal font size is a **global** user preference owned by `ChromeContext` (`260613-oo89-terminal-font-size-control`), not a per-pane or per-window value. The context exposes the **effective** size as `terminalFontSize: number` (what `TerminalClient` reads and the top-bar control displays); the internal preference is stored as `number | null` (null = unset) and persisted to `localStorage["runkit-terminal-font-size"]`. Effective = preference ?? device default ‚Äî 11px mobile / 13px desktop via the shared `isMobileViewport()` rule (narrow-width OR coarse-pointer, NOT a CSS media query ‚Äî replaces the old `matchMedia('(min-width: 640px)')` device-class read). Bounds 8‚Äì24px, step 1, exported as `TERMINAL_FONT_BOUNDS` (`{ min: 8, max: 24, step: 1 }`); all stored values clamped into `[8, 24]` on read. Helpers `clampTerminalFont`/`deviceDefaultFontSize`/`readTerminalFontSize` mirror the `fixedWidth`/`SIDEBAR_WIDTH_BOUNDS` shape.

**Mutators** (`ChromeDispatch`): `increaseTerminalFont` / `decreaseTerminalFont` step `effective ¬± step`, clamp, persist (try/catch noop); `resetTerminalFont` = **forget preference** (`localStorage.removeItem` ‚Üí preference back to `null` ‚Üí effective reverts to the device default), NOT a fixed value. First step from the unset (`null`) state operates on the device default and persists a concrete adjacent value (desktop 13 ‚Üí 14).

**Applied to xterm** (`terminal-client.tsx`): `terminalFontSize` is passed as the `fontSize` option on construction (and to the `document.fonts.load` preloads, replacing `isMobile ? 11 : 13`); an effect keyed on it sets `term.options.fontSize = N` + calls `fitAddonRef.current?.fit()` on change (guarded against an uninitialized terminal). `fit()` recomputes rows√ócols and **resizes the PTY** (the correct xterm resize path ‚Äî reflows running TUIs, not a bitmap-scaled canvas). Because the value is global, **every** live `TerminalClient` reacts on change ‚Äî including all mounted board-route panes. The mobile touch-scroll `LINE_HEIGHT` fallback reads `options.fontSize` live, so it tracks runtime changes.

**Control surfaces**: (1) a top-bar combo button `[‚àí] {size} [+]` + reset (see ¬ß FixedWidthToggle), and (2) three command-palette actions ‚Äî `terminal-font-increase` ("Increase terminal font"), `terminal-font-decrease` ("Decrease terminal font"), `terminal-font-reset` ("Reset terminal font"), no `shortcut`, wired to the dispatch fns. The palette actions are present on **both** the AppShell palette (`app.tsx`) and the board-route palette (`board-page.tsx`) ‚Äî the setting is global and Constitution V requires the palette reachable on every route. This is the same dual-mount duplication `refresh-page` follows (¬ß Command Palette View actions).

**Deliberate non-decision**: `Cmd +/-` is **NOT** intercepted ‚Äî browser-native whole-page zoom is retained as-is (no global keybinding registered), avoiding the brittleness of hijacking `Cmd +/-` / `Cmd 0`. Deferred (out of scope for v1): UI/HTML-zone scaling (`:root { font-size }`), per-pane/per-window sizing, and cross-restart persistence via a tmux `@rk_font_size` option (localStorage only).

### Terminal Font Bundling

The frontend bundles JetBrainsMono Nerd Font (patched single-file variant) as a webfont so terminal rendering is deterministic across all viewers, independent of which monospace fonts the browser happens to have installed. Without bundling, per-glyph font fallback for Nerd Font private-use-area codepoints produces visible baseline wobble within a single terminal row.

**Asset layout**: Three `.woff2` weights served from `/fonts/` ‚Äî `JetBrainsMonoNerdFont-Regular.woff2` (400 normal), `-Bold.woff2` (700 normal), `-Italic.woff2` (400 italic). All three `@font-face` rules in `app/frontend/src/globals.css` expose the same `font-family: "JetBrainsMono Nerd Font"` name and MUST declare `font-display: block`. `swap` or `fallback` would let xterm measure cells against system-font metrics that persist as misalignment ‚Äî xterm measures the character cell grid exactly once at `terminal.open()` and does not re-measure when a deferred font arrives. `index.html` includes a `<link rel="preload" as="font" type="font/woff2" crossorigin href="/fonts/JetBrainsMonoNerdFont-Regular.woff2" />` to overlap the Regular download with JS parsing (only Regular is preloaded ‚Äî Bold/Italic are a smaller fraction of the initial paint and don't justify the extra critical-path bytes).

**Load convention before `terminal.open()`**: The init routine in `app/frontend/src/components/terminal-client.tsx` awaits a concurrent `Promise.all([document.fonts.load(...), document.fonts.load(...), document.fonts.load(...)])` for all three weights at the exact `fontPx` (`isMobile ? 11 : 13`) the Terminal will use, BEFORE `new Terminal(...)` / `terminal.open()` / `fitAddon.fit()`. Three explicit `document.fonts.load(size, family)` calls (not `document.fonts.ready`) scope the await to exactly the weights xterm will request. A fresh `if (cancelled || !terminalRef.current) return;` guard MUST follow the await. Since `260531-m3pl-static-xterm-imports` made all six xterm imports static, this font-load `await Promise.all([...])` is the **only** remaining async boundary in `init()` (the former `await import(...)` boundaries are gone), so it is the sole place a post-await unmount guard is required before `new Terminal(...)`; the inter-addon `cancelled` re-checks that existed solely to guard the removed import awaits were dropped, leaving one post-construction dispose guard before `setTerminalReady(true)`.

**Primary `fontFamily`**: `'"JetBrainsMono Nerd Font", ui-monospace, monospace'` ‚Äî bundled webfont first, `ui-monospace` as the system-default monospace, generic `monospace` as final guard against total load failure. The older long tail (`JetBrains Mono`, `Fira Code`, `SF Mono`, `Menlo`, `Monaco`, `Consolas`) is dead code once `font-display: block` plus a successful load makes the webfont always win; do not reintroduce it. Non-terminal monospace surfaces pick up the same font automatically via Tailwind's `--font-mono` custom property (webfont-first). Introduced by change `260417-hyrl-bundle-jetbrains-mono-nerd-font`.

**Test caveat**: jsdom does not implement the FontFaceSet API. `src/test-setup.ts` stubs a minimal `document.fonts.load()` / `document.fonts.ready` surface (same pattern as the existing `ResizeObserver` stub) so unit tests that mount `TerminalClient` do not hang on the await.

### Terminal Unicode Width Handling

xterm.js defaults to Unicode 6 width tables, which classify many modern glyphs (most emojis, several Misc Symbols codepoints) as 1 cell. Modern tmux lays out its buffer using wcwidth with a newer Unicode table (typically 14/15), treating the same glyphs as 2 cells. Without alignment, subsequent characters in a row drift between tmux's intended column and xterm's rendered column, producing visible ghost/overlap artifacts ‚Äî especially with the WebGL renderer.

**Resolution** (`app/frontend/src/components/terminal-client.tsx`):
1. Construct the Terminal with `allowProposedApi: true` ‚Äî required to access `terminal.unicode` (a proposed-API surface in xterm v6).
2. After `terminal.open()`, `loadAddon(new UnicodeGraphemesAddon())` (statically imported since `260531-m3pl-static-xterm-imports`) and set `terminal.unicode.activeVersion = "15-graphemes"`.
3. Load order MUST precede the WebGL addon so the renderer initialises against the Unicode 15 table on first measure.

The `addon-unicode-graphemes` package (v6-era) supersedes `addon-unicode11`: it covers Unicode 15 and grapheme clusters (ZWJ sequences, flag emoji, skin-tone modifiers) at the same install cost. The `unicodeVersion` Terminal constructor option is a no-op past `"6"` without the addon ‚Äî the addon is what registers the newer width table.

Introduced by change `260418-xgl2-xterm-emoji-width`.

### Command Palette Mobile Trigger

The `CommandPalette` component listens for a `palette:open` CustomEvent on `document` (in addition to `‚åòK`). The `‚ãØ` button in Line 1 dispatches this event on mobile. This is the mobile equivalent of `‚åòK` ‚Äî physical keyboards aren't available on phones.

### Keyboard-Navigable List Scroll Pattern

Both `CommandPalette` and `ThemeSelector` use the same scroll-into-view pattern for arrow key navigation: a `listRef` on the listbox container plus a `useEffect` on `[selectedIndex, open]` that queries `[aria-selected="true"]` and calls `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })`. This ensures the selected item stays visible when navigating past the `max-h-64` scroll boundary. New keyboard-navigable list components SHOULD follow this pattern.

The sidebar session/window tree is a **third consumer** (`260613-wt1v-sidebar-keyboard-nav`, see ¬ß Sidebar ‚Üí Keyboard Navigation & Tree ARIA): a `treeRef` on the `role="tree"` container plus a `useEffect` on `[rovingKey]` that resolves the roving row (`[data-window-id]`/`[data-session-row]`) and calls `scrollIntoView({ block: "nearest" })` + `focus()`. It reuses the scroll-into-view half but deliberately diverges from the `selectedIndex` numeric-state model ‚Äî the roving cursor is a row-key STRING (robust to the variable-length tree's expand/collapse and SSE row churn, where a numeric index can desync); the focus call is gated by `focusMovedRef` so passive SSE re-renders never scroll/steal focus.

## Keyboard Shortcuts

### Global
| Key | Action | Context |
|-----|--------|---------|
| `Cmd+K` | Open command palette | Always |
| `Cmd+.` / `Ctrl+.` (`260714-t97o-web-view-lens`) | Cycle the current window's view lenses (over `availableViews`, e.g. `tty‚Üíweb‚Üítty` or `tty‚Üíchat‚Üítty`) | Terminal route ‚Äî a window-level `keydown` in `app.tsx` that `preventDefault()`s so xterm doesn't also receive it, gated by `shouldSuppressViewChord` (the same non-xterm-input rule as `‚åò\`). No-op when < 2 views. Documented in the Keyboard Shortcuts dialog (App section) + the `View:` palette entries. See ¬ß Window Views (Lens Model) |
| `Cmd+C` / `Ctrl+C` | Copy selection to clipboard (with selection) or send SIGINT (without selection) | Terminal focused ‚Äî via `attachCustomKeyEventHandler`, `keydown` only. Uses `navigator.clipboard.writeText()` with `document.execCommand('copy')` fallback for non-secure contexts (HTTP). Selection cleared after copy via `.finally()` |
| ``Ctrl+` `` | Toggle tty‚Üîchat view (`260714-r7rq`) | Terminal route with a `chatProvider` window ‚Äî plain Ctrl on BOTH platforms (NOT Cmd; Cmd+` is macOS window cycling). Document-level `keydown` capture (`use-chat-view-shortcut.ts`, speaks the unified `ViewName` ‚Äî toggles via `switchView` between `chat` and `tty`) that fires EVEN while xterm owns focus (modeled on `useSidebarKeyboardToggle` minus its xterm-focus suppression); bails on a real INPUT/TEXTAREA/contentEditable target that is not inside `.xterm`. Enabled iff `currentViews.includes("chat")` (a chat-less window ‚áí no-op). See ¬ß Window Views (Lens Model) ‚Üí shortcuts / ¬ß Chat View |

No single-key shortcuts (`j`/`k`/`c`/`r`) or `Esc Esc` ‚Äî these conflicted with xterm.js terminal input. All actions are accessible via `Cmd+K` command palette or top bar buttons.

Command palette actions include: create/rename/kill session, create/rename/kill window, move window left/right, move up/down for the current server/session/window (`260705-bpnr` ‚Äî see ¬ß Command Palette Move up/down), theme switching, "Reload tmux config" (targets the active server via `?server=` param), "Create tmux server" (opens name dialog, creates session "0" in $HOME), "Kill tmux server" (confirmation dialog, kills active server, switches to next available ‚Äî the dialog carries a daemon-specific warning when the target is `rk-daemon`; see ¬ß Infra-server de-emphasis ‚Üí kill guard), "Switch tmux server: {name}" (one entry per available server, current marked), "Keyboard Shortcuts" (opens modal showing curated tmux keybindings from `GET /api/keybindings` + hardcoded `Cmd+K`), "Copy: tmux Commands" (opens tmux commands dialog ‚Äî only visible on terminal route when `currentWindow` is available), "Notifications: Enable push" / "Notifications: Enabled ‚úì" (the Web Push opt-in gesture ‚Äî terminal-themed label, NOT a bell; see ¬ß Notifications (Web Push opt-in)), and terminal navigation (jump to any session/window).

**Session/window creation actions in the palette**:
| Action ID | Label | Behavior |
|-----------|-------|----------|
| `create-session` | "Session: Create" | Instant creation ‚Äî no dialog (see Instant Session Creation) |
| `create-session-at-folder` | "Session: Create at Folder" | Opens `CreateSessionDialog` pre-filled with `currentWindow.worktreePath`; empty if no active window |
| `create-window` | "Window: Create" | Instant window creation ‚Äî the sidebar `+ New Window` path. Since `260707-j66b` creates an **unnamed** window (`createWindow` called with no name; was hardcoded `"zsh"`), so tmux auto-names it to the active window's folder basename; the optimistic ghost is labeled with the **raw** cwd basename (see ¬ß Unnamed `+ New Window`) |
| `create-window-at-folder` | "Window: Create at Folder" | Opens `CreateSessionDialog` in `mode="window"` (dialog title changes, session name input hidden, confirms via `createWindow(server, session, undefined, cwd)` ‚Äî no name, so tmux auto-names to the folder basename; was the hardcoded `"zsh"`, dropped by `260707-j66b`); only shown when a session is active |
| `create-iframe-window` | "Window: New Iframe Window" | Opens dialog with name + URL inputs; creates iframe window via `createWindow(server, session, name, undefined, "iframe", url)`; only shown when a session is active. Unchanged by `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` ‚Äî `@rk_type=iframe` now just seeds "default view = web" (¬ß Window Views (Lens Model)) |

**Window rename action** (`260703-5ilm`): the `rename-window` action ("Window: Rename") no longer opens a modal dialog ‚Äî it dispatches a `window-heading:rename` `CustomEvent` (guarded on `currentWindow`), which the centered top-bar `WindowHeading` listens for and enters inline edit (mirrors `theme-selector:open`). The action stays registered (Constitution V keyboard path); the former window rename `<Dialog>` + its `use-dialog-state.ts` wiring were retired (the palette was the dialog's sole entry point ‚Äî the SESSION rename dialog is unaffected). See ¬ß Window Heading.

**Window move actions**: "Window: Move Left" (id `move-window-left`) and "Window: Move Right" (id `move-window-right`) in the `windowActions` group. Only shown when `currentWindow` exists. "Move Left" excluded when the current window is at the minimum index in the session; "Move Right" excluded when at the maximum index (boundary exclusion, not disabled state). On select, calls `moveWindow(server, currentWindow.windowId, targetIndex)` (source by stable window ID, destination by position) then navigates to the **same** `currentWindow.windowId` ‚Äî the window keeps its ID across the reorder (only its index changes), so the user stays on their window after the swap. Since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder` the target index is computed via the shared pure helper `computeWindowMoveTarget(index, delta, minIndex, maxIndex)` (returns `null` at a boundary ‚Äî no wraparound) rather than a raw `index ¬± 1`; both the Left/Right entries and the new up/down entries below route through it.

**Command Palette Move up/down (server / session / window)** (`260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`): a keyboard/touch reorder path parallel to the two drag surfaces, closing the Constitution V ("every user-facing action MUST be reachable via keyboard") gap that drag-only reorder left open for ALL THREE hierarchy levels. Six new `PaletteAction`s, each acting on the **current** route-context entity (the `Server: Kill` current-entity semantics), grouped with their existing families in `app.tsx`, all with boundary = **hidden** (the entry is filtered out at the top/bottom of its list ‚Äî no wraparound, no disabled state):

- **`Server: Move up` / `Server: Move down`** (`server-move-up`/`-down`, `serverActions`) ‚Äî move the current server one position within the REGULAR class (infra excluded). The new full regular-class order is computed and POSTed via `setServerOrder` (server-global `event: server-order` echo re-sorts every client). Hidden when the current server is infra (`currentRegularIdx === -1`) or at a class boundary.
- **`Session: Move up` / `Session: Move down`** (`session-move-up`/`-down`, `sessionActions`) ‚Äî move the current session one position in the **effective** session order (`deriveEffectiveSessionOrder(liveNames, sseOrder)` ‚Äî persisted `@rk_session_order` filtered to live names, un-ordered live sessions appended in natural order; the sidebar's transient drag override is component-local and NOT visible to the palette). Persisted via the EXISTING `setSessionOrder(server, order)` ‚Äî the same primitive the sidebar session drag uses; no new backend.
