- **`Window: Move up` / `Window: Move down`** (`window-move-up`/`-down`, `windowActions`) ‚Äî move the current window ¬±1 index via the EXISTING `moveWindow(server, windowId, targetIndex)`, then navigate to the same stable window ID. These are **NEW entries added ALONGSIDE** the existing `Window: Move Left`/`Move Right` (Design Decision: additive, to avoid regressing the existing actions/tests) ‚Äî four palette entries now express two operations; the Left/Right pair is flagged as a future consolidation candidate (plan Deletion Candidates), NOT auto-deleted.

**`Board: Move up` / `Board: Move down`** (`board-move-up`/`-down`, `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`) ‚Äî the same boundary-hidden / no-wraparound keyboard+touch path for the board list, but mounted in `board-page.tsx`'s `boardRouteActions` (NOT `app.tsx`), because the board route does not render AppShell and "current board" only has meaning on a `/board/$name` route (mirrors DD-8, where the board owns its own palette). Each acts on the CURRENT board (the `/board/$name` param), computes the full new order via `computeMoveOrder(boardNames, currentBoardIdx, delta)` over the backend-sorted `boards`, and POSTs it via `setBoardOrder` (server-global `event: board-order` echo re-sorts every client ‚Äî see ¬ß Board-list drag reorder). Hidden when the current board is first (`currentBoardIdx === 0` ‚Üí only Move down) or last (only Move up); a `null` from `computeMoveOrder` is a defensive no-op. `onError` surfaces `useToast().addToast`.

**Pure order-computation helpers** ‚Äî the boundary gating, effective-order derivation, and swap arithmetic are extracted into `app/frontend/src/lib/palette-move.ts` (Vitest-covered `palette-move.test.ts`) so they are testable without mounting the shell; the palette action bodies are thin wrappers that call these then invoke the client mutation. Exports: `deriveEffectiveSessionOrder(liveNames, sseOrder)` (SSE-order-‚à™-natural), `computeMoveOrder(order, currentIdx, delta)` (insert-before splice, `null` on boundary/out-of-range ‚Äî shared by Server, Session, AND Board Move), and `computeWindowMoveTarget(index, delta, minIndex, maxIndex)` (target index, `null` on boundary ‚Äî shared by Window up/down AND Left/Right). `MoveDelta = -1 | 1`.

**Cross-session move actions**: Dynamically generated "Window: Move to {sessionName}" actions (id `move-window-to-session-{sessionName}`) ‚Äî one per session other than the current one. Only shown when `currentWindow` exists AND there are at least 2 sessions. On select, calls `moveWindowToSession(server, currentWindow.windowId, targetSession)` then navigates to `/$server` (server dashboard) because tmux auto-assigns the window index in the destination session and no `/$server/$session` route exists. Flat action list (not a sub-picker) ‚Äî works well for typical session counts (2-5) and requires zero changes to the command palette component.

### Keyboard Shortcuts Modal

`app/frontend/src/components/keyboard-shortcuts.tsx` ‚Äî opened via command palette "Keyboard Shortcuts" action. Fetches `GET /api/keybindings?server=...` on-demand each time (no caching). Displays bindings in three groups:

1. **App** ‚Äî hardcoded `Cmd+K` (command palette)
2. **tmux** ‚Äî root-table bindings displayed as bare key names (e.g., `F2`, `Shift+F3`)
3. **tmux (prefix)** ‚Äî prefix-table bindings displayed as `Ctrl+S, <key>` (e.g., `Ctrl+S, \`)

Key name formatting: `S-` ‚Üí `Shift+`, `C-` ‚Üí `Ctrl+`. Shows "Loading..." during fetch, "No tmux server running" when response is empty. Uses the shared `Dialog` component.

### Tmux Commands Dialog

`app/frontend/src/components/tmux-commands-dialog.tsx` ‚Äî opened via command palette "Copy: tmux Commands" action (id `copy-tmux-attach`). Only available on terminal pages when `currentWindow` exists. Opens a `Dialog` with title "tmux commands" showing three copyable tmux command rows:

| Label | Command |
|-------|---------|
| Attach | `tmux [-L {server}] attach-session -t {session}:{window}` |
| New window | `tmux [-L {server}] new-window -t {session}` |
| Detach | `tmux [-L {server}] detach-client -t {session}` |

**Server-aware command generation**: Commands include the `-L {server}` flag only when the server is not `"default"`. When the server is `"default"`, the flag is omitted. This matches the `tmuxExecServer` convention in the backend (see `tmux-sessions.md`).

Each row has a label (`text-text-secondary text-[11px]`), a monospace code block (`bg-bg-inset border border-border rounded px-2 py-1.5 font-mono text-[11px] select-all`), and a copy button. Clicking the copy button writes the command to the clipboard via `navigator.clipboard.writeText` and swaps the copy icon to a checkmark for 1.5 seconds before reverting. Clipboard failure is silently caught.

Dialog state is a `showTmuxCommands` boolean in `app.tsx` (same pattern as `showCreateServerDialog` / `showKillServerConfirm`). Props: `server`, `session`, `window`, `onClose`.

## Visual Design

Three theme modes: **system** (follows OS), **light**, **dark**. Default: system. Linear/Raycast aesthetic.

Theme is applied via `data-theme` attribute on `<html>` (`"dark"` or `"light"`). CSS custom properties in `globals.css` switch values per `html[data-theme="dark"]` and `html[data-theme="light"]` selectors. The `@theme` block registers token names for Tailwind CSS 4 with dark palette as initial values.

### Border-Width System

A three-tier border-width vocabulary (established/completed by `260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar`'s post-review chrome polish), all in `--color-border`:

- **1px hairlines** (`border` / `border-t` / `border-b`) ‚Äî the default: card borders, tile borders, in-panel dividers, dropdown separators, the `SectionHeading` rule (was the `PageHeading` rule, retired `260704-pr0p`).
- **3px structural seams** (`border-t-[3px]` / `border-b-[3px]` / `w-[3px]` / `border-[3px]`) ‚Äî the major chrome boundaries that partition the app frame: the topbar's bottom edge (`top-bar.tsx`, was `border-b-2`), both bottombars (`app.tsx` + `board-page.tsx`, each was `border-t`), the sidebar's inter-panel separators + Sessions-section top (`collapsible-panel.tsx` + `sidebar/index.tsx` ‚Äî these already used 3px, and the polish aligned the other seams to match them), the sidebar resize handle bar (`app.tsx`, was `w-[5px]`; see ¬ß Sidebar ‚Üí Desktop), and ‚Äî since `260706-y1ar` ‚Äî the **waiting board-pane seam** (`border-[3px]` + `rk-waiting-seam`; a pulsing yellow attention border, static under reduced-motion ‚Äî see ¬ß Attention Surfacing). The intent: seams read as deliberate structure, hairlines as content detail.
- **8px selection accent** (`borderLeft: 8px solid`) ‚Äî the contrast-guardrailed colored-row accent border (`computeRowBorders`; see ¬ß Contrast-guardrailed borders). The thickest tier ‚Äî a selection/identity signal, not a structural seam. The **sidebar window row no longer uses it** (the selection and active-board cues moved off the border in the axis split ‚Äî selection = 40% tint depth, active-board pin = accent glyph; ¬ß Row Anatomy); it remains on **server tiles** (stripe/edge).

### Color Tokens

| Token | Dark | Light | Usage |
|-------|------|-------|-------|
| `--color-bg-primary` | `#0f1117` | `#f8f9fb` | Page background |
| `--color-bg-card` | `#171b24` | `#ffffff` | Card backgrounds |
| `--color-bg-inset` | `#0a0c12` | `#e8eaef` | Fixed-width outer background |
| `--color-text-primary` | `#e8eaf0` | `#1a1d24` | Primary text |
| `--color-text-secondary` | `#7a8394` | `#6b7280` | Secondary text, labels |
| `--color-border` | `#454d66` | `#d1d5db` | Borders, dividers |
| `--color-accent` | `#5b8af0` | `#4a7ae8` | Active states, focus rings |
| `--color-accent-green` | `#22c55e` | `#16a34a` | Activity indicators |
| `--font-mono` | JetBrains Mono, etc. | (same) | Everywhere |

### Theme Switching

Preference persisted to backend API (`PUT /api/settings/theme` ‚Üí `~/.rk/settings.yaml`) with localStorage key `runkit-theme` as synchronous cache (values: any theme ID or `"system"`). On init, ThemeProvider calls `getThemePreference()` from API; falls back to localStorage / `"system"` if API fails. `setTheme` writes localStorage immediately and calls `setThemePreference(id)` fire-and-forget. Three switching surfaces: (1) command palette (`Cmd+K` ‚Üí "Theme: System/Light/Dark", current indicated with "(current)" suffix), (2) top-bar ThemeToggle button (since `260715-h1ck` the L3 registry `theme` candidate ‚Äî no longer `hidden sm:flex`-wrapped; below `sm` or under width pressure it overflows into the chevron menu as a "Theme: {current}" cycle row sharing the extracted `cycleTheme()`, so mobile is no longer theme-blind; cycles system ‚Üí default-light ‚Üí default-dark), and (3) Theme Selector modal (Ctrl+Click / Cmd+Click on ThemeToggle, or command palette "Theme: Select Theme").

### No-Flicker Initialization

A blocking inline `<script>` in `index.html` `<head>` reads `localStorage("runkit-theme")`, resolves system preference via `matchMedia`, and sets `data-theme` on `<html>` before first paint. Static fallback: `data-theme="dark"` on the `<html>` tag.

### PWA Meta Tags & Theme Color

`app/frontend/index.html` includes PWA-related tags in `<head>`:
- `<meta name="theme-color" content="#0f1117" />` ‚Äî initial value matching dark theme background
- `<meta name="apple-mobile-web-app-capable" content="yes" />` ‚Äî enables standalone mode on iOS
- `<meta name="apple-mobile-web-app-status-bar-style" content="black-translucent" />` ‚Äî content renders behind the status bar
- `<link rel="apple-touch-icon" href="/generated-icons/icon-192.png" />` ‚Äî homescreen icon for iOS

The `<link rel="manifest">` tag is injected automatically by `vite-plugin-pwa` during build.

**Theme-color synchronization**: The `theme-color` meta tag value is kept in sync with the active theme via two mechanisms:
1. **Initial load** ‚Äî the blocking inline script in `index.html` sets the `theme-color` meta tag alongside `data-theme` before first paint
2. **Runtime switch** ‚Äî `applyThemeToDOM` in `ThemeProvider` sets `theme-color` to `theme.palette.background` when the user changes theme

Theme color is per-theme (derived from `palette.background`), not a fixed dark/light pair.

**Icon set**: Canonical mark at `app/frontend/public/icon.svg` (hexagonal cube, transparent). Generated variants in `app/frontend/public/generated-icons/`:
- `favicon.svg` ‚Äî copy of `icon.svg` (transparent, used as browser favicon)
- `icon-192.png` ‚Äî 192x192, solid `#0f1117` background, ~20% padding (homescreen icon)
- `icon-512.png` ‚Äî 512x512, solid `#0f1117` background, ~20% padding (splash screen)
- `icon-512-maskable.png` ‚Äî 512x512, solid `#0f1117` background, ~40% padding (maskable, safe zone for adaptive icon shapes)

Generated by `scripts/generate-icons.sh` (Node + sharp). Run via `just icons`.

**Standalone display mode**: When installed via "Add to Home Screen" (Android or iOS), the app runs without browser chrome (no address bar, no toolbar). The `display: "standalone"` manifest property and `apple-mobile-web-app-capable` meta tag enable this on their respective platforms.

### ThemeProvider Context

`app/frontend/src/contexts/theme-context.tsx` ‚Äî split context (ThemeStateContext + ThemeActionsContext) following ChromeContext pattern. Provides `useTheme()` (preference + resolved + theme object) and `useThemeActions()` (setTheme, previewTheme, cancelPreview). Listens to `matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)")` change events when preference is "system" for real-time OS theme tracking. On init: calls `getThemePreference()` from API, falls back to localStorage / `"system"` if API fails. `setTheme` writes localStorage immediately and calls `setThemePreference(id)` fire-and-forget. `applyThemeToDOM` computes CSS values via `deriveUIColors(theme.palette, theme.category)` and sets `theme-color` meta tag to `theme.palette.background`.

Provider order: `ThemeProvider > ChromeProvider > SessionProvider > AppShell`.

### xterm Terminal Theme

`terminal-client.tsx` uses `useTheme()` to get the active `Theme` object. Initial theme set at Terminal construction via `deriveXtermTheme(activeTheme.palette)` ‚Äî all 22 colors (background, foreground, cursor, cursorAccent, selectionBackground, selectionForeground, and 16 named ANSI colors). Live updates via `xtermRef.current.options.theme = deriveXtermTheme(theme.palette)` in a `useEffect` ‚Äî no terminal recreation needed. The `XTERM_THEMES` constant has been removed.

### Terminal Relay (frontend) ‚Äî `RelayMux` singleton + `TerminalClient` port (`260717-803u-relay-mux`)

Since `260717-803u-relay-mux` the browser no longer opens a `/relay/{windowId}` WebSocket per pane. A **`RelayMux` singleton** (`src/lib/relay-mux.ts`, mirroring `state-socket.ts`) owns the ONE `/ws/terminals` socket per tab; each `TerminalClient` consumes a per-stream handle. This mirrors the state-socket transport swap (`260716-qf3j`) ‚Äî same URL-builder shape (`terminalsSocketURL()` vs `stateSocketURL()`), same backoff-reconnect + re-open-live-streams lifecycle, same singleton-per-tab ownership ‚Äî but carries bulk binary terminal I/O (kept a SEPARATE socket per D6; see `architecture.md` ¬ß Terminal Relay).

- **`openStream({server, windowId, cols, rows}) ‚Üí { send, resize, close, onData, onOpened, onClosed, setWindowId }`** ‚Äî allocates a fresh client-side u32 stream id and issues an `open` control op (once the socket is open, else re-issued in `ws.onopen`). `send` emits a binary `[u32 BE streamId][payload]` data frame (strings UTF-8-encoded ‚Äî the same wire form the old relay sent as a string frame); `resize`/`close` emit control ops; `onData` fires on inbound binary frames for that id; `onOpened` on the `opened` control event; `onClosed` on `closed` (carrying 4004/4001/1000). `onOpened` was added beyond the intake's listed handle shape ‚Äî seams 2/4 (below) need the re-open signal.
- **Backoff reconnect + re-open of live streams** ‚Äî on a SOCKET-level drop the mux reconnects with exponential backoff (`RECONNECT_BASE_MS = 1000` ‚Üí `RECONNECT_CAP_MS = 30000`) and, in `ws.onopen`, **re-issues `open` for every still-live stream** ‚Äî the server re-attaches (fresh PTY) and each pane's deferred reset (below) repaints on the incoming first data frame, so a reconnect is flicker-free with NO per-pane reconnect loop. An idle tab with zero live streams lets the socket stay closed. **Implemented reconnect wording (reconciling intake A-016)**: each live stream **REUSES its SAME stream id on the new connection** (ids are unique per-connection, so reusing them across a reconnect is valid) ‚Äî NOT "fresh ids"; a closed stream's id is simply retired.
- **`setWindowId(windowId)` ‚Äî the fresh-target seam (rework M1)** ‚Äî a same-session windowId ride updates the stream's `opts.windowId` WITHOUT a wire op (the live PTY already tracks the new active window). This keeps the stream's re-open target CURRENT: without it, a transient socket drop would re-`open` the STALE open-time window and `SelectWindowInSession` would yank the pane back. `cols`/`rows` stay fresh the same way via `resize()`, so `s.opts` is the single current source the mux re-issues `open` from.
- **A stream-level `closed` retires the stream client-side** (does NOT re-open ‚Äî unlike a socket drop): `onClosed` fires and the stream is deleted from the mux map.

**`TerminalClient` port ‚Äî the four delicate seams.** `terminal-client.tsx:813`'s `new WebSocket('/relay/...')` was the ONLY socket-creation site replaced. The stream handle is surfaced through the existing `wsRef` seam via a **WebSocket-shaped adapter** (`{ readyState, send, close }`) so the shell consumers (`BottomBar`, the docked compose strip, touch-scroll, `fitAndSync`) that read `wsRef.current.{send,readyState,close}` are UNTOUCHED (a `{type:"resize"}` JSON `send` routes to the stream's `resize` op, everything else to a binary data frame; the `adapter as unknown as WebSocket` double-cast is the documented tradeoff ‚Äî a structural `wsRef` type would remove it). The four seams:

1. **Confirmation-gated window-switch receipt = the stream's first DATA frame** (was the socket's `onmessage`) ‚Äî `notifyFirstWrite()` fires at the top of the stream's `onData` handler (`handleInbound`), before the write/coalesce decision. The gate state machine (`260715-38kg`) is pure; only the receipt source changed. See ¬ß Window-Switch Slide Transition.
2. **Connect-select alignment epoch anchors on `open`‚Üí`opened`** ‚Äî the deferred reset is armed and the grid re-fit/re-synced in `stream.onOpened` (which fires on the initial open AND every transparent re-open). Because the server enqueues `opened` on the stream's own queue ahead of any data (`architecture.md` ¬ß Terminal Relay, M2), the epoch is soundly ordered in-band; the old socket-`onmessage`-races-the-select-POST hazard (memory `relay-connect-select-alignment`) is structurally gone.
3. **IntersectionObserver pane suspension = stream `close`/`open`** (no socket churn) ‚Äî see ¬ß Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension.
4. **Deferred per-stream reset** ‚Äî the deferred per-connection reset (below) is now per-stream, re-armed in `stream.onOpened`.

**Non-4004 `closed` self-heal (rework S1).** RelayMux re-opens only on a SOCKET drop, not a stream-level `closed`, so the client owns per-stream recovery: a `closed` with code 4004 prints `[session not found]` and fires `onSessionNotFound` (redirect); a non-4004 close (4001 attach-failed, 1000 PTY-EOF/graceful) prints `[reconnecting‚Ä¶]` and **probes exactly ONE fresh re-open of the current window** (bounded by a `probedReopen` flag). A genuinely gone window then 4004s the probe ‚Üí redirect; a transient one re-attaches. A second non-4004 close prints `[disconnected]` and stops (no spin on a hard-failing window). This restores the old per-pane self-heal without a per-pane reconnect loop.

**Tab budget.** With the state socket (`260716-qf3j`) the tab now holds a fixed **2 WebSockets** (state + terminals) and zero SSE ‚Äî the e2e connection guard (`connection-budget.spec.ts`) asserts exactly this. See `architecture.md` ¬ß Terminal Relay for the backend/protocol.

### Terminal Write Batching (Adaptive Flush + Deferred Reset)

Inbound terminal data in `terminal-client.tsx` ‚Äî a `RelayMux` stream's inbound binary frames since `260717-803u-relay-mux` (was per-pane relay-WebSocket data) ‚Äî flows through an **adaptive flush** (PR #244, with WebGL-renderer confirmation + context-loss survival in PR #245 ‚Äî shipped outside the fab pipeline), replacing the original always-rAF coalescing from `260327-cnav-perf-frontend-rendering`:

- **Immediate path** ‚Äî a chunk that is small (‚â§ `IMMEDIATE_WRITE_MAX_BYTES` = 64 **UTF-8 bytes**), arrives while **idle** (nothing buffered, no flush pending), and is the **first immediate write this frame** is written synchronously so a keystroke echo paints on the same tick (latency attribution showed the rAF tail dominated perceived input latency ~3:1 over the network hop; keystroke‚Üíecho went 40‚Üí10ms). The threshold is measured in UTF-8 bytes via `textByteLength` ‚Äî `String.length` UTF-16 units would under-count multibyte input and weaken the flood guard; the helper only pays for a `TextEncoder` encode in the ambiguous middle band, keeping the tiny-ASCII hot path allocation-free. The one-immediate-write-per-frame guard is `wroteImmediatelyThisFrame`, set by `markImmediateWrite()` and cleared by a one-shot rAF ‚Äî a program emitting one byte at a time still coalesces after its first byte of the frame.
- **Coalesced path** ‚Äî everything else (large chunk, already buffering, or a second small chunk in the same frame) accumulates in buffers (string concatenation for text, `Uint8Array[]` for binary) and flushes once per `requestAnimationFrame` (`flushToTerminal`), batching floods (builds, log tailing, `cat largefile`) into one xterm render pass per frame.
- **Ordering guarantee** ‚Äî terminal bytes are order-sensitive: the moment anything is buffered, every subsequent chunk buffers until the buffer drains; an immediate write only happens when the buffer is empty AND no flush is pending, so a synchronous write can never jump ahead of buffered bytes.
- **Close-time drain** ‚Äî the stream's `onClosed` handler cancels pending rAFs and calls `flushToTerminal()` (try/catch for a disposed terminal) **before** the `cancelled` check, so a transient-drop reconnect never loses tail data; `cancelAnimationFrame()` also runs on effect cleanup. *(Under the mux, a socket-level drop is transparent ‚Äî RelayMux re-opens and the pane repaints on the first data frame ‚Äî so `onClosed` fires only for stream-level closes; the close-time drain still runs before the S1 probe re-open, above.)*

**Deferred per-stream reset** (`260610-qf25-defer-terminal-reset-flicker`; became per-stream in `260717-803u-relay-mux`): each (re)open arms an effect-scoped `pendingReset` flag ‚Äî armed in the stream's `onOpened` (was `connect()`); `consumePendingReset()` (check + clear + `terminal.reset()`) runs **exactly once per stream open, immediately before that open's FIRST chunk write** ‚Äî in the same tick on the immediate path, at the top of the same rAF callback (same frame) on the coalesced path ‚Äî so clear + repaint land in **one presented frame**. The previous receipt-time reset (in the old socket's `onmessage`) guaranteed ‚â•1 fully-cleared frame whenever the first chunk took the coalesced path (a redraw is >64 bytes, so it always did): the wipe was synchronous but the repaint waited for the next animation frame. That cleared frame was the window-switch black-frame flicker. Post-change, the old content persists until the new redraw paints ‚Äî strictly better perceptually on every re-open path (sidebar click, tmux status-bar click, palette, board pane churn, transient socket-drop re-open, S1 probe re-open). **Ordering dependency**: arming on `onOpened` is only sound because the server enqueues `opened` ahead of the first data frame (`architecture.md` ¬ß Terminal Relay, M2) ‚Äî a data-before-`opened` frame would fire the reset AFTER the first repaint and wipe it.

**Handoff semantics**: an **empty flush neither consumes nor executes a pending reset** ‚Äî `flushToTerminal` early-returns when both buffers are empty, so a zero-data stream's close-time drain is a no-op (resetting with nothing to repaint would recreate the flicker); the next open simply re-arms in `onOpened`, idempotently. The **effect cleanup additionally neutralizes the closure's pending write state** (`pendingReset = false; binaryBuffers = []`): a late-delivered `onClosed`/`onData` ‚Äî which can arrive AFTER cleanup, and whose drain runs before the `cancelled` check so same-effect transient-drop tail drains keep working ‚Äî can therefore neither reset the shared terminal nor write stale old-window content after a successor effect (e.g. a `windowId` change forcing a fresh stream) has taken over. Reset-ordering unit tests live in `terminal-client.test.tsx` (no receipt-time reset; exactly once per stream open; string + binary first chunks; re-armed on re-open; zero-data close; post-consumption tail drain ‚Äî now asserting against the mocked `RelayMux`/stream handle rather than a raw `MockWebSocket` URL).

**Relay connection identity is (server, owning session), NOT windowId** (`260610-9umy-skip-same-session-reconnect`; the transport became a `RelayMux` stream in `260717-803u-relay-mux`): the stream-open effect's deps are `[terminalReady, server, wsRef, connectionEpoch]` ‚Äî `sessionName` and `windowId` are deliberately excluded (the `eslint-disable react-hooks/exhaustive-deps` comment explains why). A same-session windowId switch (sidebar click, palette, URL writeback after a tmux-status-bar click) **rides the existing stream**: tmux has already switched the active window in place (or will, via the REST `selectWindow` already fired by `navigateToWindow` and mount-time alignment in app.tsx) and the directly-attached PTY (since `260602-qn62`) redraws by itself ‚Äî no stream close/open, no `terminal.reset()`, and **xterm scrollback is preserved** across same-session switches (native `tmux attach` behavior). A dedicated `windowId`-keyed effect calls **`streamRef.current.setWindowId(windowId)`** on every ride so the mux's re-open target stays current (rework M1 ‚Äî was previously a stale `windowIdRef`-only concern; now the fresh-target is pushed into the live stream). Any GENUINE reconnect ‚Äî session change, server change, transient socket drop ‚Äî attaches to the latest window: the epoch-bumping paths re-open a fresh stream reading `windowIdRef.current`, and a socket drop's re-`open` reads the stream's `setWindowId`-kept-fresh `opts.windowId`.

Identity is tracked by `connectedSessionRef` (session the live connection serves; `""` = resolved server-side only) + `connectedServerRef` + a `connectionEpoch` state bumped by a **session-identity watcher** effect on `[sessionName, server]`. The watcher is declared BEFORE the connect effect ‚Äî ordering is load-bearing: on a same-commit server+session change it must read the PRE-change server from `connectedServerRef` (the connect effect overwrites it) to skip its bump, since the connect effect already re-runs via its own `server` dep ‚Äî bumping too would tear down and reconnect twice. Watcher direction semantics:

- **`""` ‚Üí resolved: absorption only** (record, never bump). On a cold deep-link the SSE-derived `sessionName` prop is `""` until the first snapshot; the client connects immediately by windowId and the relay resolves the owning session server-side (`ResolveWindowSession`) ‚Äî by construction the live connection is already attached to that window's owning session, so the resolution transition costs no reconnect.
- **resolved ‚Üí resolved: bump** ‚Äî cross-session navigation, or a window moved to another session. A session RENAME also lands here and reconnects ‚Äî accepted tradeoff: the SSE snapshot carries no stable session id to tell a rename from a genuine session change, renames are rare, and the deferred reset keeps any reconnect flicker-free.
- **resolved ‚Üí `""`: LOSS-OF-IDENTITY signal** ‚Äî record `""` AND bump for a probe reconnect. `sessionName` is derived by locating the URL's `@N` in the SSE snapshot, so it goes `""` and STAYS `""` when the viewed window left the snapshot: killed externally, pinned to a filtered `_rk-pin-*` session (pin transitions present as resolved ‚Üí `""`, never resolved ‚Üí resolved), or a dead deep link. The probe (by `windowIdRef.current`) either re-resolves the owning session server-side (an X ‚Üí `""` ‚Üí X ghost gap during navigation costs one flicker-free reconnect) or the relay closes 4004 ‚Üí the `onSessionNotFound` redirect fires. This is the ONLY reachable recovery path in that state ‚Äî `computeKillRedirect` and the URL writeback are both gated on a non-empty `sessionName` ‚Äî so the bump is load-bearing (review finding M1, fixed in rework cycle 1: the original "treat `""` as inert in both directions" wedged the UI on kill-while-viewing).
- **`""` ‚Üí `""`: no-op** (cold mount, still unresolved).

Deferred-reset and adaptive-flush semantics are unchanged on every stream open that IS established (cross-session switch, server change, transient drop re-open, S1 probe re-open). Connection-lifecycle unit tests live in the "TerminalClient connection identity" block of `terminal-client.test.tsx` (same-session switch keeps the stream + pushes `setWindowId`; cross-session switch closes old + opens exactly one new with the deferred reset before its first write; `""` ‚Üí resolved no-reconnect with later genuine change reconnecting; server change reconnects exactly once ‚Äî no watcher double-bump; resolved ‚Üí `""` probe; 4004 recovery after an external kill; S1's non-4004 feedback + one-probe path). The **transient-drop-latest-windowId** assertion is now split across the seam: `terminal-client.test.tsx` pins the same-session ride pushing `setWindowId("@5")` into the live stream, and `relay-mux.test.ts` pins the socket-drop reconnect re-issuing `open` with the ridden-to windowId (`relay-mux.test.ts` also unit-tests framing, id-demuxed data in/out, and `opened`/`closed` dispatch against a stubbed WebSocket).

### Window-Switch Slide Transition

Since `260703-l4nf-window-switch-slide-transition` a same-server window switch animates as a **vertical slide** of the terminal surface via the browser's [View Transitions API](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/View_Transitions_API), keyed off the two windows' positions in the flattened sidebar order (macOS-Spaces-like, but vertical because the sidebar arranges windows vertically). It is **fire-and-forget** (a play-on-switch animation), NOT a gesture-scrubbed interactive drag. It is pure UX polish and layers ON TOP of the deferred-reset / relay-identity machinery above ‚Äî a same-session switch still rides the existing socket with no reconnect; the slide just animates the in-place repaint. Progressive enhancement: any gate failure falls through to today's instant switch, byte-identical.

> **Evolution ‚Äî the slide is now an EARNED signal (`260715-38kg-window-switch-confirmed-motion`).** The mechanics below (the one seam, the gate, direction, CSS, the first-paint gate) are the `l4nf` foundation and remain accurate ‚Äî but `38kg` made the slide play ONLY on confirmed-fast arrival and layered on a pending spinner mask + a failure bounce-back. Read the l4nf mechanics here first, then ¬ß Confirmation-gated motion below for what changed. The single behavioral delta to keep straight while reading l4nf: `waitForFirstWrite()` no longer resolves `void` ‚Äî it resolves a `GateSettleReason` (`"first-write" | "timeout" | "superseded"`), and the wrapper now `skipTransition()`s on every non-`"first-write"` settle instead of always playing the slide.

**The one seam ‚Äî `navigateToWindow`.** The wrapper lives on `navigateToWindow` (`app.tsx`) alone ‚Äî the single same-server switch seam shared by sidebar clicks, command-palette `Window: Switch to ‚Ä¶` entries (keyboard path, constitution V), TopBar breadcrumb navigation, and SessionTiles clicks ‚Äî so the animation applies identically to keyboard- and mouse-driven switches. The instant-switch body is factored into a `runSwitch()` closure (optimistic `navigate` + `selectWindow` POST + mobile sidebar close); the wrapper either calls it directly (fallback) or runs it inside `document.startViewTransition`'s async callback (see the timing caveat in ¬ß URL as Resumable Bookmark ‚Äî on the animated path `runSwitch` runs ‚â•1 frame after the click). `runSwitch` **returns the `selectWindow` POST** so the gate can wait until tmux has been told to switch. **Direct `startViewTransition`, NOT TanStack Router's `viewTransition: true` option** ‚Äî the polished first-paint gate (below) needs the async-callback seam to await a custom signal, which the router option does not expose.

**Gate (`shouldAnimateWindowSwitch`).** The switch animates only when ALL hold: View Transitions supported (`viewTransitionSupported()` ‚Äî a plain-`boolean` `typeof document.startViewTransition === "function"` check, NOT a type predicate; the TS 5.7+ `dom` lib already declares the API, so no ambient augmentation and no `as` cast ‚Äî code-quality type-narrowing), `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` NOT set (checked via a **guarded** `matchMedia` ‚Äî `typeof window.matchMedia === "function"`, for jsdom/older-WebView envs), an outgoing terminal window is in view (`windowParam`/`currentWindowId` non-empty ‚Äî a first switch from SessionTiles with no outgoing surface skips), and the slide direction is non-null. Any failure ‚Üí `runSwitch()` directly (instant switch, unchanged). Cross-server navigation takes the separate `navigate` branch in `handleSidebarSelectWindow`, never `navigateToWindow`, so it falls out with no transition and no code change; board routes and the Host page are untouched.

**Direction ‚Äî flattened SSE sidebar order ‚Üí root data attribute.** `windowSwitchDirection(order, currentId, targetId)` (pure, exported, in `src/lib/window-transition.ts`, colocated `.test.ts` ‚Äî the same pure-helper pattern as `resolveServerView`/`computeKillRedirect`) returns `"up"` when the target sits BELOW current (new content enters from the bottom), `"down"` when ABOVE, and `null` when either id is missing from the order or the ids are equal (‚Üí skip). `order` is `flatWindows.map((fw) => fw.window.windowId)` read from a render-synced `switchTransitionRef` (so the click handler reads current order without re-creating the callback). The resolved direction is written to `document.documentElement.dataset.windowSwitchDirection = "up" | "down"` immediately before `startViewTransition` (the `data-theme` root-attribute pattern); the CSS pseudo-elements key off `:root[data-window-switch-direction=‚Ä¶]`. **Accepted divergence:** `flatWindows` is raw SSE order, while the sidebar's drag-reorder override (`orderOverrideRef`) is component-local, so during a transient drag-reorder window the slide direction may briefly disagree with the visual sidebar order until SSE confirms ‚Äî rare and self-healing.

**Direction-attribute latest-wins guard.** The attribute is cleared in `transition.finished.finally()`. But `finished` **FULFILLS on skip** (a rapid second switch supersedes this transition) ‚Äî it does not reject ‚Äî so a superseded transition's `finally()` would otherwise delete the attribute its successor already set, dropping the successor's direction CSS. Guard: each switch mints a monotonic token via `nextDirectionToken()` and clears the attribute only when `isLatestDirectionToken(token)` ‚Äî only the LATEST switch's cleanup may clear it (mirrors the gate's still-points-at-itself pattern; pure module state, no DOM).

**CSS (`globals.css`) ‚Äî pure transform + containment + full UA-animation neutralization.** `view-transition-name: terminal-surface` is on the terminal content container `<div>` (the shared wrapper around the `TerminalClient`/`IframeWindow` branch, merged with the fixed-width style) so **only the terminal region slides** ‚Äî sidebar, top bar, bottom bar stay static. `::view-transition-old/new(terminal-surface)` animate via pure `translateY` keyframes, **180ms ease-out**, up/down variants keyed off the root attribute. Transform-only means **no layout change** ‚Äî the container's `ResizeObserver`/`fitAndSync` path never fires, so tmux sees NO resize churn during the slide (hard constraint). Two non-obvious rules, both probe-verified:
- **Containment:** `::view-transition-image-pair(terminal-surface) { overflow: clip; }` ‚Äî without it the translating snapshots escape the terminal group and paint over the top bar / bottom bar / sidebar (the UA does no clipping on the pseudo-tree by default).
- **Full UA-default neutralization for LIFETIME, not just visuals:** `::view-transition-old/new(root)` AND `::view-transition-old/new(terminal-surface)` AND `::view-transition-group(root), ::view-transition-group(terminal-surface)` ALL get `animation: none`. The group rule is the load-bearing one: `animation: none` on old/new alone does NOT shorten the transition ‚Äî the UA's default **~250ms `::view-transition-group(*)` animations** hold the whole pseudo-tree (and thus the pointer-dead window and `transition.finished`) alive ~250‚Äì290ms past the 180ms slide. Neutralizing the group animations makes the 180ms slide govern the transition's whole lifetime.

**First-paint gate (`SwitchGate` in `window-transition.ts`) ‚Äî the polished variant.** The new-state snapshot is gated on the incoming window's first inbound bytes so the surface slides in painted, not blank, with a **~300ms budget measured from callback entry**. Mechanics, in one module:
- `beginWindowSwitchGate()` opens a per-transition gate (a distinct token) and **FIRES any prior still-pending gate on supersession** ‚Äî so rapid switches never serialize: the VT spec queues a second `startViewTransition` callback behind the first's returned promise, and the first callback holds that promise open while awaiting its gate, so firing the prior gate lets the queued second callback run at once. This call is load-bearing on BOTH the terminal AND iframe paths (a terminal‚Üíiframe switch must fire an in-flight terminal gate), so it runs before branching on iframe-vs-terminal.
- The callback does NOT `await` the `selectWindow` POST ‚Äî it **chains `openForNotify()` off it** (`void posted.then(() => gate.openForNotify()).catch(() => {})`) and awaits only `gate.waitForFirstWrite()`, whose timeout clock starts at callback entry. This hard-caps the callback (and thus document-wide render suppression) at ~300ms **regardless of the POST's fate** ‚Äî a stalled `selectWindow` (no client fetch timeout) can no longer freeze the document up to Chromium's ~4s VT deadline, and a rapid second switch never queues behind a stalled POST. `openForNotify` is the identity filter: only writes arriving AFTER the POST resolves count, so a busy OUTGOING window's still-streaming bytes (a same-session switch rides the existing socket) can't release the gate before tmux has run `select-window`.
- `settleGate` resolves the pending promise, clears the timer, and relinquishes the module slot **only when it still points at that gate** (still-points-at-itself) ‚Äî a late timeout from a superseded gate can neither resolve nor null a newer gate.
- **Release is at message-RECEIPT time ‚Äî `notifyFirstWrite()` at the TOP of the stream's `onData` handler (`handleInbound`) in `terminal-client.tsx`, before the write/coalesce decision ‚Äî NOT at write time.** Since `260717-803u-relay-mux` the receipt source is the stream's first DATA frame (inbound frames are always binary under the mux ‚Äî the old text/binary two-branch `ws.onmessage` collapsed to one `onData`); the seam and its load-bearing timing are otherwise byte-identical to `l4nf`. This is the load-bearing subtlety: `startViewTransition` suppresses rendering while its callback runs, and **rAF callbacks do not fire during suppression**. The coalesced flush (`flushToTerminal`) is reachable only via `scheduleFlush`'s `requestAnimationFrame`, and a tmux redraw's first chunk (~4KB) always exceeds `IMMEDIATE_WRITE_MAX_BYTES` (64) ‚Äî so a write-time signal is structurally unreleasable on the common path, and every animated switch would degenerate into the full 300ms freeze. `onData` is a macrotask and DOES run during suppression; releasing there is safe for capture correctness because the pending rAF flush runs at the first rendering opportunity after the callback resolves ‚Äî the same rendering update in which the new state is captured, so the received bytes are painted into the captured frame. **Distinguish this receipt-time NOTIFY (the transition first-paint gate) from the deferred per-stream RESET (`consumePendingReset`, above)** ‚Äî different mechanisms at different seams: the reset fires once per stream open before its first chunk write, the notify fires at receipt time.
- **iframe targets** (`switchTransitionRef.iframeIds`) have no terminal receipt seam, so they use the **ungated capture** (skip the wait entirely). Since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` (spec R12) the predicate is the **effective resolved view**, not raw `rkType && rkUrl`: a target is an iframe target iff `resolveView(undefined, readStoredView(server, fw.window.windowId), fw.window) === "web"` (the URL `?view=` param is unknown for a not-yet-navigated target, so it resolves from localStorage + the window's default hint only). This keeps a `web`-rendering target on the ungated path AND ‚Äî critically ‚Äî keeps an **iframe-typed window whose last-view is `tty`** (or one with no `rkUrl`) on the **gated terminal path**, exactly where it renders a `TerminalClient`. Getting this wrong reintroduces the blank-pane/stuck-transition class of bugs this section documents ‚Äî hence its own R12 task + e2e switch coverage. Because both the render branch and this classification call the same `resolveView`, the two can't drift.

**Accepted trade-offs.** (1) During the ~180ms slide the VT snapshot pseudo-element hit-tests to `<html>`, so a click landing on the terminal region mid-transition is lost ‚Äî a brief **whole-document pointer-input dead window**. Keyboard input is unaffected (it targets the focused element, not a hit-tested point), so keyboard-first flows (constitution V) never lose input. (2) The direction-vs-sidebar-drag divergence noted above.

**Testing.** `playwright.config.ts` sets reduced-motion globally so existing window-switch e2e specs run against instant switches (the product's own fallback), unchanged. **Trap worth recording:** `reducedMotion` is NOT a top-level `use` fixture in Playwright 1.59.1 ‚Äî it is **silently ignored** there and only reaches the browser context via `contextOptions`, so the config uses `use: { contextOptions: { reducedMotion: "reduce" } }` (the top-level form is a no-op AND tsc-unchecked, since the config sits outside the tsconfig include). One dedicated animated-path spec `app/frontend/tests/e2e/window-switch-transition.spec.ts` (+ companion `.spec.md` per constitution Test Companion Docs) opts back in via `test.use({ contextOptions: { reducedMotion: "no-preference" } })`, performs a same-session switch, and asserts the incoming window's content paints AND `data-window-switch-direction` clears within ~1s ‚Äî guarding against a regression that re-introduces a systematic gate-timeout freeze. Colocated Vitest unit tests cover `windowSwitchDirection` (up/down/missing/equal cases), `shouldAnimateWindowSwitch` (each gate branch), `viewTransitionSupported`, the full gate API (open-for-notify filtering, timeout, supersession-fires-pending, stale-timer isolation, stalled-POST bounded wait), and the direction-token latest-wins guard.

#### Confirmation-gated motion ‚Äî the slide is an EARNED signal (`260715-38kg-window-switch-confirmed-motion`)

The `l4nf` slide fired at click time whenever its preconditions held, even into unconfirmed content ‚Äî on a slow/failed switch the same-session pane kept showing the OLD window's bytes while the slide "animated" them, and a silent `selectWindow` failure parked the URL/heading in an indefinite limbo (input hazard: keystrokes went to the OLD window). `38kg` makes each visual state an **honest, distinct signal**:

| Signal | Meaning |
|--------|---------|
| slide | confirmed arrival (bytes within the 300ms budget) |
| spinner mask | in transit ‚Äî don't type |
| spinner ‚Üí content cut | arrived late |
| spinner ‚Üí bounce + toast | switch failed |

Optimistic navigation is UNCHANGED (heading/URL still flip at click = acknowledged intent; sidebar highlight stays SSE-derived = confirmation). Pessimistic navigation and a dimmed overlay were both rejected in the design. Frontend-only at `38kg` ‚Äî `terminal-client.tsx` was untouched then, the `notifyFirstWrite()` call being reused verbatim as the ONE arrival signal. *(The gate machine remained pure across `260717-803u-relay-mux`; only the receipt SOURCE moved ‚Äî from the socket's `onmessage` to the RelayMux stream's first `onData` frame ‚Äî see the first-paint-gate release bullet above. Behavior is preserved, guarded by the window-switch-transition e2e suite.)*

**Gate settle reasons (`window-transition.ts`).** `waitForFirstWrite()` resolves a `GateSettleReason = "first-write" | "timeout" | "superseded"` (was `void`). `settleGate(gate, reason)` carries the reason from its three callers: `notifyFirstWrite` ‚Üí `"first-write"`, the gate timer ‚Üí `"timeout"`, supersession by a newer `beginWindowSwitchGate`/`armGraceMask` ‚Üí `"superseded"`. `FIRST_WRITE_TIMEOUT_MS = 300` is UNCHANGED (forced by VT render suppression ‚Äî must not be extended). All three `l4nf` concurrency guarantees are preserved verbatim (supersession fires the prior pending gate immediately; only the INCOMING window's post-POST bytes release the gate; the still-points-at-itself guard means a stale timer never clobbers a newer gate ‚Äî and now never touches the newer gate's mask).

**`skipTransition()` on EVERY non-`first-write` settle.** In `navigateToWindow`'s VT callback the wrapper awaits the reason and calls `transition.skipTransition()` whenever `reason !== "first-write"` (`app.tsx`). This covers `"timeout"` (cut to the masked new state ‚Äî no motion into unconfirmed content) AND `"superseded"`, which has TWO cases: a rapid successor VT (the VT spec already skips this transition, so the explicit call is a harmless no-op) AND an **abandoned/bounced** switch ‚Äî `abandonSwitchFeedback()` settles a still-pending gate `"superseded"` with NO successor VT, so WITHOUT the explicit skip the failed switch would animate alongside its own failure feedback (slide = confirmed arrival, so a failed switch must never slide). The `"first-write"` fast path is byte-identical to `l4nf`. Note SSE-confirm deliberately settles `"first-write"` (via `confirmSwitchArrived`, below): an authoritative arrival IS a confirmed arrival, so its slide is correct.

**The LogoSpinner pending mask ‚Äî pure module state machine + a `useSyncExternalStore` seam.** The mask is expressed as pure, DOM-free, unit-testable module logic in `window-transition.ts` (NOT React `useState` in the wrapper ‚Äî that would duplicate arm/lift/teardown and reintroduce gate‚Üîmask drift): a `MaskState = "idle" | "masked"` with `getMaskState()` + `subscribeMaskState(listener)` (the `useSyncExternalStore` contract ‚Äî snapshot stable while unchanged, listeners fire only on an actual transition). `app.tsx` reads it via `useSyncExternalStore(subscribeMaskState, getMaskState)` and, when `"masked"`, renders an absolutely-positioned full-cover `<div className="rk-window-switch-mask" role="status">` with a centered `<LogoSpinner size={48}>` over the `terminal-surface` container (which gained `position: relative`). It FULLY hides the stale bytes (a full mask, never a dimmed overlay) and sits at `z-index: 40` (below the `z-50` toast container).
- **Armed ONLY at the 300ms gate-timeout decision ‚Äî NEVER at click time.** The mask arms as a side effect of `settleGate` when `reason === "timeout"` AND the gate was created `gated` (tty). Arming there, not in the wrapper after the await, makes the "never at click time" invariant structural (during the VT callback the screen is frozen on the old snapshot anyway, so early masking gains nothing). `beginWindowSwitchGate({ gated })` carries the tty flag; the wrapper passes `{ gated: !targetUngated }` (the `ungatedIds` classification, ¬ß Window Views ‚Üí Window-switch transition classification ‚Äî web/chat targets never mask and never reach a timeout settle).
- **POST-filtered lift via epoch + `liftAccepting`.** The SAME `notifyFirstWrite` receipt that releases the gate ALSO lifts the mask on late arrival ("one signal drives everything") ‚Äî but the lift is FILTERED exactly like the gate release: a byte counts only once the switch's `selectWindow` POST has resolved. A module-level `liftAccepting` flag is `false` from switch start until the switch opens it (`openForNotify()` on the gate path chains off the POST; `openForLift()` on the grace path ‚Äî see below), guarded by a monotonic `switchEpoch` minted per switch so a STALE switch's late POST resolution can never enable lifts for a NEWER switch's mask. Without the filter, a busy OUTGOING window's still-streaming bytes (a same-session switch rides the same socket) would un-mask stale content before tmux ever ran `select-window` ‚Äî the exact hazard being fixed.
- **Input block while masked.** The overlay's `pointer-events: auto` swallows clicks on the old window; keyboard is blocked by a capture-phase `onKeyDownCapture` on the `terminal-surface` container that `preventDefault()`+`stopPropagation()`s keystrokes (dropped, NOT buffered/replayed ‚Äî replay into the new window would be its own surprise). **Global chords are EXEMPT** via the pure `isMaskExemptKey(e)` predicate (constitution V ‚Äî Cmd+K is the primary discovery mechanism, and the swallow could otherwise kill it for up to the 5s confirmation window): `Escape`; meta (Cmd) chords EXCEPT `Cmd+V` (xterm doesn't forward meta-modified keys to the pty, but the browser's default paste DOES land in xterm's focused textarea ‚Üí the old pty, so paste stays swallowed); and the specific Ctrl-bound globals `Ctrl+K`/`.`/`\`/`` ` `` with `!altKey` required (AltGr reports `ctrlKey:true` and AltGr+char is typed INPUT, not a chord ‚Äî same modifier discipline as `use-chat-view-shortcut.ts`). Plain typing and terminal control bytes (Ctrl+C) stay dropped.
- **Lift is a CUT (a fast fade-in only), never a second slide.** `.rk-window-switch-mask` has a 120ms `rk-window-switch-mask-in` fade-IN; the lift is a plain unmount. Under `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` the mask STILL shows (input safety is never motion-only) but the fade is dropped (`animation: none`). **Ordering matters (rework G4):** the base rule + keyframes sit BEFORE the reduced-motion block, so the equal-specificity `animation: none` override wins by later source order (the same discipline as `.rk-waiting-halo`).
- **`abandonSwitchFeedback()` teardown ‚Äî settles the gate, not just the mask.** The failure/bounce and route-leave/unmount paths call `abandonSwitchFeedback()` (NOT a bare `tearDownMask()`): it settles a still-pending gate `"superseded"` AND tears the mask down. A bare unmask would leave the pending gate armed ‚Äî a `selectWindow` POST that rejects INSIDE the 300ms budget bounces first, then the gate's timer fires `settleGate(gate, "timeout")` and re-arms a mask over the bounced-back window with NO lift path (`liftAccepting` stays false after a rejected POST), a permanently stuck input-blocking mask (rework G2). `confirmSwitchArrived()` is the sibling authority-confirmed teardown: it settles a still-pending gate `"first-write"` (so its slide is correct) and tears down any mask ‚Äî closing the real gap where a same-session tmux redraw completes BEFORE `openForNotify` (those bytes filtered as outgoing), leaving no later write to lift and letting the gate arm a mask over a switch that DID land. `tearDownMask()` itself is now effectively module-internal (kept exported for unit tests only; production callers use the two above ‚Äî the plan's resolved narrowing candidate, per T012/N1).

**Failure bounce-back ‚Äî un-sticking the silent-failure limbo.** `CONFIRMATION_WINDOW_MS = 5000` (named tunable) arms a SINGLE `setTimeout` per pending switch (NOT a poll ‚Äî SSE stays the confirmation source). The bounce fires on an explicit `selectWindow` POST rejection OR the confirmation-window timeout ‚Äî **NEVER** merely because SSE still reports the old window mid-switch. `bouncePendingSwitch(target)` clears `pendingClickRef`, calls `abandonSwitchFeedback()`, explicitly `navigate`s (replace) to tmux's actual active window (a stale `activeWindow` won't retrigger the writeback effect), and `addToast("Window switch didn't confirm ‚Äî back to the active window", "error")`.
- **Server-scoped identity at all FOUR seams (rework H1, cycle 3).** `pendingClickRef` is a `PendingSwitchTarget = { server, windowId }` compared via the pure `isSamePendingTarget(pending, server, windowId)` at: (1) the mount-alignment skip, (2) the writeback's `urlMatchesPending`, (3) the writeback's `sseConfirmed`, and (4) `bouncePendingSwitch`'s guard. tmux `@N` ids are only unique per server and `AppShell` persists across `$server` changes, so a window-id-alone match false-positives on a cross-server collision (serverA `@5` vs serverB `@5`) ‚Äî see ¬ß Click-intent and URL-match above. `bouncePendingSwitch` additionally clears SILENTLY (no toast, no navigation) when the recorded server no longer matches the live route (`serverRef.current !== target.server`), and its navigate uses `target.server` only after verifying it equals the live route server ‚Äî a stale-server navigation is structurally inexpressible.
- **Three teardown effects, each a distinct route topology.** (a) **Server-change** (`$server` param change) ‚Äî declared BEFORE the alignment effect (effects run in declaration order within a commit) so the skip sees a cleared intent and serverB's alignment fires; prev-ref keyed so it no-ops on mount. (b) **Route-leave** (`!windowParam` ‚Äî windowless `/$server` SessionTiles, where the writeback can early-return) so a straggler timer can't navigate the user back with a spurious toast. (c) **Unmount** (Host `/` or a board route unmounts AppShell, but the setTimeout closure + module mask state outlive the instance). All three call `abandonSwitchFeedback()`. These are NOT subsumed by one another.
- **`beginPendingSwitch(target, { posted, graceMask })`** is the one entry point that records the intent, supersedes prior tracking, arms the confirmation timer, and (instant path only) arms the grace mask + wires `openForLift` off the POST. Its explicit-rejection handler is keyed on the **tracked object identity** (`pendingSwitchRef.current === tracked`, the still-points-at-itself pattern), NOT the windowId ‚Äî so a superseded POST's late rejection can't bounce a newer healthy switch (rework SF8). It is called from the click path (`runSwitch`), the deep-link mount-alignment effect (no grace mask ‚Äî a cold deep-link mounts a fresh connecting pane, not stale bytes), and `navigateToWaitingTarget`'s same-server branch (no grace mask). The mount-alignment effect SKIPS re-tracking when `isSamePendingTarget(pendingClickRef.current, server, windowParam)` ‚Äî a click already recorded the intent, and re-tracking would fire a DUPLICATE `selectWindow` POST and (via `beginPendingSwitch`'s supersession) cancel the click's just-armed grace mask, making the instant-path mask dead in the live app (rework G1, the cycle-2 must-fix that made the instant path actually work).

**Non-VT / reduced-motion grace-timer parity (`armGraceMask`).** Browsers without View Transitions support or with `prefers-reduced-motion: reduce` take the instant-switch path (no render-freeze phase, so no gate to time out). `armGraceMask(timeoutMs = 300)` returns a `GraceMaskHandle { openForLift(), cancel() }` and arms `maskState ‚Üí "masked"` after the same 300ms threshold UNLESS an early first write cancels it or a late one lifts it ‚Äî same threshold as the gate, different mechanism, same POST-filtered lift (`openForLift` mirrors the gate's `openForNotify`; epoch-guarded) and same `abandonSwitchFeedback` teardown. It supersedes any prior grace timer AND any still-pending gate (a rapid animated‚Üíinstant sequence must not let a stale gate's timeout mask the newer switch) and clears any leftover mask ‚Äî one feedback machinery at a time. On the instant path `runSwitch(graceMask)` receives `!ungatedIds.has(windowId)` (a gated tty target masks; web/chat stay mask-less, matching the gated path); the animated path passes `false` (its gate's timeout arms the mask instead).

**Known accepted follow-up (reviewer should-fix, NOT fixed in `38kg`).** A transient stale-mask hand-off exists on the two GATELESS switch paths: (1) an instant-path click to an **ungated** web/chat target on a non-VT browser, and (2) `navigateToWaitingTarget`'s same-server branch (no grace mask, no gate). If a prior switch left a mask showing, these paths don't proactively tear it down ‚Äî but it is **self-healing within one SSE confirm** (`confirmSwitchArrived` from the writeback clears it). The noted cheap fix is an idempotent `tearDownMask()` at the top of `beginPendingSwitch`; deferred, not applied.

**Tests.** `window-transition.test.ts` (colocated Vitest) covers the three settle reasons, the mask state machine (arm-at-timeout gated-only, lift-on-late-write via `notifyFirstWrite`, teardown on supersession / via `abandonSwitchFeedback` / via `confirmSwitchArrived`, gated-`false` does NOT arm), the `subscribeMaskState` seam (notify-on-change, unsubscribe stops), grace-timer parity (arm-after-threshold / cancel-on-early / lift-on-late), the post-POST lift filter, the SF8 stale-rejection identity guard, `isMaskExemptKey` (Cmd+V NOT exempt, AltGr NOT exempt), `isRedundantSwitch`, and `isSamePendingTarget` INCLUDING the cross-server `@N` collision ‚Äî plus all preserved `l4nf` gate/direction-token assertions. The e2e spec keeps the fast-path animated-completion guard and adds a deterministic **mask-not-stuck** poll (`toHaveCount(0)` within budget); a strict "never-flashes-on-fast-path" assert and the >300ms/failure paths are documented in the `.spec.md` as unit-covered (a >300ms first write can't be deterministically forced on localhost).

### E2E host-global filesystem state (`~/.rk/settings.yaml` snapshot/restore) (`260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`)

`scripts/test-e2e.sh` isolates the **tmux server** (dedicated `-L rk-test-e2e` socket) and the **port**, but NOT `$HOME` ‚Äî so any e2e that exercises a feature persisting to `~/.rk/` (settings, VAPID keys, push subscriptions) POSTs against the **developer's REAL host file**. `board-list-reorder.spec.ts` therefore snapshots the developer's `~/.rk/settings.yaml` and restores it around the suite so a curated board order (or any other setting) is never clobbered by test residue:

- **`beforeAll`** raw-byte-reads `settings.yaml` (`readFileSync(path, "utf8")`). Absent detection is **ENOENT-only**: a `code === "ENOENT"` read error means "no file to restore" (afterAll then deletes any residue); ANY other read error (EACCES/EIO ‚Äî the file EXISTS but couldn't be snapshotted) is **rethrown**, so afterAll never `rmSync`-deletes real settings on a failed snapshot.
- **`afterAll`** (always runs, even on test failure) restores VERBATIM: write the original bytes back if the file existed, else `rmSync({ force: true })` to delete residue ‚Äî a byte-identical round-trip. Teardown errors are swallowed so they never mask a test failure.

This is the general pattern for **any** host-global filesystem state an e2e touches: explicit save/restore in the spec, because the harness scopes tmux+port but not the filesystem. The companion `.spec.md` documents the save/restore in its Shared setup section (constitution Test Companion Docs).

## Component Conventions

- **All components are client-side** ‚Äî pure React SPA, no Server Components. Data fetched via typed API client (`app/frontend/src/api/client.ts`) and SSE context
- **No loading spinners** ‚Äî SSE keeps data fresh, the view renders with whatever data is available
- **Data fetching via context** ‚Äî `SessionProvider` at layout level owns the `EventSource` connection and provides session data via `useSessions()` hook
- **SSE via `useSessions` hook** ‚Äî thin wrapper over `SessionProvider` context. Single `EventSource` at layout level. SSE handler diffs incoming `e.data` JSON string against a `useRef<string>` before parsing ‚Äî if identical, skips `setSessions()` entirely (eliminates ~90% of redundant re-renders). When data has changed, `setSessions()` is wrapped in `startTransition()` to keep user input responsive. Auto-reconnects via `EventSource` built-in. Server-side SSE uses a module-level goroutine hub that deduplicates polling across browser tabs
- **ChromeProvider context** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/chrome-context.tsx`) ‚Äî split into state/dispatch contexts. Three hooks: `useChromeState()` (state only), `useChromeDispatch()` (dispatch only), `useChrome()` (convenience alias for both). Components that only read state (e.g., `AppShell`, `FixedWidthToggle`) use `useChromeState()` to avoid subscribing to dispatch identity changes. Manages current session:window selection, sidebar open/collapsed state, drawer state (mobile), `isConnected`, `fixedWidth`, and `terminalFontSize` (the effective global terminal font preference ‚Äî see ¬ß Terminal Font Size). Chrome derives content from the selection ‚Äî no slot injection
- **SessionProvider context** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) ‚Äî layout-level provider owning the single `EventSource`. Session data consumed via `useSessions()` hook. Connection status forwarded to ChromeProvider internally.
- **Shared `Dialog` component** (`app/frontend/src/components/dialog.tsx`) ‚Äî reusable modal with title, backdrop, close-on-click. Used for create, kill, and **session**-rename dialogs. *(The WINDOW rename dialog was retired by `260703-5ilm` ‚Äî window rename is now the centered `WindowHeading`'s inline edit; see ¬ß Window Heading.)*

## Create Session Dialog

The "Create session" dialog (breadcrumb `+ New Session` action, sidebar empty state button, or command palette) has three sections:

1. **Quick picks ("Recent:")** ‚Äî Deduplicated project root paths from existing tmux sessions (window 0's `pane_current_path`). Tappable list items with 44px min height for mobile. Selecting fills path + auto-derives session name.

2. **Path input with autocomplete** ‚Äî Text input that calls `GET /api/directories?prefix=...` with ~300ms debounce. Results appear as a dropdown below the input. Selecting a result fills the path and triggers a new autocomplete for children. Hidden directories (`.`-prefixed) are excluded from results.

3. **Session name** ‚Äî Auto-derived from the last segment of the selected path (e.g., `~/code/sahil87/run-kit` yields `run_kit`). Editable ‚Äî auto-derivation is a convenience, not a lock. When the name field is left empty at submit time, the name is derived from the path automatically via `deriveNameFromPath()`. The Create button is enabled when either a name or a path is provided.

On submit, the dialog calls `createSession(server, name, cwd)` which sends `POST /api/sessions?server={server}` with `{ name, cwd }`. If the name field is empty but a path is set, the name is derived from the path's last segment (sanitized for tmux/byobu: hyphens‚Üíunderscores, colons/periods replaced with underscores). Collision with existing session names is checked on the derived name and shows an error. The `cwd` field is omitted when no path is selected, preserving the original name-only behavior. Accessible from breadcrumb `+ New Session` dropdown action, sidebar empty state button, and command palette.

## Spawn-Agent Dialog (`260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent`; v2 field set `260714-q9cg-spawn-agent-dialog-mockup`; fab-gated tier field + sidebar entry point `260714-gsmu-spawn-dialog-tier-gate-sidebar-entry`)

`app/frontend/src/components/spawn-agent-dialog.tsx` ‚Äî a compact `Dialog` (create-session-dialog styling: `text-xs` field labels, disabled-submit styling) surfacing `rk riff` as a one-action web spawn. It is the frontend of the web-UI agent-spawn flow; the backend is `POST /api/riff` (see [architecture](/run-kit/architecture.md) ¬ß API Layer and the engine in [rk-riff](/run-kit/rk-riff.md)). **Title** carries the target session: `Spawn agent in {session}` (v2; was the static "Spawn agent" ‚Äî the rename is substring-compatible with the shipped e2e's `getByRole("dialog", { name: "Spawn agent" })`, which does case-insensitive substring matching).

**Fields ‚Äî v2 mockup set, in order Task ‚Üí Preset ‚Üí Where ‚Üí Worktree ‚Üí Agent**:

1. **Task** ‚Äî free text, optional, autofocused; empty spawns a blank agent session.
2. **Preset** ‚Äî a dropdown fetched on open (see preflight below), shown **only when the repo defines presets** (`presets.length > 0`); each option renders `name ‚Äî layout (N panes)`.
3. **Where** ‚Äî a `role="radiogroup"` with two options: **new worktree** (default, `where="worktree"`) and **this checkout** (`where="checkout"`, roots the window in the existing checkout ‚Äî no worktree created). State is the typed `RiffWhere = "worktree" | "checkout"` union (no `as` casts).
4. **Worktree** ‚Äî a text input, blank by default, placeholder `auto-named (e.g. swift-fox)`; **hidden when `where === "checkout"`** (it has no meaning there). Blank = wt auto-names; a typed name rides `worktreeName` through to `wt create --worktree-name`. No pre-filled suggestion ‚Äî `wt` exposes no name-suggest seam and constitution ¬ßIII forbids reimplementing its generator, so the placeholder is the honest fallback.
5. **Agent** ‚Äî a tier dropdown populated from the preflight's `tiers` (built-ins ‚à™ the repo's `agent.tiers`, `default` first), defaulting to the `DEFAULT_TIER = "default"` constant. Displays tier **names only** (no model IDs ‚Äî brittle to parse out of command strings). **FAB-GATED (since `gsmu`)**: the field renders **only when `tiers.length > 0`**. The backend fab-gates the presets response (`tiers: []` for a non-fab repo ‚Äî see [architecture](/run-kit/architecture.md) ¬ß API Layer `/api/riff/presets`), so an empty list HIDES the field entirely ‚Äî no label, no hint text, no disabled control ‚Äî because in a non-fab repo every tier resolves to the same `DefaultLauncher` (inert noise). When hidden, `tier` is omitted from the spawn body (see ¬ß Defaults). Non-fab-repo hiding does NOT enumerate system agents (claude/codex/gemini) ‚Äî tiers remain fab's abstraction (constitution ¬ßIII).

**Enter submits from any field** (`handleKeyDown` wired on all inputs incl. the radios and both selects). **Preflight fetch** (`getRiffPresets(server, session)`) is **best-effort**, but its two branches differ (since `gsmu`):

- **Success** ‚Äî sets `presets` and mirrors the response `tiers` **verbatim** (`setTiers(data.tiers)`, no longer gated on non-empty). A fab project returns a populated list (field shown); a non-fab repo returns `[]` (field hidden). This verbatim mirror is what makes the frontend gate follow the backend gate.
- **Failure** (e.g. non-repo cwd, network error) ‚Äî leaves the preset dropdown hidden and **keeps the Agent dropdown at the built-in `[DEFAULT_TIER]` fallback (field SHOWN)**. On a rejected fetch the repo's fab-ness is UNKNOWN, so the conservative status quo is to show the inert default rather than hide it ‚Äî still allowing a task-only spawn.

A `cancelled` ref guards the async setState; a `mountedRef` guards the submit path against a stale setState after the dialog closes.

**Defaults are byte-identical to the shipped path**: `spawnRiff` omits each field when unset/default ‚Äî `where` when `"worktree"`, `worktreeName` when blank (and always in checkout mode ‚Äî the client drops it since the backend rejects the pairing), `tier` when `"default"` ‚Äî so leaving the new fields untouched sends the same two-field body the shipped dialog did. **Since `gsmu` the submit also drops `tier` entirely when the Agent Tier field is hidden** (`tier: tiers.length > 0 ? tier : undefined`): a non-fab repo never sends an inert tier, matching the gate. The `tiers` array is a submit dependency of the `handleSubmit` `useCallback`.

**Submit ‚Üí in-flight ‚Üí outcome**: on submit it sets a `busy` flag (disables all fields + the button, guarding double-submit) and shows an **indeterminate** busy pipeline label ‚Äî `LogoSpinner` + "Spawning: worktree ‚Üí window ‚Üí agent‚Ä¶" ‚Äî with **no per-step progression**, because the synchronous endpoint emits no per-step events (intake assumption; streaming progress would need a new SSE/long-poll seam, out of proportion for v1). On success it closes and calls `onSpawned(windowId)` (wired to `app.tsx`'s `navigateToWindow`, inheriting the window-switch slide transition). **Falsy-windowId guard**: the backend `windowId` is best-effort (`""` when its `display-message` window-id resolve fails), so the dialog only navigates when `res.windowId` is truthy ‚Äî otherwise it closes without navigating and lets the SSE stream surface the new sidebar row (navigating with an empty id would land on a junk `/$server/@` URL). A `400`/`500` renders its message in-dialog (`text-red-400`; nothing was created on a `400`) and keeps the dialog open for correction.

**Entry points ‚Äî THREE (since `gsmu`; the first two are terminal-route only, the third is the sidebar)**. The two terminal-route entries open the dialog for the CURRENT window's session; the sidebar entry targets ANY listed session on ANY server (cross-server spawn):

1. **Cmd+K `Agent: Spawn`** ‚Äî a `PaletteAction` in `app.tsx`'s `agentSpawnActions` block (folded into `paletteActions`), gated on `sessionName` (mirrors `Window: Create`). Passes the CURRENT `{server, sessionName}` (`onSelect: () => handleOpenSpawnAgent(server, sessionName)`; `server` added to the memo deps). Constitution V palette parity; the shortcut/registration is documented at the registration site per `code-review.md` ("New keyboard shortcuts must be documented in the command palette registration").
2. **`+ New Agent`** ‚Äî the window-switcher dropdown's `secondaryAction` beside `+ New Window` (see ¬ß Breadcrumb Dropdowns). Threaded via an optional `onSpawnAgent?(session)` on the top-bar slot context (`top-bar-slot-context.tsx`) ‚Üí `TopBar` prop ‚Üí `BreadcrumbDropdown.secondaryAction`; absent (e.g. before `AppShell` registers, or off-terminal routes) ‚Üí the dropdown renders no `+ New Agent`. The one-arg slot signature is kept via a thin `handleSlotSpawnAgent = (sess) => handleOpenSpawnAgent(server, sess)` binding the CURRENT server (this entry is not cross-server).
3. **Sidebar session-row bot button (`gsmu`)** ‚Äî a per-row ü§ñ button in the session-row trailing icon cluster (see ¬ß Sidebar ‚Üí session-row icon cluster). It passes the ROW's explicit `{server, session}`, so it works from any route the sidebar is mounted on (Host / tmux Server / Terminal ‚Äî NOT the board-route sidebar, which passes no handler) and targets any server ‚Üí **cross-server spawn**. Wired `app.tsx` ‚Üí `<Sidebar onSpawnAgent={handleOpenSpawnAgent} />`.

All three entry points call `AppShell`'s `handleOpenSpawnAgent(server, session)`, which sets the explicit target state `spawnAgentTarget: {server, session} | null` (since `gsmu`, replacing the boolean `showSpawnAgentDialog`). The dialog renders iff `spawnAgentTarget != null` and is lazy-imported + `Suspense`-wrapped (like `CreateSessionDialog`), receiving `server={spawnAgentTarget.server}` and `session={spawnAgentTarget.session}` (no longer reading the current server from `useSessionContext`). `spawnAgentTarget != null` is folded into `dialogOpenRef` so the active-window effect treats it like every other open dialog.

**Cross-server nav on success** (`gsmu`): `onSpawned(windowId)` branches on whether the target IS the current route server. Same-server ‚Üí reuse `navigateToWindow` (inherits the window-switch slide transition). Cross-server ‚Üí `navigate({ to: "/$server/$window", params: { server: target, window: windowId } })` (+ close the mobile sidebar), mirroring `handleSidebarSelectWindow`. The falsy-`windowId` guard is preserved on both branches.

## Session-to-Project Mapping

Every tmux session is a project ‚Äî derived from tmux, no config file needed. Project root derived from window 0's `pane_current_path`.

## Activity Status

Windows are `"active"` (last tmux activity within 10 seconds) or `"idle"`. No "exited" state.

## Zustand Window Store

Window optimistic state is managed by a Zustand store at `app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`. This is the single source of truth for what windows are visible and what their display names are during the period between a user action and its SSE confirmation.

**Store location**: `app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`

**Store shape:**

```ts
// Flat entry type (not WindowInfo & {...} ‚Äî stores only the fields needed for display)
type WindowEntry = {
  session: string;
  windowId: string;
  index: number;
  name: string;
  pendingName?: string;    // non-undefined = optimistic rename, pending SSE confirmation
  killed: boolean;         // true = optimistically hidden, pending SSE confirmation
};

type GhostWindow = {
  optimisticId: string;    // client-generated unique key for React rendering / rollback
  session: string;
  name: string;
  createdAt: number;
  snapshotWindowIds: Set<string>; // windowIds present in session at creation time
};

type WindowStore = {
  entries: ReadonlyMap<string, WindowEntry>;  // keyed by windowId (@N)
  ghosts: GhostWindow[];
  // actions (the only ways to mutate window state):
  setWindowsForSession(session, incoming): void;
  addGhostWindow(session, name, currentWindowIds?: Iterable<string>): string;  // returns optimisticId
  removeGhost(optimisticId): void;
  killWindow(session, windowId): void;
  restoreWindow(session, windowId): void;
  renameWindow(session, windowId, newName): void;
  clearRename(session, windowId): void;
  clearSession(session): void;
};
```

**Key identifier**: `windowId` is the tmux `@N` value (e.g., `"@3"`). It is globally unique per tmux server, assigned at window creation, and never renumbered. It is used as the store key ‚Äî not the mutable numeric index.

**`MergedWindow` type**: defined in and exported from `app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`. Includes `windowId: string` as a required non-optional field.

**Action surface (minimal by design)**:

| Action | Effect |
|--------|--------|
| `setWindowsForSession(session, incoming)` | SSE reconciliation ‚Äî merges by `windowId`, preserves `killed`/`pendingName`, removes absent windows, reconciles ghosts |
| `addGhostWindow(session, name, currentWindowIds?)` | Creates a ghost entry; returns `optimisticId` for rollback |
| `removeGhost(optimisticId)` | Removes a ghost by ID (API failure rollback) |
| `killWindow(session, windowId)` | Sets `killed: true` |
| `restoreWindow(session, windowId)` | Sets `killed: false` (API failure rollback or always-settled cleanup) |
| `renameWindow(session, windowId, newName)` | Sets `pendingName` |
| `clearRename(session, windowId)` | Clears `pendingName` (settled or rollback) |
| `swapWindowOrder(session, srcIndex, dstIndex)` | Swaps index values of two entries (optimistic reorder); no-op if either missing |
| `clearSession(session)` | Removes all windows and ghosts for the session |

**SSE sync**: `AppShell` (in `app.tsx`) calls `setWindowsForSession(s.name, s.windows)` for each session in a `useEffect` on `rawSessions`. This keeps the store in sync with the SSE ground truth.

**Ghost reconciliation**: When `setWindowsForSession` is called, it computes `newIds = incomingIds ‚àí priorKnownIds`. For each ghost (oldest first) whose `snapshotWindowIds` does not contain any element of `newIds`, the ghost is removed. This set-difference approach is more reliable than count-based reconciliation ‚Äî it handles concurrent creates/deletes without false positives.

**useMergedSessions**: `useMergedSessions` in `optimistic-context.tsx` derives window data from the Zustand store rather than from raw `session.windows`. For each session: filters `killed: true` entries, applies `pendingName ?? name` for display, sorts by `index`, then appends ghosts.

**Consumers use the store via `useWindowStore()` hook**:
```ts
const { killWindow, restoreWindow, renameWindow, clearRename, swapWindowOrder } = useWindowStore();
```

**Session/server state** (ghost sessions, ghost servers, session kill/rename) remains in `OptimisticContext` ‚Äî these use name-based keys and are not subject to index-collision bugs.

## Optimistic UI & Mutation Feedback

All mutating API calls use the `useOptimisticAction` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-optimistic-action.ts`) which provides `{ execute, isPending }`. The hook calls `onOptimistic` synchronously before the async API call, tracks `isPending`, and calls `onRollback`/`onError` on failure and `onSettled` on success. An unmount guard (`mountedRef`) prevents state-after-unmount warnings.

**Callback contract** ‚Äî four optional result callbacks with distinct mount-safety guarantees:

| Callback | Called on | Mount guard | Use for |
|----------|-----------|-------------|---------|
| `onAlwaysSettled` | success | none ‚Äî always fires | Root-level context cleanup (e.g., `unmarkKilled`) |
| `onAlwaysRollback` | failure | none ‚Äî always fires | Root-level context cleanup (e.g., `unmarkKilled`) |
| `onSettled` | success | behind `mountedRef` | Local component state updates |
| `onRollback` | failure | behind `mountedRef` | Local component state updates |

`onAlwaysSettled`/`onAlwaysRollback` MUST be safe to call after the initiating component unmounts ‚Äî i.e., they may only interact with root-level stores/contexts like `OptimisticContext` or the Zustand window store (both always available for the lifetime of the app). Using local component state or `setState` in these callbacks will cause state-after-unmount warnings. Use `onSettled`/`onRollback` for anything that touches local component state.

`onError` is also behind the `mountedRef` guard (safe to call `addToast` ‚Äî `ToastProvider` is root-level, but error display is only meaningful when the user can see it).

**Three feedback patterns:**

1. **Ghost entries** (CRUD operations): Creating a session/window/server immediately inserts a ghost entry with `opacity-50 animate-pulse` styling. SSE reconciliation auto-clears ghosts when real data arrives. Failure removes the ghost and shows an error toast. Kill operations immediately hide the entry; failure restores it. Rename operations immediately update the displayed name; failure reverts. **Window** ghost/kill/rename state is managed by the Zustand window store (`app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`); **session and server** ghost/kill/rename state remains in `OptimisticProvider` context (`app/frontend/src/contexts/optimistic-context.tsx`). Both feed into `useMergedSessions(realSessions, currentServer)` which filters session-level overlays by `currentServer` (so cross-server ghosts/kills/renames don't leak ‚Äî see "Server Capture Convention" below) and merges with SSE data.

2. **Button loading states** (fire-and-forget): Split pane and close pane top-bar buttons show a spinner SVG (`animate-spin`) and `disabled` attribute during `isPending`. Command palette equivalents use the same hook for error toast feedback (palette closes, so spinner not visible).

3. **Inline progress** (async data): File upload shows an "Uploading..." badge in the terminal area. Directory autocomplete shows a spinner in the path input trailing slot. Server list refresh shows a spinner on the dropdown trigger.

**Error toast system**: `ToastProvider` + `Toast` component (`app/frontend/src/components/toast.tsx`). Fixed bottom-right, auto-dismiss after 4 seconds, stacked vertically. Error variant has `var(--color-ansi-1)` (red) left accent border; info variant uses `var(--color-ansi-4)` (blue). Theme-aware via CSS custom properties. Despite the "error" name it is the general toast surface (the `info` variant carries success/neutral messages). `addToast(message, variant?, action?)` takes an optional THIRD positional `action?: { label, onSelect }` (`260718-gxrq`) rendered as a keyboard-focusable `<button>` inside the toast body ‚Äî selecting it dismisses the toast then runs `onSelect`; the positional shape keeps every existing two-arg call site unchanged. Used for the post-pin "Pinned to <board>" + "View board" toast (¬ß Post-pin success feedback + toast optional action).

**Type guard**: `isGhostWindow(win)` exported from `optimistic-context.tsx` ‚Äî narrows `WindowInfo | MergedWindow` to `MergedWindow & { optimistic: true }`. Used in the sidebar and the `SessionTiles` density view instead of `as` casts. `MergedWindow` type is defined in and exported from `app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`; it includes `windowId: string` as a required non-optional field.

### Window Kill: Zustand Store Handles Kill Cleanup

Window kill state is tracked in the Zustand window store by `windowId` (the immutable tmux `@N` identifier), not by mutable index. This eliminates the index-collision bug where killing window N would cause tmux's renumbering to suppress the next window at that index.

**Kill flow** (`useOptimisticAction` pattern):
- `onOptimistic`: calls `windowStore.killWindow(session, windowId)` ‚Äî sets `killed: true` in the store
- `onAlwaysRollback` (API failure): calls `windowStore.restoreWindow(session, windowId)` ‚Äî clears `killed`
